1201 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


WISCONSIN DEP'T OF REVENUE v. HOGAN


No. 95-0438


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


198 Wis. 2d 792; 543 N.W.2d 825; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1541


November 10, 1995, Submitted On Briefs  
December 21, 1995, Opinion Released  
December 21, 1995, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: P. CHARLES JONES, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Wisconsin Department of Revenue challenged the decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which dismissed the Department's petition for judicial review of the Wisconsin Tax Appeal Commission's decision in favor of respondent taxpayers for the certification of a class and related order of tax refunds to said class.


OVERVIEW: The Commission certified a class of taxpayers, ordered refunds by the Department to the class of taxes collected on federal pensions, and the trial court dismissed the Department's petition for review as untimely without exploring the merits of the class certification. The court reversed the trial court's dismissal and overturned the Commission's class certification because (1) the class certification was not a final appealable order, (2) the Department filed a timely petition for review pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 227.49(4) of the Commission's final appealable order under Wis. Stat. § 227.52 requiring refunds, (3) the filing requirement of Wis. Stat. § 227.49(4) did not require service of process within the same time frame, and (4) class certification exceeded the Commission's statutory authority under Wis. Stat. § 71.75.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision in favor of the taxpayers against the Department, and remanded the matter with directions to enter an order reversing the summary judgment issued by the Commission in favor of the taxpayers.

 

1202 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Spagnola


No. 94-3102-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


199 Wis. 2d 123; 545 N.W.2d 519; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1522



December 20, 1995, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION -- REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Kenosha County: ROBERT V. BAKER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review from an order of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), which denied defendant's motion to dismiss the criminal complaint because he was prosecuted under Wis. Stat. § 948.02(2), which he contended was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of violating Wis. Stat. § 948,02(2), sex with a person under 16 years old, relating to an incident involving a 13-year-old girl. On appeal, defendant argued that § 948.02(2) was unconstitutional because it violated his privacy right to engage in consensual sexual relations. He also argued that the statute as applied had a chilling effect on the exercise of his right to select sexual partners. The court rejected all of defendant's arguments. According to the court, while adults have a right to privacy with regard to sexual relations and decisions involving procreation, that right is not absolute and may be circumscribed or regulated where important state interests are at stake. Defendant had no privacy right to engage in sexual intercourse with a person whom the legislature has determined is unable to give consent. The court also found that the State's interest in protecting children and prohibiting sexual activity between them and adults was of greater import than the burden upon an adult to determine whether a prospective sexual partner was unable to consent to sexual activity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's order denying defendant's motion to dismiss a criminal complaint charging him with second-degree sexual assault.

 

1203 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Nitka


No. 94-2975-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


198 Wis. 2d 388; 542 N.W.2d 238; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1645



November 22, 1995, Released


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Manitowoc County: DARRYL W. DEETS, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Manitowoc County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of physical abuse of a child.


OVERVIEW: When defendant's five-year-old son did not obey his instruction to stop throwing chestnuts at cars, defendant struck his son on the buttocks three to five times with an army cloth webbed belt. The blows missed and struck the son on his right thigh where extensive bruising appeared. At the close of the evidence at trial, the jury convicted defendant of physical abuse of a child. In affirming, the court rejected defendant's contention that his conduct was reasonable discipline. The court noted that the State presented the testimony of an examining physician, who established that defendant struck his son at least four times and that it took significant force to cause the son's injuries. According to the court, the evidence was sufficient to support the conclusion that defendant had used excessive force. Further, the court held that the introduction of testimony regarding conversations that defendant had with the investigating officer and a social worker was proper because it was offered to impeach defendant's claim that he intended to administer a light spanking.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction.

 

1204 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Johnson


No. 95-0672-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


198 Wis. 2d 389; 542 N.W.2d 239; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1633



November 22, 1995, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL from judgments of the circuit court for Monroe County: MICHAEL J. ROSBOROUGH, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed in part and reversed in part. Cause remanded with directions to the trial court to enter an order dismissing count 3 of the information charging Johnson with third-degree sexual assault with a person without consent of that person in violation of sec. 940.225(3), STATS. Judgments of conviction and sentence affirmed in all other respects. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed judgments from the Circuit Court for Monroe County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of second-degree sexual assault, a violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.225(2)(a), for an act of oral sex, and second and third degree sexual assault, violations of Wis. Stat. §§ 940.225(2)(d) and 940.225(3), for sexual intercourse with an unconscious person and without the consent of that person.


OVERVIEW: The victim was drunk, stoned, and intermittently asleep when defendant first performed oral sex on her then had vaginal intercourse. He was convicted of three offenses, one relating to the oral sex, and two relating to the single act of intercourse. In reversing the third degree sexual assault conviction, the court first observed that this conviction passed the Blockburger-Wis. Stat. § 939.66(1) test, in that the third degree offense was not a lesser-included offense of the second degree offense. The court held however that the legislature did not authorize punishment for both offenses stemming from the same act, noting that the thrust of both offenses was to protect the victim from nonconsensual intercourse, and that there was no legislative indication to punish a defendant twice for this same act. The court held that the appropriate remedy was to reverse the conviction for the lesser offense. The court also held that there was sufficient evidence to convict defendant of the oral sex offense, Wis. Stat. § 940.225(2)(a), noting that the pummeling the victim received before she passed out was force contemplated by the offense.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's third degree sexual assault conviction and affirmed his two second-degree sexual assault convictions.

 

1205 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hazen


No. 95-1379-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


198 Wis. 2d 554; 543 N.W.2d 503; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1414


October 17, 1995, Submitted On Briefs  
November 14, 1995, Opinion Released  
November 14, 1995, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Lincoln County: J. MICHAEL NOLAN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Lincoln County (Wisconsin), convicting him of assault and battery of a prison guard pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 48.183, which automatically placed a juvenile in criminal court for committing an assault or battery in a juvenile detention facility, and Wis. Stat. § 970.032, which provided for a "reverse waiver" hearing to determine jurisdiction over a juvenile.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was charged with attacking an employee of the secured juvenile correctional facility where he was confined, contended that Wis. Stat. §§ 48.183 and 970.032 violated his due process and equal protection rights by revealing his identity to the public and press. On review, the court held that Wis. Stat. §§ 48.183 and 970.032 did not deprive defendant of his right to life, liberty, or property as protected by U.S. Const. amends. V and XIV and Wis. Const. art. I, § 8. The court concluded that no governmental decision based on substantive predicates needed to be made before the trial court assumed jurisdiction under Wis. Stat. § 48.183, which automatically granted the trial court jurisdiction in certain circumstances. The only decision the trial court was to make was whether to retain jurisdiction under Wis. Stat. § 970.032. Even if the trial court decided not to retain jurisdiction, defendant's name would still have been released to the public by virtue of the trial court's original jurisdiction. Because the court did not make a decision to assume jurisdiction based on substantive predicates, the statutes did not create a constitutionally protected right.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1206 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Baye


No. 95-0833-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1355



October 31, 1995, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Vilas County: JAMES B. MOHR, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Vilas County (Wisconsin), which convicted him for possessing less than 500 grams of marijuana with intent to manufacture, as a party to the crime, and more than 42.5 grams of marijuana without having paid the controlled substance occupational tax.


OVERVIEW: The police arrested defendant while he was loading marijuana growing equipment on his truck and just after he had taken physical possession of some marijuana from his accomplice. The State charged the two with producing marijuana at the accomplice's residence. Defendant was convicted and he appealed. The court held that at a minimum the evidence showed the existence of a common enterprise in which defendant and his accomplice shared the enterprise's proceeds and over which defendant exerted substantial control. In the alternative, the evidence permitted a finding that defendant had exclusive control over the operation and that the accomplice was an employee. If the jury reached either conclusion, then it could find that defendant legally possessed at least a share of the marijuana that the enterprise produced even if defendant's physical possession just before his arrest was insufficient by itself to prove legal possession. Defendant had not shown reasonable grounds for conviction on the simple possession lesser charge. Additionally, defendant had not shown that the State lacked either the power or a rational basis to tax 42.5 grams as occupational possession.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and order convicting defendant.

 

1207 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Oney v. Schrauth


No. 94-3298


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


197 Wis. 2d 891; 541 N.W.2d 229; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1329


September 11, 1995, Submitted On Briefs  
October 26, 1995, Opinion Released  
October 26, 1995, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected January 8, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Dane County: MARK A. FRANKEL, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizen sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which dismissed his tort action against appellee probation officer and granted the probation officer's motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The probation officer conducted a search of a probationer's home in which the citizen was present. The officer found a list of computer software that the citizen claimed belonged to him. Because of the software, a search warrant was obtained for the citizen's house where pornographic material was found. No charges were filed. He alleged that the officer provided misleading statements in order to obtain the search warrant. The trial court granted the officer's motion for summary judgment holding that the citizen failed to serve notice upon the attorney general within 120 days from the search as required by Wis. Stat. § 893.82(3). The court noted that the officer's acts stemmed from his duties as a probation officer because he was searching the probationer's home when the additional evidence was found; therefore the statute applied. The court noted that the officer did not search the citizen's home and that the citizen provided the additional software programs that the officer requested after the search of the probationer's home.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that granted summary judgment in favor of the probation officer.

 

1208 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Wilke v. City of Appleton


No. 95-0120


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


197 Wis. 2d 717; 541 N.W.2d 198; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1294


August 28, 1995, Submitted On Briefs  
October 17, 1995, Opinion Released  
October 17, 1995, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Outagamie County: JAMES BAYORGEON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff personal property owner sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Outagamie County (Wisconsin), which dismissed his complaint with prejudice. The owner sought a declaratory judgment that City of Appleton, Wis., Municipal Code § 12-32(c), governing non-summary abatement, was unconstitutional and that defendant city violated the owner's due process rights.


OVERVIEW: The owner had a business in which he stored large household appliances outdoors. The city inspected the business and found several ordinance violations, including the storage of the appliances. The city directed the owner to take corrective action, but the owner failed to do so. After giving notice to the owner, the city, pursuant to § 12-32, entered the premises and removed the appliances to a warehouse. The city notified the owner that unless he reclaimed his property it would be disposed of. When the owner failed to contact the city, the property was sold to offset the costs of abatement and storage. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment dismissing the owner's complaint. The court concluded that § 12-32 denied the owner neither substantive nor procedural due process. Section 12-32(c) was designed to provide the city with a procedure for eliminating public nuisances through the seizure and removal of nuisances. The procedure had a reasonable and rational relationship to the purpose or object of the enactment. The ordinance also provided the owner with the opportunity to contest the abatement procedure in a meaningful time and in a meaningful manner.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment dismissing the owner's complaint with prejudice.

 

1209 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. George H. v. Fennema


No. 95-2684-W


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1261



October 12, 1995, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.



DISPOSITION: Writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed an application seeking a writ of habeas corpus to require respondent director to release him from a health center.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner alleged that he was taken into custody and held under an emergency detention pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 51.15, for a probable cause hearing. At the hearing, he objected on the grounds that the trial court lacked personal jurisdiction because the hearing was not held within the statutory time frame as required under Wis. Stat. § 51.20(7)(a). The trial court denied his motion to dismiss, and found probable cause. Petitioner sought a writ of habeas corpus. He claimed that Wis. Stat. §§ 51.15(5) and 51.20(7)(a) were unconstitutional, and denied him his right to due process and equal protection. The court denied the petitioner's request for habeas corpus relief. The court held that petitioner failed to carry his burden that the statutes were unconstitutional. First, the court reasoned the 72-hour provision under § 51.20(7)(a) was not ambiguous. Second, the court reasoned petitioner was considered a late detainee as he was detained later in the week, therefore the weekend and holidays were excluded within the time frame that he was entitled to a probable cause hearing. Last, the court reasoned petitioner was not denied his right to equal protection or due process.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petitioner's request for habeas corpus relief.

 

1210 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Angela M.W. v. Kruzicki


No. 95-2480-W


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


197 Wis. 2d 532; 541 N.W.2d 482; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1246


September 20, 1995, Oral Argument  
October 6, 1995, Opinion Released  
October 6, 1995, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] HABEAS CORPUS original proceeding. SUPERVISORY WRIT to the circuit court for Waukesha County: KATHRYN W. FOSTER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The obstetrician for petitioner expectant mother found she was using drugs during pregnancy. When she refused help, he reported her to respondent county. The county, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 48.19(1)(c), took the mother's viable fetus into protective custody, necessitating the internment of the mother. She petitioned for habeas or supervisory relief to the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin) and appealed the denial of her petitions.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the mother's viable fetus was a "person" under the statutory definition of "child" in Wis. Stat. § 48.02(2). Therefore, the county had the jurisdiction to exercise its authority over the fetus as an endangered child. The court further held that all components of the juvenile court's exclusive original jurisdiction had been satisfied in this case, so that it had subject matter jurisdiction over the custody order and personal jurisdiction over the fetus as the endangered child. Although the mother contended that the juvenile court lacked personal jurisdiction over her, the court noted that the statute did not require original jurisdiction over the parent. The juvenile court was authorized to adjudicate the matter of protective custody and to issue a protective order for the custody of the viable fetus pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 48.19(1)(c). Finally, the court held that the pending custody statute, Wis. Stat. § 48.13, and protective custody provisions of Wis. Stat. § 48.19(1), represented a proper and tailored means by which the state might exercise its compelling interest in promoting the health, safety, and welfare of the mother's viable fetus.


OUTCOME: The court denied the mother's petitions for a writ of habeas corpus or, in the alternative, for a supervisory writ, in the matter involving the county's order obtaining protective custody over the mother's viable fetus.

 

1211 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Carol J.R. v. County of Milwaukee (In re Carol J.R.)


No. 94-0688


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


196 Wis. 2d 882; 540 N.W.2d 233; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1158


November 1, 1994, Submitted On Briefs  
September 19, 1995, Opinion Released  
September 19, 1995, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: DAVID L. DANCEY, Reserve Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which denied her motion for post-commitment relief from a probate court commissioner's order granting respondent county's motion for involuntary medication.


OVERVIEW: The patient was committed to county custody for involuntary treatment. After a hearing, a probate court commissioner filed an order authorizing the involuntary administration of psychotropic drugs, using appropriate medical standards. The patient moved the trial court to vacate the order, contending that a probate court commissioner lacked authority to conduct hearings under Wis. Stat. § 51.61(1)(g). The court affirmed the denial of the post-commitment motion. The court held that the Wisconsin Supreme Court's recognition of a court commissioner's authority to hear and determine the medication issue under a previous version of Wis. Stat. § 51.61 survived unscathed from a repeal and recreation of Wis. Stat. § 51.61(1)(g)(3).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying post-commitment relief.

 

1212 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hall


No. 94-2848-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


196 Wis. 2d 850; 540 N.W.2d 219; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1130


July 10, 1995, Submitted On Briefs  
September 14, 1995, Opinion Released  
September 14, 1995, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: RICHARD J. CALLAWAY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of two counts of delivering cocaine base within 1,000 feet of school premises, second or subsequent offense, and two counts of failing to comply with Wisconsin's drug tax stamp law, contrary to Wis. Stat. §§ 139.87--139.95.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two counts of delivering cocaine base within 1,000 feet of school premises, second or subsequent offense, and two counts of failing to comply with Wisconsin's drug tax stamp law, contrary to §§ 139.87--139.95. He contended that the "affix and display" and the "payment" provisions of the drug tax stamp law violated his right against compelled self-incrimination guaranteed by the Wisconsin and United States Constitutions. The court affirmed the convictions. The court held that the drug tax stamp statute both contemplated and permitted the anonymous payment of the tax and, therefore, did not subject those who complied with its provisions of compelled self-incrimination. The court relied upon Wis. Stat. § 139.91, which provided that dealers may not have been required to provide any identifying information in connection with the purchase of stamps. The court also held that the affix and display provision of the drug tax stamp statute, as construed, did not violate a defendant's right against compelled self-incrimination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted defendant of two counts of delivering cocaine base within 1,000 feet of school premises, second or subsequent offense, and two counts of failing to comply with Wisconsin's drug tax stamp law.

 

1213 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. VERDONE


No. 95-0752-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


197 Wis. 2d 118; 541 N.W.2d 838; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1110



September 6, 1995, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Taylor County: DOUGLAS T. FOX, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Taylor County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant of obstructing an officer in violation of Wis. Stat. § 946.41(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction, arguing that the evidence was insufficient because his refusal to give the arresting officer his driver's license and his date of birth did not "obstruct" the officer. The court held that a person obstructed an officer in the course of his official duties if he prevented or made more difficult the performance of the officer's duties. The officer made a valid arrest for a speeding violation recorded by radar and for operation of a vehicle without displaying state registration plates. In order for the officer to properly identify defendant, who was driving the vehicle, it was necessary to know more than his name. The officer made a prima facie showing of a statutory violation when he testified that defendant would neither produce a valid driver's license nor provide his date of birth. The officer testified that he needed the date of birth to verify defendant's driving status on the teletype. Thus, the jury was entitled to infer from the evidence that defendant's conduct "obstructed" the officer in the course of pursuing a valid stop for traffic violations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1214 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ambrose


No. 94-3391-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


196 Wis. 2d 768; 540 N.W.2d 208; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1066


July 17, 1995, Oral Argument  
September 6, 1995, Opinion Released  
September 6, 1995, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Brown County: RICHARD G. GREENWOOD, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Brown County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of seven counts of sexual exploitation by a therapist contrary to Wis. Stat. § 940.22.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a high school teacher who had consensual sexual intercourse with a student. Although he was pursuing a master's degree in psychology, he was not a therapist. The student sought him out to talk to because she was depressed and having trouble getting along with her parents. They met about once a week during lunch hour to discuss her problems. Defendant gave her advice and on a couple of occasions, he gave her homework, such as writing down the arguments she had with her family. He would go over the assignment, and they would discuss how she could have done things differently. Upon review, the court found that § 940.22 required proof of a professional therapist-patient/client relationship to sustain a conviction. The court concluded that defendant was not a professional therapist and was counseling the student within a teacher-student relationship. His meetings with the student were ad hoc, loosely structured, and stopped altogether during school vacations or when other duties intervened. He did not take a patient history, make a diagnosis, take notes of the meetings, develop a treatment plan, or charge a fee. Defendant did not hold himself out as a therapist.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for seven counts of sexual exploitation by a therapist.

 

1215 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Professional Guardianships, Inc. v. Ruth E.J. (In re Ruth E. J.)


No. 95-2010


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


196 Wis. 2d 794; 540 N.W.2d 213; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1070


August 17, 1995, Submitted On Briefs  
September 6, 1995, Opinion Released  
September 6, 1995, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Brown County: RICHARD G. GREENWOOD, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded for further proceedings. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant guardian sought review of the order of the Circuit Court, Brown County (Wisconsin), which dismissed her motion to permit her ward to receive electroconvulsive treatment. This order explained the basis for the reversal of the trial court's prior order.


OVERVIEW: The ward was incompetent and the guardian was appointed for her. The ward was incapable of giving her consent to any treatment. The ward's doctors stated that the only chance of recovery for the ward was electroconvulsive treatment. The trial court dismissed the guardian's application for treatment on the ground that Wis. Stat. § 51.61(1)(k) did not grant authority to order such treatment without the patient's consent. The guardian appealed. The court found that the statute denied the ward her right to equal protection and her right to life. Because the ward could not make a choice of medical care, the trial court was required to hold a hearing to determine if the treatment was proper.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court.

 

1216 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Management Computer Servs. v. Hawkins, Ash, Baptie & Co.


No. 93-0140


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


196 Wis. 2d 578; 539 N.W.2d 111; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1245


April 21, 1994, Oral Argument  
August 31, 1995, Opinion Released  
August 31, 1995, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL and CROSS-APPEAL from a judgment and orders of the circuit court for La Crosse County: ROBERT W. RADCLIFFE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed Circuit Court for La Crosse County's (Wisconsin) dismissal of its punitive damages claims and all other adverse rulings and orders, and respondents cross-appealed, arguing petitioner's conversion claim should have been dismissed and frivolous costs and sanctions against petitioner should have been granted.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner's complaint alleged respondent breached its agreement with petitioner contrary to Wisconsin criminal and civil statutes. Respondent counterclaimed. After trial, both parties appealed various aspects of trial, verdict, and awards. Court ruled breach of contract verdict against respondent was correctly set aside, since contract was too indefinite to be enforced as petitioner claimed. Court found petitioner established its damages for conversion with sufficient definiteness and that thus award had been incorrectly reduced. Court agreed credible evidence did not establish respondent enjoyed, and therefore must disgorge, unjust enrichment. Court concluded reasonable punitive damages amounted to approximately 10 times amount of compensatory damages award. Lower court was correct in dismissing Wisconsin Organized Crime Control Act, Wis. Stat. §§ 946.80-946.88, claims, since petitioner had been unable to establish Racketeer Influenced Corrupt Organization Act, 18 U.S.C.S. § 1961 et seq., violations in another suit.


OUTCOME: Court affirmed vacating the breach of contract verdict, affirmed reducing the unjust enrichment award, affirmed granting summary judgment that dismissed WOCCA claim, vacated part of order that reduced the award for conversion, and modified judgment by decreasing amount of punitive damages award.

 

1217 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Martin B. (In re Martin B.)


Nos. 94-1975, 95-0765


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1020



August 23, 1995, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION HAS NOT BEEN RELEASED FOR PUBLICATION IN THE PERMANENT LAW REPORTS. UNTIL RELEASED, IT IS SUBJECT TO REVISION OR WITHDRAWAL.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged a decision of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin) that terminated his parental rights immediately after he was adjudicated the biological father of a child.


OVERVIEW: The State filed a petition to terminate an unmarried mother and father's parental rights. The mother did not contest. As to the father, the State claimed that he failed to assume parental responsibility pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 48.415(6). The matter went to hearing on a paternity issue and the termination petition. The trial court adjudicated the father as the child's father and then terminated his rights. In affirming the judgment, the court found that the consolidation of the paternity issue and the termination petition did not offend the provisions of § 48.415 or Wis. Stat. § 48.423 nor abridge the father's rights. There was evidence that the father maintained a relationship with the child during his first few months of life, but he had little contact after that. The father claimed that once the substantial parental relationship existed, it did not matter that the relationship later disappeared. This claim was waived because this construction of Wis. Stat. § 48.415(6)(a)(2) was not asserted in the trial court. Trial counsel was not ineffective for failing to raise the father's construction of the statute because the construction had never been raised or adopted by the courts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1218 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Osgood


No. 94-2103


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1021



August 23, 1995, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION HAS NOT BEEN RELEASED FOR PUBLICATION IN THE PERMANENT LAW REPORTS. UNTIL RELEASED, IT IS SUBJECT TO REVISION OR WITHDRAWAL.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Racine County: DENNIS J. FLYNN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant inmate sought review of an order of the Racine County Circuit Court (Wisconsin), which denied his motion for postconviction relief from a judgment convicting him of first-degree sexual assault in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.225(1)(d).


OVERVIEW: The inmate was initially charged with having sexual intercourse with his four-year-old daughter in violation of § 940.225(1)(d). At trial, the daughter testified that the inmate touched her vaginal area with his fingers; the testimony of two pediatricians was consistent with that claim. The trial court permitted the State to amend the information during the trial to charge the inmate with assault based on sexual contact rather than intercourse. On appeal, the court affirmed the inmate's conviction. Sexual contact was not a lesser-included offense of sexual intercourse and the inclusion of both forms of assault in the same statute, § 940.225(1)(d), did not violate due process or equal protection; the legislature reasonably could conclude that sexual activity by an adult with a child, regardless of whether the conduct involved sexual contact or sexual intercourse, was a social evil that should be forbidden. The inmate failed to object to the amendment of the information and thus waived his right to challenge it on appeal; moreover, the amendment did not prejudice the inmate where it did not change the factual basis for the charge or have any impact on his theory of defense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

State v. Lohmeier


No. 94-2187-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


196 Wis. 2d 432; 538 N.W.2d 821; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 999


July 12, 1995, Oral Argument  
August 16, 1995, Opinion Released  
August 16, 1995, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Walworth County: JAMES L. CARLSON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded with directions. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Walworth County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant of two counts of homicide by intoxicated use of a vehicle contrary to Wis. Stat. § 940.04(1)(a), two counts of homicide by prohibited alcohol concentration contrary to § 940.09(1)(b) and two counts of hit and run causing death contrary to §§ 346.67 and 346.74(5). Defendant argued, inter alia, that § 940.09(2) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant struck the victims with his car as they walked along the road where he was driving. Defendant's blood alcohol level was over the legal limit. A witness testified that one of the victims was in the road and the other was on the edge of the road. An accident reconstructionist testified that the victims had been on the road, not on the shoulder. Defendant attempted to present a defense that the accident would have occurred even if he had been exercising due care in the operation of the vehicle. The trial court gave a jury instruction that it was no defense that the victims may have been contributorily negligence. Defendant was found guilty and appealed. The court rejected defendant's argument that § 940.09(2) violated the Equal Protection Clause. The court held that defendants who committed crimes under § 940.01 and § 940.09 were not similarly situated. The court held that the jury instruction was erroneous because if deprived defendant of his intervening cause defense. The court held that there was a probability that the jury was misled by the erroneous instruction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's ruling that the statute was constitutional but reversed defendant's convictions and remanded for a new trial.

Waushara County v. Mack


Nos. 94-2157, 94-2226


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 982



August 10, 1995, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION HAS NOT BEEN RELEASED FOR PUBLICATION IN THE PERMANENT LAW REPORTS. UNTIL RELEASED, IT IS SUBJECT TO REVISION OR WITHDRAWAL.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and orders of the circuit court for Waushara County: LEWIS MURACH, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant-third-party plaintiff challenged orders of the Circuit Court for Waushara County (Wisconsin) in a civil forfeiture action by plaintiff Waushara County, Wisconsin and dismissed defendant's counterclaim and cross-claims without prejudice. The County's action alleged that defendant had violated a trespassing ordinance by installing a pier in violation of the riparian rights of third-party defendant neighbor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court lacked personal jurisdiction over him because he had not been served with process. The court held that defendant waived his claim when he appeared by requesting legal counsel, demanding a jury trial, requesting document production, and moving for a protective order. Defendant also claimed that the trial court had jurisdiction over his counterclaim and cross-claims under Wis. Stat. § 801.01(2). The court held that the trial court properly dismissed the claims because they were not authorized under Wis. Stat. § 66.119(3)(b). Further, the cross-claim allegations against the sitting judge were a transparent attempt to obtain a substitution after the time had expired under Wis. Stat. § 801.58(1). The court held that defendant was properly enjoined from filing lis pendens against the neighbor's property because his counterclaim and cross-claims were properly dismissed. Further, the ex parte proceedings held by the trial court did not violate Wis. Sup. Ct. R. 60.20(2)(a). Finally, the court imposed sanctions against defendant due to his disrespectful and scandalous accusations against the trial court after the court's warning.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and imposed sanctions upon defendant for his scandalous and disrespectful briefs.

 

1221 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Miller


No. 94-0159


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


196 Wis. 2d 238; 538 N.W.2d 573; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 945


June 13, 1995, Submitted On Briefs  
August 3, 1995, Opinion Released  
August 3, 1995, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected December 7, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Clark County: MICHAEL W. BRENNAN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, members of the Old Order Amish faith, sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court for Clark County (Wisconsin), which found in the State's favor and directed appellants to pay a forfeiture for their failure to display a "slow-moving vehicle" emblem on their horse-drawn buggies as required by Wis. Stat. § 347.245.


OVERVIEW: The State charged appellants with violating Wis. Stat. § 347.245 when they refused to display red-orange, triangular "slow-moving vehicle" emblems on their horse-drawn buggies. Appellants claimed that emblems violated their religious beliefs, but the trial court found for the State and ordered appellants to pay a forfeiture. Appellants sought review and the court reversed. The court held that the Religious Freedom Restoration Act (RFRA), 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 2000bb to 2000bb-4, governed the case. The RFRA restored the compelling state interest test for controversies over laws that substantially burdened the First Amendment right to free exercise of religion. As applied to appellants, the court held that the slow-moving vehicle (SMV) statute failed RFRA's compelling state interest test. Although the court found that the State had a compelling interest in traffic safety, it said that the State failed to show that the SMV statute represented the least restrictive means of furthering that interest. The court noted that appellants were willing to place white reflective tape and lanterns on their buggies and that the State had not proven that those measures were any less safe than the emblem.


OUTCOME: The court reversed an order that directed appellants to pay a forfeiture for not displaying a "slow-moving vehicle" emblem on their horse-drawn buggies, as required by State law.

 

1222 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. Dane County


No. 92-0946


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


195 Wis. 2d 892; 537 N.W.2d 74; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 882


July 9, 1993, Submitted On Briefs  
July 20, 1995, Released  
July 20, 1995, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL and CROSS-APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Dane County: RICHARD J. CALLAWAY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; cross-appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, mother and son, appealed a decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which dismissed their action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, alleging that defendants, county and social worker, violated their procedural and substantive due process rights when the social worker changed a delinquent stepson's placement, in violation of Wis. Stat. Ann. § 48.357(1).


OVERVIEW: The mother's stepson was adjudged delinquent and placed out of the home and under the supervision of the county. The social worker later placed the stepson back in the home, where he shot the mother and her son. The trial court dismissed their actions under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 for violation of their procedural and substantive due process rights by placement of the stepson back in the home without first providing them with notice and an opportunity to file an objection with the court, as required by Wis. Stat. Ann. § 48.357(1). A jury found in the social worker's favor on their negligence claim, due to lack of causation. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that postdeprivation state law remedies under state tort law were adequate, and their availability defeated the procedural due process claim. For substantive due process purposes, no special relationship existed between the stepson and the state, thereby relieving the state of any duty to protect him. The state had no duty to protect the mother and the stepson from the stepson's violent behavior. The trial court correctly instructed the jury on the issue of causation, and the jury verdict was supported by credible evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing the mother and son's action for deprivation of constitutional rights in violation of the federal civil rights statute was affirmed. Adequate postdeprivation state law remedies existed to afford them procedural due process, and the state had no duty under substantive due process to protect them from violence when the stepson was not in custody.

Wisconsin Retired Teachers Ass'n v. Employee Trust Funds Bd.


No. 94-0712


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


195 Wis. 2d 1001; 537 N.W.2d 400; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 893; 19 Employee Benefits Cas. (BNA) 2894


March 16, 1995, Oral Argument  
July 20, 1995, Released  
July 20, 1995, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL and CROSS-APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: ANGELA B. BARTELL, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff teacher's association and defendant Employee Trust Funds Board (board) challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which held that the Special Investment Performance Dividend Legislation (SIPD), 1987 Wis. Act 27, §§ 436m, 684r, 688km, amending the Wisconsin Retirement System (WRS), Wis. Stat. § 40, violated constitutional prohibitions against the taking of property without just compensation.


OVERVIEW: The WRS provided retirement benefits for public employees. Under the SIPD, earnings on the WRS trust fund assets of certain annuitants were used to pay supplemental benefits that were not a commitment of the WRS trust fund. The purpose of the SIPD was to reduce the general purpose revenue funding of supplemental benefits The court affirmed the judgment in part and held that the SIPD unconstitutionally took the property of the teachers who were WRS annuitants for a public purpose without just compensation. The court further held that that the teacher's association did not have to comply with the notice of claim statute, Wis. Stat. § 893.82(3), because it did not apply to a claim of unconstitutional taking. However, the court reversed the amount awarded the teacher's association and held that because the unconstitutional taking was continuing, the teacher's association was entitled to declaratory relief and an injunction against the SIPD, in addition to just compensation. Additionally, the court held that the teacher's association was entitled to attorneys' fees under the common fund doctrine because it was appropriate to pay attorney fees out of the sum recovered.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment finding that the legislation violated constitutional prohibitions against the taking of property without just compensation, reversed the judgment in part, and remanded with directions.

State v. Koch


No. 94-1230


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


195 Wis. 2d 801; 537 N.W.2d 39; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 854


February 23, 1995, Oral Argument  
July 12, 1995, Released  
July 12, 1995, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Manitowoc County: FRED H. HAZLEWOOD, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, van line and goods transporter, sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Manitowoc County (Wisconsin), which granted summary judgment in favor of respondent State of Wisconsin, in the State's enforcement action against the goods transporter for its failure to provide worker's compensation insurance for its employees in violation of Wis. Stat. § 102.28(2)(a).


OVERVIEW: The goods transporter had an agency agreement with the van line whereby it hauled goods for the van line's customers. The van line obtained worker's compensation coverage for the goods transporter's drivers. The State informed the goods transporter that it was illegally uninsured and that the certificates of insurance naming the van line as the named insured and the goods transporter as certificate holders were insufficient to show compliance with the Worker's Compensation Act (Act). The State commenced an enforcement action against the goods transporter. The goods transporter filed a third-party claim against the van line. The trial court granted summary judgment for the State. The goods transporter and the van line appealed. The court held that the goods transporter's contractual arrangement with the van line to provide it with worker's compensation insurance was void because it was inconsistent with § 102.28(2)(a) and the intent of the Act generally, in that it failed to provide coverage for all of its potential employees and all potential work-related activities of its employees. Therefore, the goods transporter was uninsured and subject to the forfeitures under § 102.82(2)(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, which granted summary judgment in favor of the State.

Shoreline Park Preservation v. Wisconsin Dep't of Admin.


No. 94-2512


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


195 Wis. 2d 750; 537 N.W.2d 388; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 846


June 13, 1995, Submitted On Briefs  
July 6, 1995, Released  
July 6, 1995, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: MORIA KRUEGER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant preservationists challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) dismissing their petition to review a decision by the Department of Administration (Wisconsin). The Department concluded that a proposed parking center to be built adjacent to both a state office building and a proposed convention center complied with the Wisconsin Environmental Policy Act (WEPA), Wis. Stat. § 1.11.


OVERVIEW: The Department ruled that the final environmental impact statement (EIS) complied with WEPA. The court concluded that the state legislation appropriating state funds for construction of the parking ramp was not enacted through a private or local bill within the meaning of Wis. Const. art. IV, § 18 as the state had a proprietary interest in providing parking for employees working in its buildings, wherever they were located. Having failed to overcome the presumption of regularity attaching to the presiding officer's actions at the EIS hearings, the court rejected the preservationists' claim that the hearing officer was biased. The site-specific language of the legislation authorizing the parking ramp's funding rendered consideration or implementation of any alternative remote and speculative and not at all reasonably related to the purposes of the environmental review of the project under Wis. Stat. § 1.11(2)(e) of WEPA. The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the preservationists' new evidence motion as the trial court exercised its discretion under Wis. Stat. § 227.56(1) in a manner that its decision had a rational basis and was consistent with applicable law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which dismissed the preservations' petition to review the Department's decision approving construction of a parking center under the WEPA.

Howard M. v. Jean R. (In re Jenae K. S.)


No. 94-0955


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


196 Wis. 2d 16; 539 N.W.2d 104; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 825


June 13, 1995, Submitted On Briefs  
July 6, 1995, Opinion Released  
July 6, 1995, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dodge County: JOSEPH E. SCHULTZ, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Dodge County (Wisconsin) terminated appellant guardian's custody of a child and transferred it to respondent, the child's mother. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The guardian challenged the standard of review used by the trial court for deciding custody. The court found that when a guardianship was terminated, a parent was entitled to custody of a child unless the trial court finds that the parent is unfit or compelling reasons exist for awarding custody to a third party. The second issue was whether sufficient evidence supported the trial court's finding that there were no compelling circumstances making it appropriate to award custody to a third party, the guardian. The court concluded that the evidence was sufficient to support the trial court's finding that no compelling reasons existed for awarding custody of the child to the guardian. The court found that the facts of record from which the trial court concluded that there were no compelling circumstances to deny the mother custody of child differed from the facts the guardian stressed in his brief. After hearing the evidence, the court might have concluded that the mother was the parent the guardian asserted her to be, but it did not, and the court could not second guess the trial court decision under its standard of review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Schultz v. City of Cumberland


No. 94-3390


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 844



July 5, 1995, Released

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Barron County: EDWARD R. BRUNNER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bar owner sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Barron County (Wisconsin), upholding an order of respondent city council revoking his liquor license.


OVERVIEW: The city council revoked the bar owner's liquor license under Wis. Stat. § 125.12(2)(ag)2, finding that he maintained a disorderly or riotous indecent or improper house, based on public displays of sexual acts and prostitution on the premises. The bar owner sought review of the judgment upholding the revocation of his liquor license, arguing that § 125.12(2)(ag)2 was unconstitutionally overbroad and that the facts of the case did not justify revocation. On appeal, the court found that the bar owner lacked standing to challenge the statute on the basis of its overbreadth because the acts in questions, public sex and prostitution, were not protected by the First Amendment. Next, the court rejected the argument that the conduct that occurred on the premises was insufficient to justify revocation. Police officers testified to witnessing nude entertainers performing fellatio on patrons in exchange for money and numerous acts of cunnilingus and several masturbatory acts occurring between entertainers and patrons. As the licensee, the owner was responsible for the activities occurring on his licensed premises. The court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed on appeal.

State v. Hicks


No. 94-2542-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 796



June 27, 1995, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: STANLEY A. MILLER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with instructions. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Wisconsin appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which dismissed one count of a criminal complaint charging defendant with violating the controlled substances tax statute, Wis. Stat. §§ 139.87-139.96 (1993-94).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with one count of attempting to deliver cocaine, as party to a crime. The State subsequently filed an amended information and added one count of possessing cocaine without evidence that the controlled substances tax had been paid in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 139.87-139.96 (1993-94). Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the count charged in the amended information on the ground that the statute was unconstitutional as implemented because it violated his right to be free from compelled self-incrimination. The trial court granted defendant's motion and the State appealed. The court reversed, holding that defendant did not have standing to challenge the constitutionality of the tax because the procedures he alleged were implemented under the statute had not caused him any injury because he had never attempted to comply with them. The court also held that the statute had already been upheld on its face as constitutionally permissible and thus, where defendant had not engaged in the procedures which he alleged made a facially constitutional statute unconstitutional, the trial court erred by granting defendant's motion to dismiss.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's grant of defendant's motion to dismiss and it ordered the reinstatement of charge against defendant for one count of possessing cocaine without evidence that the controlled substances tax had been paid.

Fond Du Lac County v. Mentzel


No. 94-1924


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


195 Wis. 2d 313; 536 N.W.2d 160; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 753


May 4, 1995, Oral Argument  
June 14, 1995, Opinion Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Fond du Lac County: STEVEN W. WEINKE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant nightclub owner appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Fond du Lac County (Wisconsin), which found the nightclub owner guilty of violating Fond Du Lac County, Wis., Cabaret Ordinance § 1.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found the nightclub owner guilty of violating Fond Du Lac County, Wis., Cabaret Ordinance § 1, which required certain liquor license holders to obtain a cabaret permit before providing any form of dance entertainment. The nightclub owner appealed, contending that the county's regulatory scheme was vague and overbroad and that it violated equal protection principles because the same type of entertainment was permitted in a city within the county. On appeal, the court held that Cabaret Ordinance § 1 was facially unconstitutional under the overbreadth doctrine because it encompassed nude expression which was not associated with harmful secondary effects. A plain reading of the ordinance revealed that many forms of unclothed entertainment that did not effectuate secondary concerns would have been subject to the ordinance. A modern dance of which nude dance was a part would have been prohibited by the ordinance if offered in a venue that had liquor on the premises. Yet the county could not have pointed to any harmful secondary effects emanating from such a performance, such as prostitution or criminal activity.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which found the nightclub owner guilty of violating a county ordinance.

1233 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Gloria A. v. State (In the Interest of Estel A.)


No. 95-0315-NM


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


195 Wis. 2d 268; 536 N.W.2d 396; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 739


May 18, 1995, Submitted on Briefs  
June 13, 1995, Released  
June 13, 1995, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: MEL FLANAGAN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of an order from the Circuit Court, Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, that terminated her parental rights to her children pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 48.43. The mother filed a notice of no merit appeal pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 809.32. The issues on appeal were whether § 809.32 applied to an appeal of a termination order and whether the notice of appeal deadline in Wis. Stat. § 809.107(5) could be extended.


OVERVIEW: The court concluded that the no merit procedure in Wis. Stat. § 809.32, which established a 180-day time limit for filing a notice of appeal, did not apply to appeals from orders terminating parental rights. Appeals from termination orders were governed by Wis. Stat. § 809.107 exclusively. The court was not authorized under Wis. Stat. § 809.82(2)(a) to enlarge the 15-day time limit for filing the notice of appeal under Wis. Stat. § 809.107(5). The mother argued that the 15-day time limit violated the separation of powers doctrine and denied her due process and equal protection rights. The mother did not show that the 15-day time limit imposed by the legislature unconstitutionally intruded upon or burdened the judiciary in an area of shared power. The shortened appeal time did not violate due process. There were minimal content requirements for a notice of appeal, and an extension of time to file a brief could be requested. The equal protection challenge failed because there was a rational basis for having a short time limit. Children and parents had a significant interest in proceedings that affected the familial relationship. There was no basis for appellate review.


OUTCOME: The mother's no merit appeal of an order that terminated her parental rights to her children was dismissed.

 

1234 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Love, Voss & Murray v. Wisconsin Dep't of Revenue


No. 94-2185


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


195 Wis. 2d 189; 536 N.W.2d 126; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 717


April 18, 1995, Submitted On Briefs  
June 7, 1995, Opinion Released  
June 7, 1995, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Waukesha County: PATRICK L. SNYDER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant partnership challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), finding that appellee commission's assessment of a surcharge tax against the partnership under Wis. Stat. § 77.93 was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The partnership, a law firm, asserted that the surcharge tax against it was unconstitutional because it violated the equal protection clause. The court disagreed and affirmed the tax assessment. In affirming, the court held that constitutional challenges to a statute must overcome a strong presumption of constitutionality. A party attacking a statute on constitutional grounds had the burden of proving that the statute was unconstitutional beyond a reasonable doubt. In the area of taxation, the legislature had wide discretion in making classifications. These types of classifications need only be reasonably related to the purposes of the legislation. The court noted that the exemption provided to farmers did not violate the constitution because farmers, unlike other businesses, could not necessarily absorb the recycling surcharge tax through increasing the prices of their product because of the vagaries of the commodity marketplace. Additionally, the court noted that the classification served a legitimate state interest by giving a partial exemption to a valuable part of Wisconsin's economy, which had seen a decrease in numbers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1235 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Burrus v. Goodrich


No. 94-1329


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


194 Wis. 2d 654; 535 N.W.2d 85; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 599


March 30, 1995, Oral Argument  
May 11, 1995, Released  
May 11, 1995, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: SARAH O'BRIEN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Department of Corrections appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which declared rules that established minimum periods of time that life-term inmates were required to serve in maximum-security institutions invalid ex post facto laws, in an action by plaintiff inmates for a declaratory judgment that the rules violated the Ex Post Facto Clauses of the state and federal Constitutions.


OVERVIEW: The inmates argued that rules adopted by the Department, which established minimum periods of time that life-term inmates were required to serve in maximum-security institutions, violated the Ex Post Facto Clauses of the state and federal Constitutions, and the trial court agreed. The court concluded that no ex post facto violation existed and reversed. The court found that considered as a whole the rules established presumptive security classifications for life-term inmates according to risks presented in four categories, and they permitted recognition of individual or exceptional cases through a discretionary early-reassignment process. They were drafted to achieve legitimate governmental and correctional ends, and nothing in the record suggested an aim to punish for past activity or to accomplish a more burdensome punishment. The Department's concern was not the imposition of additional penal sanctions on life-term inmates but was directed toward assessment and amelioration of the risks presented by inmates in all categories in a prison setting. Under such circumstances, the rules were not punishment even though they might have bore harshly upon the ones affected.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment declaring the Department's rules invalid.

 

1236 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re Amanda A.


Nos. 94-3384, 94-3385


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


194 Wis. 2d 627; 534 N.W.2d 907; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 601


March 30, 1995, Submitted on Briefs  
May 10, 1995, Opinion Released  
May 10, 1995 Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEALS from an order of the circuit court for Winnebago County: WILLIAM H. CARVER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent father appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Winnebago County (Wisconsin) terminating his parental rights. He claimed that Wis. Stat. § 48.415(8) was applied to him in violation of the prohibition on ex post facto laws. He further argued that the order violated his due process, equal protection, and double jeopardy rights and that the trial court abused its discretion in issuing the order without a psychological examination.


OVERVIEW: The father was convicted of murdering his children's mother. After his conviction, § 48.415(8) was enacted making murder of the other parent grounds for termination of parental rights. The court held that application of § 48.415(8) to the father did not violate the prohibition on ex post facto laws because the legislative intent was not to punish murders but to provide support for children. For the same reason, application of the statute did not violate the double jeopardy clause. There was no violation of the father's due process or equal protection rights because of the state's compelling interest in providing for the support of the children. The father was not entitled to notice that his parental rights could be terminated because he could not remedy the problem. Rehabilitation of the family unit was impossible. The trial court had discretion whether to require a psychological evaluation of the father. It ordered one but decided not to require it when the psychologist testified that he had determined that the father was unfit based upon his examination of the children. The trial court did not abuse its discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which terminated the father's parental rights.

Evers v. Shandor


No. 94-1763


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


193 Wis. 2d 640; 537 N.W.2d 434; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 536



April 25, 1995, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Outagamie County: WILLIAM M. ATKINSON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employer sought review of the summary judgment of the Circuit Court for Outagamie County (Wisconsin) in favor of defendant employee, thereby dismissing the employer's action against employee that alleged civil claims under the Wisconsin Organized Crime Control Act (WOCCA), Wis. Stat. §§ 946.80 to 946.88, and civil rights claims under 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1983, 1985.


OVERVIEW: The employer brought an action against the employee that alleged that the employee had violated WOCCA by participating in a pattern of racketeering and by conspiring to present perjured testimony at a criminal prosecution of the employer. The employer also alleged that the employee conspired with others acting under the "color of state law" to deprive the employer of his constitutional rights contrary to 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1983, 1985. The trial court granted the employee's motion for summary judgment, and the employer sought review. The court affirmed the summary judgment on alternative grounds. The court affirmed the trial court's finding that the doctrine of in pari delicto prevented recovery. The court held that the complaint failed to state a claim for damages under 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1983 or 1985.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary dismissal of the employer's action against the employee that alleged federal civil rights violations as well as civil claims under WOCCA.

State v. Wolfe


No. 94-2663-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


193 Wis. 2d 641; 537 N.W.2d 435; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 527



April 19, 1995, Released


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Sheboygan County: GARY LANGHOFF, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Sheboygan County (Wisconsin), which suspended defendant's driver's license for six months, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 161.50, after defendant pleaded guilty to possession of marijuana in violation of Wis. Stat. § 161.41(3r). On appeal, defendant asserted that the suspension of his license violated his due process rights because a vehicle was not used in the commission of the offense.


OVERVIEW: Police executed a search warrant at defendant's residence and discovered less than one ounce of marijuana in various units. He was charged with three counts of possession of marijuana in violation of Wis. Stat. § 161.41(3r), but no allegations were made regarding the use of a motor vehicle in the commission of the offense. After defendant pleaded no contest and was convicted on each count, his license was suspended pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 161.50. While defendant conceded that having a driver's license was not a fundamental right, he argued that the suspension was not rationally related to the furtherance of a proper public purpose because the revocation sanction for drug offenders had no reasonable relationship to public health, safety, and welfare where the use or operation of a motor vehicle was not directly related to the commission of the offense. On appeal, the court held that § 161.50 had a rational relationship to the state's strong interest in punishing drug offenders, deterring future possession and use of controlled substances, and protecting citizens on state roads from those who might have been driving while impaired.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Terry H. v. Marathon County


No. 94-2097


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


192 Wis. 2d 765; 532 N.W.2d 470; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 330



March 14, 1995, Released


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Marathon County: MICHAEL W. HOOVER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mentally ill individual sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Marathon County (Wisconsin) recommitting him to involuntary treatment under Wis. Stat. ch. 51. The mentally ill individual contended that the civil mental health recommitment standard contained in Wis. Stat. §§ 51.20(1)(am), 51.20(13)(g)3 was facially unconstitutional because it did not require a person to be found dangerous.


OVERVIEW: The trial court committed the mentally ill individual to the custody of a health care center. Respondent county petitioned for an extension of that commitment order. A jury recommitment trial was held where the jury found that he was mentally ill, that he would have been a proper subject for commitment if treatment were withdrawn, and that he was a proper subject for treatment. The court held that the recommitment standard required a finding of dangerousness and that the mentally ill individual's constitutional challenge failed. The mentally ill individual also contended that the trial court's jury instructions and special verdict constituted an unconstitutional application of the recommitment statute because the jury was not required to make a finding of dangerousness. The court found that the challenge to the instructions and the verdict were not properly preserved for appeal. Even if the court were to consider those challenges, the instructions properly instructed the jury that they were required to make a finding of dangerousness under the recommitment standard. Applying that standard, the jury in effect found that the mentally ill individual was dangerous to himself or others.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order from the trial court recommitting the mentally ill individual to involuntary treatment.

State v. Runkel


No. 94-2606-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


192 Wis. 2d 766; 532 N.W.2d 470; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 346



March 14, 1995, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)(5), STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: GEORGE W. GREENE, JR., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with instructions. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant for disorderly conduct, party to a crime, contrary to Wis. Stat. §§ 947.01 and 939.05.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction arose from her actions outside a clinic that performed abortions. Defendant and several other individuals locked themselves to a pipe which was welded to a van parked in front of the clinic's entrance. On appeal from her conviction, defendant claimed that: (1) the trial court erroneously exercised its discretion when it admitted irrelevant evidence; (2) the trial court erroneously exercised its discretion in instructing the jury; (3) remarks during the prosecutor's opening statement violated her constitutional right against self-incrimination; (4) the complaint was sufficient to withstand a motion to dismiss; and (5) the trial court erred in refusing to strike the testimony of a fire chief despite the State's failure to provide defendant with a copy of the fire chief's written incident report prior to trial. The first four arguments were held to be without merit. The court held that the State was obligated under Wis. Stat. § 971.24(1) to give defendant a copy of the fire chief's report because it contained written statements of a witness testifying on behalf of the State. Therefore, the court reversed the judgment, but did not order the verdict set aside.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, but did not order the verdict set aside. Instead, the court remanded the matter to the trial court for further fact-finding and resolution.

State v. Gomaz


No. 94-2628


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


192 Wis. 2d 766; 532 N.W.2d 470; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 315



March 9, 1995, Released


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Grant County: JOHN R. WAGNER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Grant County (Wisconsin), which entered a default judgment against him and assessed a penalty for speeding in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.57(4)(h).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the 55-mile per hour speed limit of Wis. Stat. § 346.57(4)(h) was unconstitutional because it was federally imposed and, therefore, violated the Tenth Amendment of the United States Constitution. The court disagreed. Defendant also argued that the trial court erred in entering a default judgment that violated his right to due process. The trial court entered a default judgment after finding that defendant was given notice and that he did not appear or post a cash bond. Defendant's failure to appear was treated as a no contest plea, and the trial court found him guilty. Pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 345.30, jurisdiction over actions for violations of traffic regulations was conferred upon circuit courts. Therefore, the trial court had subject matter jurisdiction over the violation. The court held that the trial court properly followed the procedures of Wis. Stat. § 345.37(1)(b) in considering the nonappearance to be a plea of no contest and in entering the default judgment. It was not error for the trial court to issue the default judgment when defendant did not appear in court at the specified time.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.
