State v. Baumann


No. 92-3198


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


191 Wis. 2d 824; 532 N.W.2d 144; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 261



February 28, 1995, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JEFFREY A. WAGNER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees, city and state, filed an injunctive action against appellant protestors to enjoin the nuisances created by the protestors. The circuit court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) issued the injunction through a motion for summary judgment. The protestors appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that abortion protestors blockading activities of medical clinics interfered with others' enjoyment of life, health, and safety, denied access to the clinics, resulted in harassment, intimidation, physical assault, and vandalism and disrupted public order. The court affirmed the injunction because the blockading activities were a legal nuisance. The protestors' affidavits were inadequate where they were conclusory and without evidentiary facts. The injunction was proper due to a sufficient probability that the protestors' future conduct would have violated rights and caused irreparable injuries and the balance of equities was in favor of the city and state. There was no violation of the First, Ninth, or Tenth Amendments because they did not protect activities that were a nuisance. Also, the injunction was narrowly tailored to burden no more speech than necessary to serve a significant government interest. The injunction was not vague or overbroad. The state did not have to seek leave of the court under Wis. Stat. § 823.02 to file the action and the state and city could have joined together in the petition. The complaint stated a proper cause of action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the injunction against the protestors.

February 28, 1995, Opinion Filed

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of non-final orders of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which directed the state crime laboratories to conduct additional analysis requested by two defendants on alleged cocaine base. Defendants were charged with possession of cocaine base with intent to deliver and delivery of cocaine base. Defendants cross-appealed non-final orders denying their motions to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with possession of cocaine base with intent to deliver and delivery of cocaine base. The lower court ordered that the state crime lab conduct additional analysis, requested by each defendant, on alleged cocaine base. The state appealed. Defendants cross-appealed the lower court's orders denying their motions to dismiss on the ground that the statute proscribing possession and delivery of cocaine, Wis. On appeal, the court concluded that the lower court did not abuse its discretion in ordering the crime lab to perform certain tests because the lab was capable of performing the tests, the costs were relatively low, defendants could not pay for testing at another lab, and the test results could help the jury in its deliberations. Defendants could not assert that the broad definition within the statute constituted an abuse of police power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders of the lower court.

Stat. §§ 346.04(3) and 346.17(3)(c) and (d).

The court also held that the legislature was presumed to act with full knowledge of existing laws.

Rhonda R.D. v. Franklin R.D. (In the Interest of Christopher D.)

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of two orders of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which terminated his parental rights to his minor son and denied his claim of ineffective assistance of counsel. Respondent mother had initiated the action to terminate the father's parental rights on the basis of abandonment.


OVERVIEW: Prior to their separation, the parties lived in Washington. The mother took the son with her to Wisconsin and was later awarded sole custody of him. The father had little contact with his son during the next six years and was in arrears in child support payments. The father's trial counsel did not provide ineffective assistance.

State v. Martin


Nos. 94-1643-CR, 94-2130


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


191 Wis. 2d 646; 530 N.W.2d 420; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 200


December 19, 1994, Submitted on Briefs  
February 15, 1995, Opinion Released  
February 15, 1995, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Waukesha County: JOSEPH E. WIMMER, Judge. APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Waukesha County: J. MAC DAVIS, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile charged with battery of a prisoner in violation of Wis. Stat. 940.20(1), appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which overturned the holding of a court commissioner that Wis. Stat. §§ 48.183, 970.032, and 939.635, under which the adult criminal court obtained jurisdiction of the juvenile were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile also appealed from a subsequent holding of the juvenile court, that it did not have jurisdiction over the proceeding because of Wis. Stat. § 48.183. The appeals were consolidated. The statutes waived juveniles who committed battery while in a juvenile correctional facility to the jurisdiction of adult criminal courts, and set a minimum sentence of three years for the offense. The court held that the juvenile did not have a substantive due process right to individualized treatment either in the waiver procedure, or in sentencing because it was neither explicitly nor inherently found in the U.S. Constitution; therefore, rational basis review was appropriate. The court noted that the legislature had a rational basis for seeking to control increasing violence in juvenile correctional facilities, and was empowered to simulate a healthy school-like environment for juveniles. The court concluded that there was ample justification for setting a presumptive minimum sentence for juveniles who committed acts of battery within a secured institution, but not for adults who committed similar acts. The court held that the state classifications were neither arbitrary nor irrational.


OUTCOME: The orders of the Circuit Court, and of the juvenile court were affirmed.

Miller by & Through Sommer v. Kretz


No. 94-2231


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


191 Wis. 2d 573; 531 N.W.2d 93; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 131


January 11, 1995, Submitted on Briefs  
February 7, 1995, Opinion Released  
February 7, 1995, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Vilas County: ROBERT E. KINNEY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Vilas County (Wisconsin), which granted partial summary judgment for defendants, a doctor, an insurance company, and Wisconsin Patient's Compensation Fund, in the patient's malpractice lawsuit.


OVERVIEW: The doctor diagnosed the patient with a heart murmur when he was four years old. The doctor told the patient's mother that the murmur was only functional and would disappear in time. When the patient was over 10 years old, he underwent a physical examination for insurance purposes, where physicians discovered that he had severe systolic hypertension in his upper extremities. The court affirmed the trial court's decision granting partial summary judgment for defendants. The court determined that the patient's action was barred under Wis. Stat. §§ 893.55 and 893.56 because the action was commenced more than five years from the date of the doctor's act or omission and after the patient reached 10 years of age. The court determined that § 893.55(1)(b) was not unconstitutional because it did not irrationally or arbitrarily create a classification of immune tortfeasors. Statutes of limitations were policy considerations within the province of the legislature. The five-year discovery limitation for medical malpractice claims was a distinct time period and consistent with the act's purpose. The statute applied to all health care providers in the state equally.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

1249 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Town of Eagle v. Christensen


No. 94-0503


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


191 Wis. 2d 301; 529 N.W.2d 245; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 81


November 8, 1994, Submitted On Briefs  
January 26, 1995, Released  
January 26, 1995, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Waukesha County: PATRICK L. SNYDER, Judge. APPEAL from judgments of the circuit court for Jefferson County: ARNOLD SCHUMANN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded with directions. Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant town filed a declaratory judgment action against respondents, the assessor of a neighboring town, state officials, and the Wisconsin Department of Revenue, and sought a determination that the property valuation and equalization processes used by the assessor of the neighboring town violated the uniformity clause of the Wisconsin Constitution. The Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin) dismissed the action and the town appealed.


OVERVIEW: The town initiated a declaratory judgement action in an effort to challenge the property valuation and equalization processes utilized by the assessor of the neighboring town. The trial court dismissed the action. On review, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment with regard to the assessor of the neighboring town, but reversed the trial court's judgment with regard to the department and the state officials. In reaching its decision, the court held that the town failed to state a claim against the assessor for the neighboring town. Conversely, the court found that the town asserted a cause of action against the department and the state officials. The court held that the town had standing to pursue the action. Furthermore, the court held that it was not necessary for the town to exhaust administrative remedies. Lastly, the court concluded that the action was not barred by the doctrine of sovereign immunity. The court remanded the case and instructed the trial court as to venue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court with regard to the assessor of the neighboring town, but reversed the judgment of the trial court with regard to the department and the state officials. The court remanded the case and instructed the trial court as to the proper venue.

STATE v. HOLSTEN

Stat. § 948.02(2) was unconstitutional because it allowed identical punishment for sexual assault involving only contact and for sexual assault involving penetration. The court affirmed because it found appellate review was precluded and that defendant had abandoned his right to present any possible defense to the charge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court that convicted defendant after a no-contest plea for second-degree sexual assault of a child and denied his motion for postconviction relief that sought sentence modification.

 

1251 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Matteson


No. 94-0770-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


191 Wis. 2d 360; 530 N.W.2d 69; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 57



January 19, 1995, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)(5), STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Crawford County: MICHAEL KIRCHMAN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Crawford County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of manufacturing a controlled substance (marijuana) in violation of Wis. Stat. § 161.41(1)(h). He contended that the affidavit supporting issuance of a search warrant of his home was inadequate to support a finding of probable cause, and that his prosecution violated the establishment of religion clause of the First Amendment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a priest, grew marijuana in his basement for sacramental use. Police, acting on anonymous tip, obtained a warrant and found the plants. On appeal, the court held that the search warrant was valid and that defendant's arguments regarding his First Amendment rights had been rejected in an earlier case. The affidavit was valid because of the detail provided by the informer and evidence of high electrical usage patterns in defendant's home tended to reduce the chances that the tip was false. Although statements in the affidavit that defendant's electrical usage was substantially higher than that of other homes in the area were false, because the statement was not made intentionally or recklessly, the affidavit withstood the Franks test for a challenge to a warrant affidavit on the basis of false information. The court rejected defendant's establishment of religion argument because there was little difference between that argument and a previously rejected proposition that the Native American Church's exemption from prosecution under Wis. Stat. 161.115 for religious use of peyote and mescaline violated the establishment and equal protection clauses of the First Amendment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for manufacturing a controlled substance.

 

1252 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Grewal v. Wisconsin Veterinary Examining bd.


No. 94-1195-FT


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


191 Wis. 2d 360; 530 N.W.2d 70; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 30



January 17, 1995, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)(5), STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: MICHAEL J. SKWIERAWSKI, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, the State of Wisconsin Veterinary Examining Board, appealed an order from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which reversed the Board's decision denying petitioner applicant a license to practice veterinary medicine in the state and held that the Board's administrative rules for licensure by endorsement were unconstitutional and violated the applicant's constitutional right to equal protection under the law.


OVERVIEW: The applicant was licensed to practice veterinary medicine in India. In an attempt to become licensed in Wisconsin, she took the national examination in the state and failed. She then applied for a license by the endorsement procedures set forth in Wis. Stat. § 453.072(1). Her application was denied by the Board under Wis. Admin. Code § VE 4.01(1) because she had failed the licensing examinations and had not subsequently passed them. The circuit court reversed. On appeal by the Board, the court reversed the circuit court's order. The court held that the Board did not exceed its authority in establishing the requirements for licensure by endorsement. The rules were designed to effectuate the purpose of the statute by ensuring that applicants were properly qualified. The court also held that § 4.01(1) did not create an unconstitutional classification in denial of the applicant's equal protection rights. The rules did not permit licensure if the applicant failed the national examination in Wisconsin or elsewhere. The mistaken licensure by forfeiture of two foreign veterinarians who had failed the examination in another state did not render the rules themselves invalid.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the Board's order.

State v. Stambaugh


No. 94-1611-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


190 Wis. 2d 471; 528 N.W.2d 92; 1994 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1648



December 28, 1994, Released


NOTICE: UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: GEORGE W. GREENE, JR., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) that convicted him of disorderly conduct as a party to a crime, which crime was a violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 947.01, 939.05. The State had not provided the defense with the report of a fire chief that was made regarding the subject incident, and the trial court denied the defense a mistrial that was sought on the basis of the denial of the report.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had been found inside a van that was blocking an abortion clinic entrance, and inside the van his arm was apparently locked inside a pipe that was affixed to the van. At trial, upon cross-examination of the fire chief that had been dispatched to dislodge defendant, the defense found out about his report. Defendant relied on Wis. Stat. § 971.24 for the right to the report, and the court rejected the arguments of the State that § 971.24 only applied to statements of witnesses called to testify on behalf of the State made to authorities and to statements prepared by an investigating authority. The court held that § 971.24 put no such restrictions on the type of statement that had to be provided to the opposing party. Because the report was not part of the record on appeal, the court was unable to determine whether or not the error in failing to disclose the report was harmless. The report had to be produced on remand. The court rejected defendant's other arguments, including one that the evidence was insufficient to convict him.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for further fact finding and resolution consistent with the court's opinion.

 

1254 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Village of McFarland v. Blatterman


No. 94-0418


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


190 Wis. 2d 469; 528 N.W.2d 91; 1994 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1541



December 8, 1994, Released


NOTICE: UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: GEORGE NORTHRUP, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which affirmed defendant's convictions in a municipal court for operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated, operating a motor vehicle with a prohibited breath alcohol concentration, failure to notify police of an accident, and open intoxicants in a motor vehicle.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his municipal court convictions to the trial court. The trial court concluded that the only issue on appeal was proof of operation, and it did not make findings as to the ultimate facts necessary to affirm the municipal court's judgment. The court held that: (1) on appeal from a municipal court decision, Wis. Stat. § 800.14(5) required the trial court to consider all of the issues decided by the municipal court; (2) § 800.14(5) contemplated that a defendant who elected to appeal on the record made before a municipal court was entitled to be heard on the issues decided against him by that court; (3) a circuit court reviewing a municipal court decision under § 800.14(5) was required to find the ultimate facts and state separately its conclusions of law; (4) it was unnecessary for defendant to request the trial court to make findings on all of the issues presented by his appeal because Wis. Stat. § 805.17(2) anticipated that the trial court would review the record and state its findings on all of the issues raised; and (5) § 805.14(5) would be unconstitutional if it did not allow defendant to be heard on the issues raised in his appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Kircher


No. 93-2881-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


189 Wis. 2d 392; 525 N.W.2d 788; 1994 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1463

November 23, 1994, Released  
November 23, 1994, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dodge County: DANIEL GEORGE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Dodge County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of homicide by intoxicated use of a vehicle.


OVERVIEW: Defendant struck a pedestrian with his vehicle. He placed a 911 telephone call to notify the police. The tape recording of the call was not preserved. An officer interviewed defendant after he waived his Miranda rights, but defendant refused to respond to questions regarding whether he had been drinking. He did not dispute that he was under the influence of an intoxicant. Instead, he attempted to establish the affirmative defense under Wis. Stat. § 940.09(2) that the accident would have occurred even if he had been exercising due care and had not been under the influence of an intoxicant. The court upheld the convictions. The district attorney requested the tapes but was informed that the tape had been cleared and used to record other calls. The tape recording no longer existed, and other witnesses testified that defendant did not slur his speech or give any indication of intoxication after the accident.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for homicide by intoxicated use of a vehicle.

Hacker v. State Dep't of Health & Social Servs.


No. 93-1043


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


189 Wis. 2d 328; 525 N.W.2d 364; 1994 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1433


November 8, 1994, Submitted On Briefs  
November 17, 1994, Released  
November 17, 1994, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dodge County: JOSEPH E. SCHULTZ, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner facility owner appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Dodge County (Wisconsin), which affirmed a decision of Respondent Wisconsin Department of Health and Social Services (DHSS) authorizing revocation under Wis. Stat. § 50.01(1g) of the operating licenses for the owner's two community-based residential facilities (CBRFs).


OVERVIEW: The DHSS hearing officer found that the owner, also a registered nurse, violated Wis. Stat. § 50.09(1)(L) by providing nursing care to CBRF residents and violated Wis. Stat. § 50.09(1)(e) by yelling at a resident. On appeal, the court first determined that its scope of review for revocation of the owner's CBRF licenses was do novo because the scope of Wis. Stat. § 50.01(1g) was a matter of first impression. The court then held that the DHSS applied the proper legal standard when it concluded that the owner failed to obtain prior physician approval for nursing assistance provided to CBRF residents. Wis. Stat. § 50.01(1g) defined a CBRF as a place where no nursing care was provided to residents. The court held that the record supported the findings that the owner provided nursing care to residents on three occasions: a resident was administered a laxative in an amount exceeding a doctor's order; the owner removed a resident's bowel obstruction without a doctor's order; and the owner used shortening from the kitchen to perform a nursing procedure on a patient, potentially contaminating the patient with food particles, all violations of Wis. Stat. § 50.09(1)(L).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Association of State Prosecutors ex rel. Feiss v. Milwaukee County


No. 93-3329


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


189 Wis. 2d 291; 525 N.W.2d 768; 1994 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1406


October 24, 1994, Submitted On Briefs  
November 15, 1994, Released  
November 15, 1994, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: LAURENCE C. GRAM, JR., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent county challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which entered a peremptory writ of mandamus that directed the county to transfer pension funds on behalf of petitioner district attorney and class members from the county retirement system to the state retirement system.


OVERVIEW: All district attorneys became state officers or employees. Those attorneys in the county were given the option to remain in the county retirement system or to transfer to the state retirement system. The non-vested attorneys elected to have the county contributions made on their behalf transferred to the state plan. The county argued that it was unable to make the transfer. The trial court ordered that the county had a duty to transfer the contributions pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 978.12(5)(c)5. The county argued that the contributions were impossible to calculate, that it did not have a duty to transfer contributions, and that § 978.12(5)(c)5 was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the order because after examining the content, subject matter, scope, and objective of § 978.12(5)(c)5, the county clearly had a duty to transfer the contributions after the attorneys' job category switched from county to state employee. Furthermore, amounts of contributions were readily available from actuarial reports and records maintained by the county. The court also found that the statute was constitutional because the transfer of contributions was not a taking without due process of law.


OUTCOME: The peremptory writ of mandamus directing the county to transfer pension funds on behalf of the district attorneys from the county plan to the state plan was affirmed.

 

1259 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Brandmiller v. Arreola


No. 93-2842


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


189 Wis. 2d 215; 525 N.W.2d 353; 1994 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1369


August 2, 1994, Submitted On Briefs  
November 8, 1994, Released  
November 8, 1994, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: ROBERT J. MIECH, Reserve Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs in a class action suit appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which granted summary judgment for defendant municipalities, concluding that the municipalities' ordinances prohibiting "cruising" were constitutional. Plaintiffs were ticketed for violation of the ordinances and they filed the suit seeking declaratory and injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs alleged that the cruising ordinances were unconstitutional; that the municipalities' cruising ordinances were violative of the police powers doctrine; and that state law preempted the municipalities' regulation of "cruising." The court found that the ordinances did not violate the constitutional right to travel, or the right of privacy. The court held that the right to travel did not guarantee the right to drive a car repeatedly on the same street. Moreover, driving a car was a privilege, not a right, and driving a car exposed the driver to less of an expectation of privacy. The court would not engage in an overbreadth analysis because First Amendment rights were not implicated. Prohibiting cruising did not infringe on plaintiffs' right of freedom of association, and the prohibition did not infringe upon the right to freely move about one's community. The ordinances were reasonably related to the public purpose of preventing a threat to public health, safety and welfare. Therefore, passing the cruising ordinances was a valid exercise of police power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment for the municipalities.

Lundeen v. Wisconsin Dep't of Agric., Trade & Consumer Protection

COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN

September 13, 1994, Submitted On Briefs

November 8, 1994, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Burnett County: JAMES H. TAYLOR, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant dairy farmer sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Burnett County (Wisconsin), which dismissed his petition for review and affirmed a decision of the Wisconsin Department of Agriculture, Trade and Consumer Protection, which concluded that the Department properly issued notice of intent to suspend his dairy license and properly charged him with reinspection fees after a warrantless inspection uncovered several violations.


OVERVIEW: After the Wisconsin Department of Agriculture, Trade and Consumer Protection conducted a warrantless inspection of the farmer's premises, it issued a notice of its intent to suspend the farmer's license. However, the license was not suspended. The farmer asserted that the warrantless inspection violated his Fourth Amendment rights because the search was made without prior notification and without his presence and the inspectors had unbridled discretion to search his property and belongings. The Department determined that the warrantless searches were proper but refused to consider the constitutional issue. The trial court entered a judgment affirming the Department's decision and dismissing the farmer's petition for review. On appeal, the court concluded that the statutory scheme provided adequate constitutional protection for warrantless searches and affirmed the judgment of the trial court dismissing the petition. The court held that warrantless and unannounced inspections were necessary to further the State's interest in regulating dairy farms and to preserve the public health and safety. In addition, the court noted that there was no evidence of abuse by the Department.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1261 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Harris


No. 93-0730-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


189 Wis. 2d 162; 525 N.W.2d 334; 1994 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1374


December 15, 1993, Submitted on Briefs  
November 8, 1994, Opinion Released  
November 8, 1994, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of first-degree murder and armed robbery, both as a party to a crime. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in admitting nontestimonial derivative evidence after suppressing his confession for violation of his right to counsel under U.S. Const. amend V.


OVERVIEW: Because the trial court concluded that defendant's Miranda rights were violated but that his confession was voluntary, it denied defendant's motion to suppress the physical evidence, including the murder weapon. On review, the court affirmed, finding that the trial court's ruling that defendant's confession was voluntary was supported by the evidence presented at the suppression hearing. The trial court properly admitted the physical evidence because derivative, non-testimonial evidence was admissible when its discovery resulted from a suppressed, but voluntary confession. The arguable benefits from excluding such evidence were far outweighed by the advantages of having relevant and probative evidence, not obtained by actual coercion, available at trial to aid in the pursuit of truth. Although defendant contended that he should have been granted a new trial because a juror, who became the foreperson, was exposed to a newspaper article that referred to defendant's suppressed confession, the court noted that, following an individual voir dire of the juror, defense counsel did not object to the juror and thus waived this issue on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Lake Bluff Hous. Partners v. City of S. Milwaukee

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city and its building inspector sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which entered judgment in favor of respondent property developer and granted a writ of mandamus directing the city to issue a building permit.


OVERVIEW: After securing a site-specific low-income housing tax credit for the project, the developer met with city officials to review plans, at which time the city confirmed the site's zoning classification for multi-family residential use. The developer then conducted erosion studies and modified its plans to comply with the city's concerns. 1264 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. La Forge


No. 94-0516


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


188 Wis. 2d 605; 526 N.W.2d 280; 1994 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1219



October 4, 1994, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Ashland County: NORMAN L. YACKEL, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Ashland County (Wisconsin) in a civil forfeiture action, which provided for a six-month jail sentence in the event defendant did not pay his fine and court costs. Defendant also appealed from an order denying his motion for sentence reconsideration.


OVERVIEW: After a judgment was entered against defendant in a civil forfeiture action, the court ordered that defendant would be subject to a six-month jail sentence under Wis. Stat. § 778.09 if he failed to pay the judgment and court costs. On appeal, defendant asserted that the statute unconstitutionally deprived him of equal protection in light of Wis. Stat. § 800.095, which provided that a defendant could only be sentenced to a maximum jail term of 90 days for failure to pay a forfeiture under a local ordinance and that the amount owed by a defendant was reduced by at least $ 25 for each day served. The court concluded that defendant had failed to demonstrate that § 778.09 was unconstitutional beyond a reasonable doubt or that the six-month jail sentence in the event of nonpayment violated his equal protection rights. The court therefore affirmed the trial court's judgment and order. The court held that there was a rational basis for the more severe punishment under § 778.09 for violations of state law, as opposed to violations of a local ordinance, in light of the fact that the State controlled the nature of the conduct it determined to be illegal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and order.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant owner appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court, Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), ordering the closure and sale of his apartment building, which was declared a public nuisance under the state Drug House Abatement Law, Wis. Stat. § 823.113.


OVERVIEW: The owner possessed an apartment building. Wis. v. King


No. 94-0638-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


187 Wis. 2d 548; 523 N.W.2d 159; 1994 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1147


August 30, 1994, Submitted On Briefs  
September 20, 1994, Released  
September 20, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Marathon County: RAYMOND F. THUMS, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Circuit Court for Marathon County (Wisconsin) for homicide by negligent operation of a vehicle, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.10, and reckless driving causing great bodily harm, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.62(4). He argued that he did not receive a fair trial due to amnesia and that the penalty provision of negligent vehicular injury denied him equal protection.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's truck collided with maintenance vehicles in a construction zone, killed one worker, and injured another. Defendant had no memory of the accident. An expert found that defendant suffered from amnesia, even one year after the accident. The court found that defendant was not denied a fair trial due to his amnesia. He and his attorney had the opportunity to construct a defense through information that defendant recalled prior to the collision. He was able to testify on a number of issues that ruled out potential causes of the accident. A reconstruction specialist and other experts provided a thorough reconstruction of the accident. The State had a strong case based on circumstantial evidence and defendant did not set forth any factors that may have impeded a fair trial. There was a rational basis for the legislature to punish vehicular homicide more severely than negligent vehicular injury and the statute did not violate the Equal Protection Clause. The court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1267 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Metro Builders Ass'n v. Town of Pewaukee


No. 93-2798


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


188 Wis. 2d 80; 524 N.W.2d 648; 1994 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1144



September 20, 1994, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waukesha County: ROBERT G. MAWDSLEY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, property owners and a building association, sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which dismissed their complaint against defendant town claiming the trial court erroneously concluded that their complaint failed to present a justiciable controversy and that they were required to exhaust administrative remedies before challenging the constitutionality of a town ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The complaint sought a declaratory judgment that the ordinance assessing impact fees as a condition of obtaining a building permit was unconstitutional. The trial court determined that appellants lacked standing to contest the validity of the ordinance because no one had applied for a building permit and had not been assessed the impact fee, they had not suffered any injury, no justiciable controversy was presented, and plaintiffs failed to exhaust administrative remedies. The court reversed. The complaint's allegations were sufficient to confer standing. Owners of real estate had standing to challenge the diminishment of their property's value by means of an unconstitutional ordinance, and businesses had a legally protectable interest in preventing injury to their businesses. Because the complaint alleged the ordinance in fact injured the plaintiffs' property and businesses a justiciable controversy was present. A case was ripe when the facts were sufficiently developed to admit conclusive adjudication. The action was not seeking review of an administrative decision, therefore, relief could not be afforded by an administrative agency.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court dismissing plaintiffs complaint was reversed and the cause was remanded.

 

1268 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sanders


Nos. 93-2284-CR, 93-2286-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


188 Wis. 2d 80; 524 N.W.2d 648; 1994 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1104



September 8, 1994, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgments of the circuit court for Wood County: EDWARD F. ZAPPEN, JR., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from judgments of the Circuit Court for Wood County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of several counts of causing great bodily harm by operating a vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant or controlled substance and hit and run, and sentenced him to five years in prison followed by a six-year period of probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant struck an oncoming vehicle while he made a left turn in front of the vehicle. The driver and her two children were seriously injured. Another motorist called for an ambulance. When the motorist returned, defendant was gone. Defendant arrived at his girlfriend's house and told her roommate that he had had been drinking and that he left the scene of the accident because he would go to jail. Defendant refused to call the police, as suggested. The police tested defendant's blood for tetrahydrocannabinols (THC) after they obtained a warrant to test his blood alcohol level. The court affirmed the conviction. The court held that: (1) once the police came into lawful possession of the blood samples, defendant lost any expectation of privacy, and the police could test for the presence of THC without violating defendant's Fourth Amendment rights; (2) the trial court properly excluded evidence of the driver's negligence because the law imposed strict criminal liability on one who injured another while operating a vehicle under the influence of alcohol or controlled substances; and (3) defendant did not have a defense of necessity because natural forces did not cause the accident.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of the trial court.

 

1269 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Hacker v. State Dep't of Health & Social Servs.


No. 93-1043


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


1994 Wisc. App. LEXIS 958



August 4, 1994, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION HAS NOT BEEN RELEASED FOR PUBLICATION IN THE PERMANENT LAW REPORTS. UNTIL RELEASED, IT IS SUBJECT TO REVISION OR WITHDRAWAL.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dodge County: JOSEPH E. SCHULTZ, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant licensee, who was the owner and operator of two community-based residential facilities (CBRFs), challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Dodge County (Wisconsin) that affirmed a decision of respondent, the Wisconsin Department of Health and Social Services (DHSS), that authorized the revocation of the operating licenses of both CBRFs.


OVERVIEW: The licensee was a registered nurse. In revoking her licenses, DHSS found that she had performed rectal examinations, gave a resident an enema, yelled at a resident, and taken other actions that were prohibited in CBRFs by Wis. Stat. §§ 50.01(1g), .09(1)(L), (1)(e). The licensee asserted that DHSS used an incorrect legal standard to revoke her licenses, that the standard used was unconstitutionally vague, that certain findings were unsupported by substantial evidence, and that license revocation was an inappropriate sanction. The court affirmed the judgment. Under Wis. Stat. § 50.01(1g), a CBRF was a place where no nursing care was provided to residents. Substantial evidence, consisting of the licensee's own concessions, the testimony of a CBRF employee, and other evidence supported the findings of DHSS that the licensee improperly provided nursing services on several occasions. The notice of intent to revoke the licenses provided the licensee with adequate notice of the factual and legal basis for the revocation. Although not all the charges against the licensee were proven, the license revocation was based on the four proven charges and it was not an excessive sanction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court order.

 

1270 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Corcoran


No. 93-2671-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


186 Wis. 2d 616; 522 N.W.2d 226; 1994 Wisc. App. LEXIS 954


May 31, 1994, Submitted On Briefs  
August 3, 1994, Released  
August 3, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waukesha County: MARIANNE E. BECKER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his destruction of computer data conviction under Wis. Stat. § 943.70(2)(a)(2), (b)(3) entered by the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin). Defendant claimed federal copyright law pre-empted state law, that the state criminal statute was overbroad and vague, constituted involuntary servitude, and that the statute violated equal protection.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was hired to write specialized computer software. Concerned that he would not be paid for his work due to the work's quality, defendant created programs to delete computer data. Plaintiff state prosecutor charged defendant with the felony destruction of computer data. Defendant brought a motion to dismiss the information, alleging that federal copyright law pre-empted the state statute, that the statute was vague and unenforceable, impaired his right to contract, constituted involuntary servitude, and violated his equal protection rights. The trial court denied defendant's motion, holding that pre-emption did not apply and that the destruction was of the company's data, not defendant's program. The trial court entered a conviction. Defendant appealed. The reviewing court affirmed, finding that where defendant did not have a copyright on the company's data, the statute did not result in defendant's financial loss, defendant was not being forced to fill contract terms, and the statute was not vague or overbroad, the conviction was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The reviewing court affirmed the trial court's conviction of defendant for felony destruction of computer data, holding that where defendant did not have a copyright for data, defendant suffered no financial loss, defendant was not forced to fill contract terms, and the statute was not vague or overbroad, the conviction was proper.

 

1271 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brooks


No. 93-2696-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


187 Wis. 2d 292; 523 N.W.2d 208; 1994 Wisc. App. LEXIS 942



August 2, 1994, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JOHN A. FRANKE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of failing to summon or provide assistance to a victim of a crime, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 940.34(2)(a). Defendant also appealed from an order denying his motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that Wis. Stat. § 940.30(2)(a) was unconstitutional because it was unduly vague and ambiguous. Because the court had previously upheld the statute against the same challenge, it did not address that argument. Defendant also argued that the trial court misused its discretion by admitting photographs of the victim into evidence and functioning as an advocate for the state, and thereby demonstrating bias towards defendant. The court found that the trial court applied the proper legal standards to the facts of record to reach a reasonable conclusion. Admission of the photographs was proper because they related to the issue that the victim was exposed to bodily harm. The trial court properly directed counsel to comment upon what he expected to prove by way of a defense. The court concluded that the trial judge did not violate defendant's constitutional right to a fair trial because no bias was apparent from the record. The basis for defendant's motion for a new trial was trial court error, which the court had determined to be meritless. No substantial probability existed, therefore, that a new trial would have produced a different result.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's orders convicting defendant for failing to summon or provide assistance to a crime victim and denying defendant's motion for postconviction relief.

 

1272 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Slavik v. Labor & Indus. Review Comm'n


No. 93-3342


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


187 Wis. 2d 293; 523 N.W.2d 208; 1994 Wisc. App. LEXIS 946



August 2, 1994, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Outagamie County: DENNIS C. LUEBKE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former employee brought an action challenging the decisions of appellees, the Labor and Industry Review Commission (LIRC) and the Department of Industry, Labor, and Human Relations (DILHR) to collect an overpayment of unemployment compensation to the employee. The employee appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Outagamie County which upheld the decisions.


OVERVIEW: Through DILHR error, the employee was paid unemployment compensation without reduction for the employee's pension benefits. The employee contended that both the DILHR and the LIRC improperly refused to exercise their authority to waive collection of the overpayment in view of the DILHR error. The appellate court first held that, because authority to waive recovery of an overpayment was not one of LIRC's specified statutory powers, and the power to waive recovery was not implied in its review functions, the LIRC lacked authority to waive recovery of the overpayment or to direct the DILHR to do so. Further, the court lacked statutory authority for judicial review of the DILHR's discretionary administrative decision to collect the overpayment and, in any event, no statutory grounds for reversing the decision existed.


OUTCOME: The judgment upholding the decisions of the LIRC and the DILHR was affirmed.

State v. La Plante


No. 93-1672-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


186 Wis. 2d 427; 521 N.W.2d 448; 1994 Wisc. App. LEXIS 862


March 1, 1994, Submitted on Briefs  
July 19, 1994, Released  
July 19, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JOHN A. FRANKE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted her of violating Wis. Stat. § 940.34, the failure to aid statute.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of violating the failure to aid statute, Wis. Stat. § 940.34. She sought review and contended that the statute was unconstitutionally vague. The court held that, when examining a challenge to the constitutionality of a statute, it engaged in a de novo review and was required to indulge every presumption to sustain the constitutionality of the statute. The court found that the statute was not vague because it sufficiently warned persons that their conduct came near the proscribed area. The court held that the evidence proved that defendant knew that a crime was in the process of occurring and that the victim was exposed to bodily harm from such crime. The court found that the statute had not violated her right against self-incrimination because she was merely required to summon assistance and was not forced to compel information in violation of the Fifth Amendment privilege. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of violating the failure to aid statute.

 

1274 of 2046 DOCUMENTS



City of Brookfield v. Public Serv. Comm'n


No. 93-0608


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


186 Wis. 2d 129; 519 N.W.2d 718; 1994 Wisc. App. LEXIS 762


November 11, 1993, Submitted On Briefs  
June 22, 1994, Released  
June 22, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waukesha County: PATRICK L. SNYDER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner municipalities appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which affirmed respondent Public Service Commission's order permitting respondent Milwaukee Metropolitan Sewerage District to charge the municipalities for the recovery of capital costs on the basis of taxable property value.


OVERVIEW: This case continued the decade-long dispute between the Sewerage District and municipalities outside of the district, over the municipalities respective share of the Sewerage District's annual capital costs. The dispute centered around funding for the Sewerage District's capital improvement program known as the Water Pollution Abatement Project. The sole issue on appeal was whether the Sewerage District's property value based method was permissible under Wis. Stat. § 66.91(5)(c). The Commission ruled that the Sewerage District's method of allocating capital costs to the municipalities based on property values was reasonable and not unjustly discriminatory, and was authorized by § 66.91(5)(c)2. The municipalities did not appeal the Commission's findings that the property value method was reasonable and not unjustly discriminatory. Instead, the municipalities argued that § 66.91(5)(c) did not provide the Sewerage District with the authority to charge on a property value basis in this case. The court agreed with the Commission that the Sewerage District's use of property values in this case was permissible under § 66.91(5)(c), by the plain language of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, which affirmed the Commission's order.

1276 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lewis


No. 93-2139-CR-NM


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


185 Wis. 2d 918; 520 N.W.2d 291; 1994 Wisc. App. LEXIS 729



June 14, 1994, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: LEE E. WELLS, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a bench trial in the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), defendant was convicted of first-degree intentional homicide and burglary, in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 940.01(1) and 943.10(1)(a). The trial court sentenced defendant to life in prison, with parole eligibility in 2028, for the homicide, and to a concurrent 10-year prison term for the burglary. Defendant appealed; his counsel filed a no-merit report.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of killing the victim and burglarizing her residence. The victim had been repeatedly struck with a hibachi grill, and there was evidence of strangulation. A witness identified defendant as the man he saw carrying property later identified as the victim's from her backyard. Defendant admitted entering the residence to burglarize it, but he claimed to have no memory of anything else. Affirming the conviction and sentence, the court rejected defendant's claim that an interrogating officer's "false friend" approach made several of his statements to the officer involuntary. The life sentence and parole eligibility date were not inappropriate; although defendant's life was shattered by alcohol and drug abuse and he had taken some positive steps in his life, the slaying was brutal and committed intentionally to eliminate a witness. The crime was planned against a handpicked, vulnerable victim. Wis. Stat. § 943.10 was not unconstitutional as failing to distinguish between burglary and breaking and entering; burglary by definition required only the entry into a home with the intention of stealing or committing a felony.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

 

1277 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bush


No. 93-2495


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


185 Wis. 2d 716; 519 N.W.2d 645; 1994 Wisc. App. LEXIS 671


April 25, 1994, Submitted On Briefs  
June 1, 1994, Released  
June 1, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Eau Claire County: GREGORY A. PETERSON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a postconviction order from the Circuit Court, Eau Claire County, Wisconsin. Under the order, his motion to strike and to order a new presentence investigation report (PSI) was denied. Defendant was convicted of attempted second-degree assault as a repeater. His motion to correct his sentence under the attempt statute, Wis. Stat. § 939.32(1) was also denied.


OVERVIEW: The PSI contained inaccuracies about defendant's prior inpatient treatment. He moved the trial court to modify his sentence based in part on these inaccuracies. Although the sentence was later modified and he was placed on probation, he never sought modification of his PSI. When probation was revoked, his motion to strike the PSI was denied on grounds of waiver and public policy. Based on the procedural posture of the case, the court concluded that the motion was properly denied. The trial court had no express authority to grant the relief requested. Policy principles and considerations of judicial administration dictated that courts should not exercise their jurisdiction to correct a PSI for reasons solely related to the Department of Corrections Administration. Defendant's motion to correct his sentence was properly denied. Under § 939.32(1), a sentence for an attempted crime was half the maximum sentence for the completed crime. Under Wis. Stat. § 939.50(3)(c), the maximum sentence for sexual assault was 10 years. Under Wis. Stat. § 939.62(1)(b, defendant's sentence could be increased up to six years based on his repeater status. The 11-year sentence was correctly calculated.


OUTCOME: The order denying defendant's motion to strike and correct his PSI and to correct his sentence was affirmed.

Lukas v. City of Milton


No. 93-0692


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


185 Wis. 2d 709; 520 N.W.2d 110; 1994 Wisc. App. LEXIS 645



May 26, 1994, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Rock County: MICHAEL J. BYRON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a builder, appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin), which remanded the builder's zoning petition to defendant, the City, for redetermination.


OVERVIEW: The builder commenced an action alleging several claims related to the City's denial of his rezoning petition. The trial court concluded that the denial was arbitrary and capricious because the plan commission and city council failed to state reasons for the denial. The trial court remanded the matter to the City for a redetermination of the petition "as if it had just been filed." The builder appealed, arguing that Milton Wis. Ordinances § 9.17, a mobile home park zoning ordinance, was unconstitutionally vague. The court held that even though § 9.17 did not include meaningful criteria by which approval of mobile home park zoning was governed, the standards provided in § 9.17 were sufficient because it provided sufficient guidance and adequate criteria for judicial review of the City's decision on a petition. The builder argue that § 9.17 was violative of equal protection. The court did not address the issue because the builder did not show any compelling reason, and the City was deprived of an opportunity to make a record and present evidence supporting the constitutionality of its ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1279 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ameritech Corp.


No. 93-1750


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


185 Wis. 2d 686; 517 N.W.2d 705; 1994 Wisc. App. LEXIS 828


February 1, 1994, Submitted On Briefs  
May 26, 1994, Released  
May 26, 1994, Filed [***1] 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: MARK A. FRANKEL, Judge. Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State appealed a decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which granted a motion filed by defendant corporation to strike the State's request for a jury trial in an action involving the promotion and issuance of credit cards. Other defendants were a bank and affiliates of the bank and the corporation.


OVERVIEW: The State filed an action against defendants, seeking injunctive relief and the imposition of civil forfeitures and penalties for violation of the deceptive advertising law, Wis. Stat. § 100.18(1), and for multiple provisions of the Wisconsin Consumer Act, Wis. Stat. §§ 421-427. The violations were in connection with the promotion and issuance of the corporation's credit cards. The State requested a jury trial, and the corporation filed a motion to strike the request on the ground that the suit was an equitable action. The trial court granted the motion, and the State appealed. The court affirmed, holding that a party had a constitutional right to have a statutory claim tried to a jury when the statute codified an action known to the common law in 1848 and when the action was regarded as at law in 1848. Because those conditions were not satisfied, the State was not entitled to a jury trial on the issue of the corporation's liability.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of the corporation's motion to strike the State's request for a jury trial.

 

1280 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


City of Milwaukee v. Kilgore


No. 92-0949


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


185 Wis. 2d 499; 517 N.W.2d 689; 1994 Wisc. App. LEXIS 621


May 4, 1993, Submitted On Briefs  
May 17, 1994, Released  
May 17, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JOHN E. MC CORMICK, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the Secretary of the Wisconsin Department of Transportation, a city, and three municipal judges, challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) that entered declaratory and injunctive relief in favor of respondent class, whose drivers' licenses had been suspended. The judgment prohibited suspension of drivers' licenses for nonpayment of forfeitures arising from non-traffic related offenses.


OVERVIEW: Members of the class had individually received orders from the Wisconsin Department of Transportation suspending their drivers' licenses for failure to pay fines imposed by municipal court judges for non-traffic charges. The class claimed that municipal courts were precluded from suspending operating licenses for nonpayment of forfeitures for violations of non-traffic city ordinances under Wis. Stat. § 343.30(5). The trial court had determined that statutory authority for suspension was unconstitutional. The court disagreed, reversed the judgment, and held that under Wis. Stat. §§ 800.09 and 800.095, municipal court judges had such authority and, further, that the statutory authority was constitutional. The court ruled that the lack of reference in Wis. Stat. § 343.30(5) to Wis. Stat. §§ 800.09, 800.095 was inadvertent and that the interpretation of Wis. Stat. § 343.30(5) had to include the insertion of references to Wis. Stat. §§ 800.09 and 800.095 to avoid an absurd result. The court also ruled that, because the suspension provision operated to secure the class's prospective compliance with the courts' orders, the Excessive Fines Clause of the Eighth Amendment did not apply.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which had prohibited municipal court judges from suspending drivers' licenses for failure to pay fines imposed for non-traffic offenses.

 

1281 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


City of Oak Creek v. State Dep't of Natural Resources


No. 93-1122


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


185 Wis. 2d 424; 518 N.W.2d 276; 1994 Wisc. App. LEXIS 582


December 15, 1993, Submitted on Briefs  
May 10, 1994, Released  
May 10, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: GEORGE A. BURNS, JR., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which affirmed a determination of respondent Division of Hearings and Appeals of Department of Administration for the State of Wisconsin (DHA). The circuit court ordered the city to remove a concrete channel from a creek and to submit to respondent State of Wisconsin Department of Natural Resources a plan for restoration of the creek.


OVERVIEW: The city relocated a creek by creating a concrete channel upon its bed without securing a permit from the appropriate authorities. The city challenged the circuit court's conclusion that Wis. Stat. § 30.055 was enacted in violation of the Wisconsin Constitution, the DHA's finding of navigability, the resulting applicability of chapter 30 of the Wisconsin Statutes permit requirements, and several findings that supported the conclusion that the creek had to be restored to its natural condition. Wis. Stat. § 30.055 provided that the city was not required to secure permits with regard to the creek. The court concluded that Wis. Stat. § 30.055 was a private or local law and, as such, was subject to the requirements of Wis. Const. art. IV, § 18, which required private or local laws to be passed only in single-subject bills. Because Wis. Stat. § 30.055 was not passed in a single-subject bill, it was enacted in violation of Wis. Const. art. IV, § 18 . The court also concluded that the DHA's finding of navigability and need for restoration were supported by credible and substantial evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders.

 

1282 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Safe Water Ass'n v. City of Fond du Lac


No. 93-2275


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


184 Wis. 2d 365; 516 N.W.2d 13; 1994 Wisc. App. LEXIS 529


March 8, 1994, Submitted On Briefs  
April 27, 1994, Released  
April 27, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Fond du Lac County: PETER L. GRIMM, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff clean water group sought review of the grant of summary judgment to defendant city on the group's request to enjoin the city from fluoridating water pursuant to ordinance by the Circuit Court for Fond du Lac County (Wisconsin). The group alleged that a stay granted by the trial court constituted prejudicial error, that the ordinance was not a valid exercise of the city's powers, and that the ordinance violated their right to privacy.


OVERVIEW: In 1950, the city council passed an ordinance authorizing the use of fluorine in the city's water. From many years the city used sodium fluoride as the fluoridation agent and later it used hydrofluosilicic acid. Both compounds were approved by the Wisconsin Department of Natural Resources (DNR) for fluoridation. In response to the oversight in the ordinance in not specifying the other two compounds, the city passed an amendment authorizing fluoridation as approved by the DNR. At a hearing on the matter the group expressed its concern for the use of fluoridation in water. The group alleged that fluoride needlessly exposed residents to health dangers, while numerous other doctors stated that the additive would benefit dental health. The trial court froze discovery pending the outcome of the parties' summary judgment motions. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment for the city. The court held that the city properly exercised its powers in further the health and welfare of the city by way of the ordinance. The court also held that the group abandoned the discovery issue by filing its own summary judgment motion and that the group had no liberty right in fluoridation of water.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the city on the clean water group's request to enjoin the city from fluoridating water in the city.

 

1283 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Evers v. Sullivan


No. 92-1276


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


184 Wis. 2d 401; 516 N.W.2d 789; 1994 Wisc. App. LEXIS 385



April 14, 1994, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: P. CHARLES JONES, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which affirmed a decision of respondent, the Department of Corrections (DOC), determining the inmate's mandatory release date pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 302.11 (1984). The DOC classified the inmate as subject to § 302.11 even though some of the conduct for which the inmate was convicted occurred prior to the effective date of the act.


OVERVIEW: In 1988, the inmate was convicted of 23 felony counts and one misdemeanor count. The DOC calculated the inmate's mandatory release date by applying § 302.11, which became effective on June 1, 1984. The DOC asserted that classifying the inmate under the new law was the most rational choice because 20 of his 24 convictions were for offenses that occurred, at least in part, after the effective date of the statute. The DOC further claimed that its choice was consistent with the Legislature's intent to provide for a later mandatory release date. The inmate argued, inter alia, that applying the new law to him had an unconstitutional ex post facto effect. The court found that it was not the new law that caused the inmate's reclassification but his conviction for offenses that he committed after the effective date of the new law, for which the trial court imposed sentences to run concurrently with the inmate's previous sentence. Although the sentences for new offenses may have disrupted the inmate's expectation of serving the entirety of his original sentence under the old law, he put that expectation at risk by continuing to commit offenses after the effective date of the new law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1284 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Erickson Oil Prods. v. Wisconsin Dep't of Transp.


No. 93-2154


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


184 Wis. 2d 36; 516 N.W.2d 755; 1994 Wisc. App. LEXIS 344


March 22, 1994, Oral Argument  
April 5, 1994, Released  
April 5, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for St. Croix County: DONNA J. MUZA, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff oil company appealed a decision of the Circuit Court for St. Croix County (Wisconsin), which dismissed its action against the State, the Department of Transportation (DOT), and the Department of Development (DOD), seeking only injunctive relief to prevent the State from conveying land to a third party and specific performance of a land sale contract between the oil company and the State.


OVERVIEW: The oil company and the State entered into a contract for the purchase of State-owned land at a highway interchange. Spite the fact that the oil company was the only developer to submit an offer, the State rejected its offer to purchase and returned a down payment. The trial court dismissed the oil company's action for declaratory and injunctive relief, and on appeal, the court affirmed. The State had not consented to be sued for specific performance of a contract for the sale of State surplus real estate. The court declined to adopt the reasoning of other jurisdictions and conclude that by authorizing the DOT to enter into contracts for the sale of State-owned land, the Wisconsin Legislature intended that such contracts be enforceable and binding on both parties and thus the legislature consented to such suits to enforce these contracts. It was not for the courts in Wisconsin to preempt the legislature's function to determine when and how it may be sued. A remedy was available to the oil company in that Wis. Stats. ch. 16 provided a procedure for submitting a claim to a state claims commission which could recommend to the Legislature that the claim be paid.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of the oil company's suit for injunction and specific performance based on the State's asserted sovereign immunity was affirmed.

State v. Edwards

OVERVIEW: Defendant's theory of defense at trial was that he thought he was going to have sex with a "nice girl" as a result of mutual consent, but his accuser was actually a prostitute who wanted cocaine in exchange for sex and claimed rape after he told her he did not have any drugs. Defendant argued that the trial court unconstitutionally prejudiced the credibility of his theory when it refused to allow three defense witnesses to testify about the accuser's cocaine use and prostitution activities. The instant court disagreed. As the evidence proffered was either not probative or was unreliable concerning the accuser being a prostitute or using drugs, the trial court properly refused to admit the testimony.
