1286 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Carlson & Erickson Builders v. Lampert Yards


No. 93-0195


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


183 Wis. 2d 220; 515 N.W.2d 305; 1994 Wisc. App. LEXIS 457; 1994-1 Trade Cas. (CCH) P70,569


November 23, 1993, Submitted on briefs  
March 22, 1994, Decided  
March 22, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal and Cross-Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Door County: John D. Koehn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded with directions. No costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an antitrust action, defendants, a lumber supplier and a building contractor, appealed from a decision of the Circuit Court for Door County (Wisconsin), which partially denied their challenge to a jury verdict in favor of plaintiff building contractor. Plaintiff cross-appealed from the trial court's remittitur order, which granted plaintiff the option of a reduced verdict or a new trial on damages.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff alleged that defendants violated the unfair trade provisions of Wis. Stat. § 133.05(1), (2) by engaging in the secret payment of unearned discounts, special services, or privileges not extended to all purchasers on like terms and conditions. Plaintiff also alleged that the supplier violated Wis. Stat. § 133.04 by engaging in price discrimination between different purchasers. A jury awarded damages to plaintiff on both claims. On appeal, the court held that: (1) the trial court erred in instructing the jury to apply the ordinary burden of proof because civil damage claims alleging violations of §§ 133.04 and 133.05 required the "middle" standard of proof -- clear, satisfactory, and convincing evidence -- and, thus, defendants were entitled to a new trial; (2) section 133.05(2) required plaintiff to prove that defendant contractor knew that any unearned discounts, special services, or privileges it received were secret and that they were not extended to all purchasers on like terms and conditions; and (3) defendant contractor failed to demonstrate that § 133.05 was void for vagueness, even though "unearned discounts" and "like terms and conditions" were not defined.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision and remanded the case for a new trial on both liability and damages.

 

1287 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Barman


No. 93-2102-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


183 Wis. 2d 180; 515 N.W.2d 493; 1994 Wisc. App. LEXIS 547


February 7, 1994, Submitted on briefs  
March 15, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal and Cross-Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: Jack Aulik, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded. No costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed an order of the circuit court (Wisconsin), which dismissed charges against defendant of homicide by negligent operation of a vehicle. Defendant cross-appealed the trial court's ruling that Wis. Stat. §§ 940.10, 939.25 were not unconstitutionally vague in violation of his equal protection and due process rights.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with homicide by negligent operation of a vehicle. On defendant's motions to dismiss the complaint, the trial court found sufficient probable cause and concluded that Wis. Stat. § 940.10 was not unconstitutionally vague. However, it dismissed the complaint based on the State's failure to rebut defendant's prima facie claim of discriminatory prosecution. On appeal by both sides, the court reversed as to the finding of discriminatory prosecution and otherwise affirmed. Defendant failed to show that the prosecution was motivated by a desire to deny his constitutional right or a desire to adversely affect him. Even if defendant had made such a prima facie showing, the prosecutor validly exercised his prosecutorial discretion because the prosecution was based on reevaluation of the applicable law. The other factors considered, such as the extent of harm and the deterrent effect of prosecution, showed a rational basis for a charging decision. Contrary to defendant's assertion, the phrase "ordinary negligence to a high degree" was not unconstitutionally vague, and the evidence provided probable cause for the conclusion that defendant committed vehicular homicide.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that dismissed charges against defendant of homicide by negligent operation of a vehicle. The court affirmed the order insofar as it ruled that the negligent vehicular homicide statute was not unconstitutionally vague in violation of his equal protection and due process rights.

 

1288 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Price


Nos. 92-0065-CR, 92-0976-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


183 Wis. 2d 428; 516 N.W.2d 19; 1994 Wisc. App. LEXIS 282



March 9, 1994, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Winnebago County: ROBERT A. HAASE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Winnebago County (Wisconsin) that convicted him of endangering safety by conduct regardless of life and of being a party to the crimes of first-degree intentional homicide, kidnapping, pointing a firearm, and false imprisonment in the death of the victim. The court also denied his postconviction motion seeking a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that he did not receive effective assistance of trial counsel and that the failure of another person involved in the events leading to the death of the victim to testify violated his due process rights. The court affirmed the judgment and order. The court explained that in order to prevail on his ineffective assistance of counsel claim, defendant had to show that there was a reasonable probability that, but for his counsel's unprofessional errors, the result of the proceeding would have been different. The court noted that a reasonable probability was a probability sufficient to undermine confidence in the outcome. The court found no prejudice in defense counsel's failure to cross-examine a witness regarding inconsistencies in his testimony. The court opined that it was a reasonable strategic to permit testimony regarding a prior violent incident involving defendant that otherwise would have been inadmissible in an effort to impeach several State witnesses. Because the witness who refused to testify was entitled to be advised of his Fifth Amendment rights, the court found no due process violation when the witness invoked those rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and the denial of his postconviction motion for a new trial.

 

1289 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


University of Wisconsin La Crosse Found. v. Town of Washington


No. 93-1163


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


182 Wis. 2d 490; 513 N.W.2d 417; 1994 Wisc. App. LEXIS 129


December 17, 1993, Oral argument  
February 24, 1994, Decided  
February 24, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for La Crosse County: Michael J. Mulroy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff university foundation appealed a judgment for the Circuit Court of La Crosse County (Wisconsin), which dismissed its action against defendants, a town and a county, for a refund of real estate taxes paid on an arboretum and a declaration that the arboretum was exempt from general property taxes under Wis. Stat. § 70.11(20).


OVERVIEW: Although a county board had not approved a property tax exemption for the arboretum as authorized by Wis. Stat. § 70.11(20), the foundation sought a tax refund and a declaration of the arboretum's tax-exempt status. The circuit court dismissed the foundation's action because the county board had not approved the exemption. On appeal, the court affirmed the dismissal by finding that the circuit court reached the right result for the wrong reason. The court held that § 70.11(20) was unconstitutional because the delegation of power to the county board to approve or disapprove a property tax exemption violated the state constitution in many respects. The power to grant tax exemptions was vested solely in the legislature under Wis. Const. art. IV, § 1, and was not a power of a local, legislative, and administrative character which the legislature could delegate to a county board under Wis. Const. art. IV, § 22. Further, Wis. Stat. § 70.11(20) violated the uniformity clause, Wis. Const. art. VIII, § 1. The part of Wis. Stat. § 70.11(20) which required the county board to approve the tax exemption could not be severed from the remainder of the statute to preserve its constitutionality.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's order in favor of the town and county.

 

1290 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hanson


No. 93-1921-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


182 Wis. 2d 481; 513 N.W.2d 700; 1994 Wisc. App. LEXIS 194


December 28, 1993, Submitted on briefs  
February 23, 1994, Decided  
February 23, 1994, Filed [***1] 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Kenosha County: Mary Wagner-Malloy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), for enticement of a child with the intent of exposure, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 948.07(3), arguing that § 948.07(3) violated his constitutional rights to equal protection.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant challenged only the constitutionality of the child enticement statute and subsequent conviction. The court examined the statute under the rational basis analysis because defendant's claim did not involve fundamental rights or a suspect criterion. Defendant argued that the statutory penalty scheme of the child enticement statute was irrational. He asserted that there was no reason why enticement to commit the act of exposure, a Class C felony, should be more serious and thus have a greater penalty than the act of exposure itself, a Class A misdemeanor. The court held the gravamen of the crime was not the commission of an enumerated act, but succeeding in getting a child to enter a place with intent to commit such a crime. Defendant's second, related issue was whether Wis. Stat. § 948.07(3) was unconstitutional as applied to him. He argued that he was denied equal protection because it was irrational for § 948.07(1) to distinguish between acts against children under and over the age of 16, while § 948.07(3) applied to acts against children of any age. The court agreed with the state that this distinction was not a basis for an equal protection challenge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1291 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brelove


No. 93-1055-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


182 Wis. 2d 511; 514 N.W.2d 879; 1994 Wisc. App. LEXIS 395



February 22, 1994, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JANINE P. GESKE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of 36 crimes stemming from six distinct incidents of sexual assault, and from the order denying his request for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with eight distinct assaults. Charges relating to one of the assaults were severed, and defendant was convicted of six assaults and related crimes. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court rejected defendant's claim that the trial court erroneously exercised its discretion in failing to sever certain counts, finding that the initial joinder of the charges was proper because all of the incidents occurred within a very limited geographic area, each incident involved a young, black female who was traveling alone, each incident involved the use or threat of use of a weapon, and all of the incidents took place over a relatively short period of time. The court also concluded that the trial court properly considered the prejudice resulting from its failure to sever the offenses. The trial court did not deny defendant his right to due process of law and a fair trial by not dismissing certain counts based upon destruction of allegedly exculpatory evidence where defendant failed to show bad faith on the part of the police. Line-up procedures used to identify defendant were not unduly suggestive. There was sufficient evidence to support the convictions.


OUTCOME: The judgment and order were affirmed.

 

1292 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


City of River Falls v. St. Bridget's Catholic Church


No. 93-2637


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


182 Wis. 2d 436; 513 N.W.2d 673; 1994 Wisc. App. LEXIS 161


January 31, 1994, Submitted on briefs  
February 15, 1994, Decided  
February 15, 1994, Filed [***1] 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Pierce County: Robert W. Wing, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city filed an action against defendant church, after it refused to pay a public fire protection charge, seeking a declaration that Wis. Stat. § 196.03(3)(b) was constitutional and that the charge was a fee, not a tax. The Circuit Court for Pierce County (Wisconsin) held that § 196.03(3)(B) was constitutional and was a fee. The church sought review of the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The trial court noted that (1) the charge could be imposed by either a public or a private water utility, (2) the city imposed the charge in its capacity as a utility to pay its operational expenses, not as a municipality to collect revenue, and (3) nonpayment of the charge did not result in a lien on the customer's property. On appeal, the church argued that the trial court erred by concluding that § 196.03(3)(b) imposed a fee and not an unconstitutional tax on otherwise tax exempt properties. The court found that the difference between taxes and fees was that the primary purpose of a tax was to obtain revenue for the government, while the primary purpose of a fee was to cover the expense of providing a service or of regulation and supervision of certain activities. The charge was a fee and not a tax because the primary purpose of the charge was to cover the expense of making water available, storing water, and ensuring that water would be delivered in case it was needed to fight fires. The fact that the charge lacked some of the common characteristics of a tax supported the conclusion that the charge was a fee and not a tax.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

James A. O. v. George C. B. (In re James A. O.)


No. 93-1216-FT


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN

November 24, 1993, Submitted on briefs

February 1, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: Gary A. Gerlach, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a mother and son, sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which dismissed their petition for adjudication of the paternity of the son because the petition was time-barred under Wis. Stat. § 893.88 and awarded respondent alleged father attorney's fees and costs.


OVERVIEW: The 25-year-old son and his mother brought an action against his alleged father to establish paternity to allow the son to qualify for financial aid and other benefits. The lower court dismissed the action as time-barred under § 893.88 and the court affirmed the dismissal. The court found that Wis. Const. art. I, § 9 was not violated by the dismissal of the action because the statute gave the son 19 years within which to file an action and the father was entitled to be free from the claim under the statute at a certain point. The court determined that the statute of limitations in the statute was a reasonable limitation imposed by the legislature. The court reversed the award of costs and attorney's fees to the alleged father because the son and mother's cause of action was supported by a substantial argument for modification of the existing law and the fact that they did not prevail did not render their action frivolous.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of appellants' paternity suit based on the statute of limitations, but reversed and vacated the award of attorney's fees and costs to the alleged father.

State ex rel. Seibert v. Husz

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Outagamie County (Wisconsin), which affirmed respondent parole commission's denial of parole to the prisoner. The commission based its decision to deny parole on the prisoner's failure to participate in and complete a sex offender treatment program (SOTP).


OVERVIEW: The prisoner contended that the trial court erred by concluding that the commission's decision to deny parole had a rational basis in the record and was not arbitrary and capricious. Further, the prisoner contended that the commission unconstitutionally based its decision on his non-participation in SOTP because the program required him to admit his guilt of the two second-degree sexual assault crimes of which he was convicted, which violated his constitutional right not to incriminate himself. In addition, the commission's determination that the prisoner posed an "unreasonable risk to the public" was authorized by Wis. Adm. Under the plain language of § PAC 1.06(7), the failure to attend SOTP was a permissible ground for denying parole. The commission's decision was not based on the prisoner's refusal to admit his guilt of the sexual assaults.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to affirm the commission's denial of parole to the prisoner.

 

1295 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gordon


No. 93-2156-CR-FT


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


181 Wis. 2d 370; 514 N.W.2d 424; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1675



December 28, 1993, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Shawano county: THOMAS G. GROVER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction in the Circuit Court for Shawano County (Wisconsin) for misdemeanor welfare fraud in violation of Wis. Stat. § 49.12(6), as well as the trial court's order denying her postconviction motions to vacate and dismiss the conviction on the grounds of double jeopardy.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was receiving food stamps through the county but failed to report that her son was employed and living in her home. When the county investigated, defendant lied and said her son was living elsewhere; she was charged under a county ordinance for making false representations in a welfare fraud investigation. She admitted to this charge and was ordered to pay a forfeiture. Subsequently, the state charged her with misdemeanor welfare fraud for failing to report her son's income; defendant pleaded guilty. On appeal, she claimed that the double jeopardy clause barred the second prosecution. Affirming, the court held that the double jeopardy clause was not implicated because the county action was a civil action rather than a criminal prosecution and the civil action did not result in the imposition of a criminal punishment but in a civil forfeiture. Also, the elements of the civil offense and criminal offense were not identical as required for application of the double jeopardy clause. Merely because the investigator advised her that public assistance could be denied her if she refused to cooperate was not coercive or violative of defendant's right against self-incrimination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for welfare fraud.

State v. Udulutch


No. 92-2306


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


181 Wis. 2d 365; 514 N.W.2d 421; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1620



December 16, 1993, Released [*1] 


NOTICE: UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Columbia county: WALLACE A. BRADY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant unlicensed business operator sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court, Columbia County (Wisconsin), which entered judgment on the pleadings in favor of respondent State, enjoined him from operating an unlicensed business, and ordered him to pay a forfeiture. The unlicensed business operator argued that the State waived its right to assert sovereign immunity and that the licensing statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Wis. Stat. § 105.01(1) (1985) provided that anyone who assisted employers in obtaining employees for a fee was an employment agent that was required to obtain a license under Wis. Stat. § 105.05(1). The court rejected the unlicensed business operator's contention that the licensing statute was void for vagueness. The court found that the statute was clear as it applied to the unlicensed business operator because he admitted that he assisted employers in obtaining employees for a fee. The court determined that the unlicensed business operator lacked standing to raise the statute's vagueness because his conduct fell within the statute's clear proscriptions. However, the court determined that the trial court erred in granting judgment on the pleadings on the ground that the unlicensed business operator lacked standing to raise an equal protection challenge to the statute. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in part and reversed it in part, finding that he had sufficiently alleged unequal protection of the laws and a personal stake in the controversy's outcome to challenge the statute's unequal treatment of contingent fee and non-contingent fee employer-paid search firms.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order granting judgment on the pleadings in favor of the State in part, reversed in part, and remanded with directions permitting the unlicensed business operator to bring his equal protection argument.

Grall v. Bugher

Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


181 Wis. 2d 163; 511 N.W.2d 336; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1622

December 16, 1993, Decided  
December 16, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to review filed.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: Mark A. Frankel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff purchasers of new automobiles (purchasers) sought review of the decision of the circuit court for Dane county (Wisconsin), which granted the motion to dismiss filed by defendant Department of Revenue (Department) and dismissed the purchasers' complaint alleging that the manufacturers' rebates they received should not have been subject to sales tax.


OVERVIEW: The purchasers bought their automobiles under a manufacturer's rebate program, and the sales tax was applied to the full, undiscounted price of the vehicles. The purchasers sued the Department, claiming that the "manufacturers' rebates" they received in connection with their purchases should not have been subject to the five percent state sales tax. The Department filed a motion to dismiss asserting that sovereign immunity barred the action. The trial court granted the motion and dismissed the complaint. The purchasers appealed. The court stated that the test for whether the principle of sovereign immunity applied was whether the relief sought would have required payment from state funds. The court stated that there was no question that the purchasers were seeking to recover funds from the state. The court held that the Department was immune from suit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

Village of Elm Grove v. Landowski


Nos. 93-0901, 93-1365


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin

December 1, 1993, Submitted on briefs  
December 15, 1993, Decided  
December 15, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Waukesha county: James R. Kieffer, Judge.

Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Walworth county: James L. Carlson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Two appeals were before the court in which defendants challenged the warnings given under the implied consent law, Wis. Stat. § 343.305(4). One defendant appealed his conviction for operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated (OWI), which followed the denial of his motion to suppress the chemical test result. A second defendant sought review of the revocation of his operator's license for refusing to take the test.


OVERVIEW: Defendants each held a regular Wisconsin driver's license at the time of his arrest for OWI. Before asking defendants to submit to chemical tests, the arresting officers advised them of all warnings required under the implied consent law, Wis. Stat. §343.305(4), including those that pertained to commercial vehicle operation. One defendant took the test and was subsequently convicted of OWI. The other refused the test and his license was revoked after a hearing. On appeal, defendants argued that the delivery of the commercial motor vehicle warnings to noncommercial operators violated the public policy and objectives of the implied consent law. Defendants agreed that each arresting officer followed the mandates of the implied consent law to the letter, by advising defendants of all required warnings, but claimed that such full compliance was fatal. The court ruled that the illogic of the argument was self-evident and that the officers could not have violated the statute by following it. The court also held that the delivery of the commercial motor vehicle warnings, to a suspect who only held a regular license, did not violate equal protection principles.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction for OWI and the revocation of the operator's license.

 

1299 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Coleman


No. 92-0705-CR-NM


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT I


181 Wis. 2d 364; 514 N.W.2d 421; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1602



December 14, 1993, Released [*1] 


NOTICE: UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: FRANK T. CRIVELLO, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of first-degree intentional homicide and one count of robbery; sentenced him to cumulative sentences of 10 years in prison on the robbery charge and life in prison on the homicide charge; and established his parole eligibility date for the homicide conviction at January 1, 2065.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's counsel filed a no merit report pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 809.32. The court reviewed the report and agreed that there was no arguable merit to any issue that could be raised on appeal. The trial court did not misuse its discretion when it excluded evidence that the victim was intoxicated, potentially suicidal, and had been involved in an altercation several hours before he was killed by defendant. Evidence of the victim's other wrongs or acts was not admissible to prove defendant acted in self-defense where there was no evidence that defendant knew of the prior wrongs or acts. For the same reason, information concerning the victim's prior criminal record would not have been admissible and the prosecution's failure to produce that information until the third day of trial was not grounds for a mistrial. The homicide sentence was based on a consideration of the requisite factors, was reasonable and not an abuse of discretion, and the trial court was authorized to set a parole eligibility date that was later than would otherwise apply pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 304.06. Defendant's representation at trial was not ineffective.


OUTCOME: The judgment and sentences were affirmed.

OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by a jury of first-degree sexual assault of a child, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 948.02(1). State v. Perry


No. 93-1309-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


181 Wis. 2d 43; 510 N.W.2d 722; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1557


October 25, 1993, Submitted on briefs  
December 7, 1993, Decided  
December 7, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Dunn county: James A. Wendland, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Dunn County (Wisconsin), which denied his request for postconviction relief after the jury found him not guilty of attempted murder but guilty of aggravated battery. Defendant contended that charging him with both aggravated battery and attempted intentional homicide for the same act was improper because the two crimes were inconsistent.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and a friend attacked the victim. Defendant argued that the victim was the aggressor. The state initially charged defendant with attempted intentional homicide; it later charged him with aggravated battery. On appeal, defendant contended that he was impermissibly charged with inconsistent crimes for the same act and that the trial court erred by denying his request for a lesser included offense instruction on the negligent use of a weapon. The court ruled that because defendant was convicted of, and therefore punished for, only one crime that it need not address a double jeopardy argument. As to the request for a lesser included offense instruction, the court concluded that the error, if any, was harmless and did not cause any prejudice. The court also held that because there were two persons charged with causing the victim's injuries, defendant and his friend, the trial court correctly determined that it would make the most sense to hold defendant's restitution hearing in conjunction with his co-defendant's hearing. Consequently, defendant was required to wait until the conclusion of the co-defendant's trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and the order.

Patricia H.C. v. Louise H. (In re Nastassja L.H.-J.)


No. 92-2681


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


181 Wis. 2d 666; 512 N.W.2d 189; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1538


July 21, 1993, Submitted on briefs  
December 2, 1993, Decided  
December 2, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for La Crosse county: Dennis G. Montabon, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a paternity action involving non-marital child, appellant mother sought review from an order of the Circuit Court, La Crosse County (Wisconsin), which granted respondent grandmother's petition seeking visitation pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 767.245.


OVERVIEW: A non-marital child, who lived with her mother, had a close relationship with her grandmother. After the mother terminated the relationship, the grandmother filed a petition, in an on-going paternity case, seeking visitation pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 767.245. The mother filed a motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction. After a hearing, the trial court granted the grandmother visitation. On appeal by the mother, the court affirmed. The court held that, pursuant to case law, the trial court had jurisdiction over the grandmother's petition because (1) there was an underlying paternity action over which the trial court had jurisdiction, and (2) the child's family was not intact because the father did not live with the mother and the child. The court declined to consider the mother's claim that Wis. Stat. § 767.245 violated her constitutional rights, because the mother failed to notify the attorney general of her claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which had been in favor of the grandmother.

 

1303 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jones


No. 92-1316-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


180 Wis. 2d 467; 514 N.W.2d 53; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1481



November 18, 1993, Decided [*1] 


NOTICE: UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Grant county: JOHN R. WAGNER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Grant County (Wisconsin) convicting him of first degree intentional homicide and burglary. Defendant asserted that the trial court erred by refusing to suppress evidence obtained during a search of the residence where he was a guest, and by refusing to suppress statements taken in violation of his right to remain silent and his right to counsel.


OVERVIEW: The victim's daughter signed a permission to search form and the officers found defendant and codefendant when they searched her home. The officers also found evidence incriminating them. The court concluded that the daughter's consent was voluntary. The presence of the officers was no basis to find a lack of voluntariness. The daughter could have questioned the form, but did not. When defendant made his first statement to police, a deputy told defendant that he was not under arrest but that he would have been by day's end. Defendant waived his right to an attorney and to remain silent. The court saw no harm in warning defendant of his Miranda rights prior to arrest and the deputy was not required to read defendant his Miranda rights after defendant returned from the rest room. Prior to the questioning that resulted in the second statement, an attorney was appointed to defendant. Midway through questioning by a captain, defendant's attorney appeared at the jail but was not permitted to see defendant until the interview ended. Defendant's Sixth Amendment right to counsel was not violated because adversarial judicial criminal proceedings had not been initiated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the trial court convicting defendant of first degree intentional homicide and burglary.

 

1304 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. White


No. 93-0008-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


180 Wis. 2d 203; 509 N.W.2d 434; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1434


October 4, 1993, Submitted On Briefs  
November 10, 1993, Released  
November 10, 1993, Filed [***1] 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Racine county: DENNIS J. FLYNN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin), which entered judgment upon defendant's conviction of failure to cause her daughter to attend school regularly, in contravention on Wis. Stat. § 118.15 (1989-1990).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by jury of failure to cause her daughter to attend school regularly, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 118.15 (1989-90). Defendant challenge her conviction. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held: (1) Wis. Stat. § 118.15, when viewed as a whole was not unconstitutionally vague, because the statute adequately explained what the term "attend school regularly" means; (2) the heading of Wis. Stat. § 118.15 indicated that school attendance was mandatory; (3) while the term "regularly" was not defined in Wis. Stat. § 118.15, it's common meaning indicated that "regularly" meant "on a regular basis" and "in a regular manner," and a person of ordinary intelligence would read the term "regularly" to mean to attend school "constantly and uniformly"; (4) Wis. Sat. § 118.15 cross-referenced Wis. Stat. 118.16, which defined truancy, and a person of ordinary intelligence would know that any unexcused absence of part of a day or all of one day was truancy; and (5) defendant had a hearing to resolve the truancy problem, and was on notice that her child was a truant, therefore, the statute was not vague for lack of sufficient warning to persons wishing to obey the law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that entered judgment upon defendant's conviction of failure to cause her daughter to attend school regularly.

 

1305 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Thiel


Nos. 93-1724-CR-FT, 93-1725-CR-FT


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


180 Wis. 2d 472; 514 N.W.2d 56; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1402



November 4, 1993, Released


NOTICE: UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waupaca county: JOHN P. HOFFMANN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Waupaca County (Wisconsin), which modified his sentence to remove a condition of his probation that would have allowed him, with his probation agent's permission, to possess a firearm for use during hunting season.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from his conviction, defendant argued that Wis. Stat. § 941.29, which forbid a convicted felon from possessing a firearm, was adopted after he had completed his sentence for a felony conviction and, as applied to him, was an ex post facto law. In affirming, the court ruled that in claimed ex post facto cases--where unpleasant consequences might be visited on an individual for prior conduct--the question was whether the legislative aim was to punish that individual for past activity, or whether the restriction of the individual came about as a relevant incident to a regulation of a present situation. The court held that the plain "legislative aim" of § 941.29 was protection of the public safety and that had the statute been intended as additional punishment for persons previously convicted of felonies, the legislature would not have provided various methods of obtaining relief from the prohibition against firearm possession. The court further held that applying § 941.29 to convicted felons, regardless of the date of the conviction, did not transform the statute into an unconstitutional ex post facto law, even though it bore harshly upon the person affected.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Northern States Power Co. v. Bugher


No. 92-1634


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1358



October 28, 1993, Decided [*1] 


NOTICE: UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from order of the circuit court for Dane county: JACK F. AULIK, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff power company sought review of the order of the circuit court for Dane County (Wisconsin) dismissing its 42 U.S.C. § 1983 action against defendant, certain past and present secretaries of the Wisconsin Department of Revenue.


OVERVIEW: The power company claimed as a charitable deduction the value of land it donated to the federal government for a scenic riverway. The department disallowed the deduction and assessed additional tax. The Tax Appeals Commission denied the company's petition for redetermination. The circuit court affirmed the order dismissing the company's petition for review. On appeal, the company raised an equal protection claim and the court held that the company's failure to bring this claim resulted in its waiver on appeal. Thereafter, the company brought a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action against the department's past and present secretaries to prevent the collection of the tax. The court noted that a § 1983 action could only be brought by taxpayers who had exhausted their administrative remedies, including judicial review. Because the company did not raise the equal protection issue before the commission, the court affirmed, finding that it failed to exhaust its administrative remedies and could not attack the additional franchise tax imposed on it on constitutional grounds.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed on appeal.

 

1307 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Mullen v. Braatz


No. 93-2076


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


179 Wis. 2d 749; 508 N.W.2d 446; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1354


August 27, 1993, Submitted on a motion  
October 26, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Barron county: Edward R. Brunner, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Barron County (Wisconsin), which dismissed their complaint against defendant. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the appeal, contending that jurisdiction was lacking because the notice of appeal was not timely filed. Defendant contended that he mailed a notice of entry of judgment, thus shortening the time for filing a notice of appeal to 45 days.


OVERVIEW: Judgment was entered for defendant. Three days later, defendant filed notice of entry of judgment with the clerk of the court and claimed to have sent a copy to plaintiffs. Thereafter, plaintiffs filed a notice of appeal 90 days after the entry of the judgment. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the appeal as not timely. On appeal, the court remanded. The court held that the presumption that mail sent was received was rebuttable. The court ruled that if the presumption was not rebuttable then it would have been unconstitutional as a violation of the Due Process Clause. The court concluded that plaintiffs should have had an opportunity to demonstrate that they did not receive the notice of entry of judgment, thereby making their notice of appeal timely. The court held that rebutting the presumption required a factual determination, and therefore the case was remanded to the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case for a factual determination by the trial court as to whether notice of entry of judgment was received by plaintiffs.

State v. Neumann


No. 92-2844-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


179 Wis. 2d 687; 508 N.W.2d 54; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1357


August 5, 1993, Oral argument  
October 26, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: Michael J. Barron, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which entered judgment on a jury verdict and convicted defendant of second-degree sexual assault in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.225(2)(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant and the victim had dated for several years and the relationship, while volatile at times, had not been violent. One evening, defendant became heavily intoxicated; the couple argued and, as defendant became aggressive, the victim unsuccessfully attempted to leave his company. On appeal from his conviction, defendant argued, among other things, that the trial court improperly instructed the jury that it could not consider evidence of the couple's prior consensual sexual contacts to determine whether the victim had consented to sexual intercourse on the date of the incident. The court agreed but, finding the error harmless, affirmed the conviction. The court, noting that the state had the burden to prove nonconsent, reasoned that although the jury should have been able to consider the prior consensual contact, the error was harmless because evidence of consent to prior non-violent contact was of no probative value regarding consent to sexual intercourse under the threat or use of violence. Also, rejecting defendant's arguments to the contrary, the court determined that § 940.225(2)(a) did not require the state to prove intent and was not unconstitutionally overbroad.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of second-degree sexual assault.

OVERVIEW: Pursuant to the parties' marital settlement agreement, the father had custody of the son during the school year and the mother had custody during the summer. 1310 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. O'Connell


No. 92-1254-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


179 Wis. 2d 598; 508 N.W.2d 23; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1285


May 6, 1993, Submitted on briefs  
October 7, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: George Northrup, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which convicted her of three counts of theft, one count of obtaining telecommunications service by fraud, and one count of participating in an enterprise through a pattern of racketeering activity.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued, inter alia, that (1) the complaint charging a violation of the Wisconsin Organized Crime Control Act (WOCCA), Wis. Stat. §§ 946.80-946.88, was deficient; (2) the thefts were not committed as part of an enterprise, preventing her conviction for racketeering; (3) WOCCA was unconstitutionally vague; and (4) the trial court erroneously exercised its discretion by failing to grant a continuance. Upon review, the court found defendant's arguments without merit. The disposition of the stolen goods was conducted within the business. That was the infiltration of legitimate business with racketeering money that WOCCA was designed to combat. On its face, and as applied to the facts of the case, the WOCCA definition of "pattern of racketeering activity" was not unconstitutionally vague. Defendant did not explain in what way the trial court's refusal to grant a continuance affected the quality of assistance her counsel provided, and the court found nothing on that subject in the record. The trial court did not erroneously exercise its discretion when it denied defendant's motion for a continuance.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions for three counts of theft, one count of obtaining telecommunications service by fraud, and one count of participating in an enterprise through a pattern of racketeering activity were affirmed.

Scheunemann v. City of West Bend


No. 92-3073


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


179 Wis. 2d 469; 507 N.W.2d 163; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1239


July 28, 1993, Submitted on briefs  
September 29, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Washington county: Richard T. Becker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizens sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Washington County (Wisconsin), which found in favor of defendants, city and associated individuals, in a declaratory judgment action in which the citizens challenged on statutory and constitutional grounds a city ordinance banning "cruising." The trial court upheld the ordinance's validity.


OVERVIEW: A number of business residents and other citizens complained to the police regarding the negative effects that cruising had on the area. Cars would cruise up and down the street causing congestion amongst other things. In response, the city passed a cruising ordinance. A number of citizens brought a declaratory judgment challenging the validity of the ordinance. The trial court granted the city's motion for summary judgment and withheld the validity of the ordinance. The court affirmed on appeal. The court found that the ordinance was specifically limited in its application to a designated daily time span and to a designated area. Moreover, the ordinance established standards for cruising. Thus, the ordinance was not unconstitutionally overboard. The court upheld the ordinance finding that under the intermediate scrutiny standard the ordinance was narrowly tailored to meet the city's objectives. The purpose of the ordinance was to create a safer and less congested public street thus it enhanced the constitutional right to travel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which found that the city's ordinance, was valid.

 

1312 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Fed. Land Bank v. Gruetzman


No. 92-2631


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


179 Wis. 2d 503; 508 N.W.2d 75; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1185



September 16, 1993, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Green county: WILLIAM D. JOHNSTON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bank sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Green County (Wisconsin), which adjudged that the applicable homestead exemption between the parties to be $ 40,000 in a declaratory judgment action.


OVERVIEW: The bank foreclosed upon certain real properties. The homestead exemption under Wis. Stat. § 815.20 was $ 25,000 when the mortgagor signed the promissory notes for the properties. The mortgagor purchased the real estate which he sought to have released from the bank's judgment lien. In the meantime, the homestead exemption under § 815.20 was increased to $ 40,000. The mortgagor sought to use the higher sum to offset the mortgage on the property where he resided. A declaratory suit was filed, and the trial court ruled that $ 40,000 was the proper exemption amount. The bank sought review. The court reversed in part, affirmed in part, and remanded, holding that under Campbell, in the analogous field of personal property exemptions, the Wisconsin Supreme Court had explicitly held that the amount of the statutory exemption as between debtor and creditor was determined by the amount of the exemption in effect when the contract between them was made. The Campbell decision was still binding precedent on the courts in Wisconsin.


OUTCOME: The court reversed in part, affirmed in part, and remanded the trial court's ruling that the $ 40,000 homestead exemption applied as opposed to the old $ 25,000 exemption in the declaratory action.

State v. Maday


No. 92-2989-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


179 Wis. 2d 346; 507 N.W.2d 365; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1181


July 28, 1993, Submitted on briefs  
September 15, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review dismissed.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Winnebago county: William E. Crane, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Winnebago County (Wisconsin), which denied his motion to prohibit the testimony of the State's experts in his trial for sexual contact with a minor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with two counts of sexual contact with two different minor boys. After his arraignment, the State filed notice of its intent to use expert testimony. Defendant filed a motion seeking psychological examinations of the witnesses by qualified psychologists. The trial court denied the motion. Defendant renewed the motion, without success, after receiving the written reports of the State's experts. Defendant petitioned for leave to appeal a nonfinal order. The court reversed and remanded the lower court's order and held that defendant should have been able to obtain access to all relevant evidence necessary to have been heard in his or her own defense. The court found that the trial court had the discretion to grant a motion for psychological examination of a victim after defendant presented evidence of a compelling need or reason for the examination and the trial court balanced the rights of the defendant against the interests of the victim.The court held that since the State was putting the behavior of the two witnesses into issue, fundamental fairness required that defendant had the opportunity to present relevant evidence to counter the State's evidence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded with directions the decision of the lower court, which denied defendant's motion to prohibit the testimony of the State's experts in his trial for sexual contact with a minor.

In re Paternity of Devon M.W.


No. 92-0753


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


179 Wis. 2d 501; 508 N.W.2d 74; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1143



September 2, 1993, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Dane county: SUSAN R. STEINGASS, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant putative father sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which denied part of his motion under Wis. Stat. § 806.07 to vacate a default paternity judgment.


OVERVIEW: The putative father sought to vacate a default order of paternity and assignment of his income for child support after blood tests revealed he was not the father of the child in question. The putative father also requested that all moneys wrongfully deducted from his salary be returned to him with interest. The family court entered judgment vacating the judgment of paternity, dismissing the complaint, ordering the refund of $ 200 to the putative father, and denying all other relief. The court found that the putative father's arguments did not establish that the judgment and order assigning his income were unlawful. The court found that there was nothing unjust about the assignment of his income pursuant to the default judgment. The court found that it did not appear that the family court exercised its discretion to consider whether it would have been equitable for respondent State to have retained the money it lawfully collected. The court found that during the time the State was collecting money, the putative father was lawfully adjudicated the father and found that once the judgment was vacated, the State stopped collecting funds.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the family court vacating the default judgment. The court reversed the decision of the family court in awarding a $ 200 refund to the putative father. The court remanded the case for the family court to determine the just terms for vacating the default judgment and to award the putative father statutory prejudgment interest on whatever amount it determined he was entitled to receive.

 

1316 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Allen


No. 93-0381-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


179 Wis. 2d 67; 505 N.W.2d 801; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1118


July 27, 1993, Submitted on briefs  
August 31, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Marathon county: Michael W. Hoover, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Marathon County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of first degree intentional homicide.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that a 10-month delay between his conviction and his sentencing violated his right to a speedy trial. The court agreed that the right to a speedy trial encompassed the time from which the person was accused until the time was sentencing. The court stated that the test to determine whether a defendant's speedy trial right was violated was: (1) the length of the delay; (2) the reason for the delay; (3) defendant's assertion of his right; and (4) prejudice to defendant. The court held that the 10 month delay was too long, and proceeded to consider the other factors. The court held that although the State asked for the continuances, its reason for delay was to wait for the determination in another court of the constitutionality of a statute, not to prejudice defendant, so the factor did not weigh heavily against the State. The court held that defendant had asserted his right. The court found no prejudice to defendant. Although defendant argued that he suffered anxiety in waiting to know his sentence, the court noted that defendant faced a mandatory life sentence. The court found no prejudice in the lack of programs at the county jail as opposed to state prison.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1317 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Vogt


No. 92-2693-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


178 Wis. 2d 877; 506 N.W.2d 427; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1079



August 25, 1993, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Winnebago county: BRUCE SCHMIDT, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court, Winnebago County, Wisconsin, that convicted him of possessing marijuana with intent to deliver it within 1,000 feet of a school in violation of Wis. Stat. § 161.41(1m)(h)2. Defendant also appealed from an order denying his postconviction motions for relief.


OVERVIEW: The court rejected defendant's claim that the trial court lost jurisdiction over him because it did not hold a preliminary hearing within 10 days of the initial appearance as required under Wis. Stat. § 970.03(2). The time limit was extended for cause because defendant had requested substitution of counsel on the day of the preliminary examination. His exercise of his right to substitution waived any time defect. Defendant claimed his statements implicating him in prior harvesting and delivery of marijuana were erroneously admitted. The evidence constituted "other acts" under Wis. Stat. § 904.04 but was admissible to show opportunity, intent, and knowledge as provided under § 904.04(2). The trial court did not misuse its discretion in concluding that the probative value outweighed any prejudicial effect. The evidence was also admissible as an admission by a party opponent. The trial court found that counsel's decision not to oppose the State's trial amendment was trial strategy. Based on the record from the postconviction motion hearing, the finding was not clearly erroneous. Because there was no trial error, the court did not grant a new trial in the interest of justice.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant of possession of marijuana with intent to deliver it within 1000 feet of a school was affirmed.

Fetzner v. Fetzner


No. 91-2050


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


178 Wis. 2d 875; 506 N.W.2d 426; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1039



August 19, 1993, Released [*1] 


NOTICE: UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: RICHARD J. CALLAWAY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Modified and, as modified, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent husband appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which denied the husband's motion for relief from an order under Wis. Stat. § 806.07 and awarded attorney's fees to petitioner wife on the motion.


OVERVIEW: When appealing a child support order, the husband claimed that Wis. Adm. Code § HSS 80.04(2), on which the trial court based the calculation of the support amount, was unconstitutional. The court, on appeal, concluded that the husband had waived the constitutionality of the rule because he failed to raise it in the trial court before commencing the appeal. In ruling on the husband's motion for relief from the trial court's order pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 806.07, the trial court denied the motion on the grounds that, on appeal, the court had expressly allowed application of the rule's standard in the case. The trial court then held that the husband's motion was frivolous and it awarded the wife $ 150 in fees. On appeal, the court modified the amount awarded and affirmed because the husband's attempt to raise the constitutionality issue by seeking relief from the order under § 806.07 did not cure his failure to raise the issue before the order was entered. Because the trial court lacked authority to award attorney's fees, the award was modified to conform with the trial court's discretionary authority under § 814.07 to award up to $ 50 in costs.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment by reducing the amount awarded to the wife to $ 50 and affirmed as modified. The court denied the wife's motion to dismiss the appeal as moot.

State v. Heft


No. 92-2938-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


178 Wis. 2d 823; 505 N.W.2d 437; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1045


June 18, 1993, Submitted on briefs  
August 18, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to review filed.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Racine county: Barbara A. Kluka, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin) that denied her motion for postconviction relief. She was convicted of homicide by the intoxicated use of a vehicle. She argued that her motion should have been granted because her rights to due process and equal protection were denied by the application of Wis. Stat. § 905.13, which prohibited comment upon a witness's claim of privilege.


OVERVIEW: Defendant did not contest the elements of the crime but rather sought to prove the affirmative defense contained in Wis. Stat. § 940.09(2) that the death would have occurred even if she had been exercising due care and had not been under the influence of an intoxicant. Defendant asserted that the accident and death of her passenger occurred because her car was rear-ended by another driver and was propelled off the road, where it subsequently rolled over. The other driver was called as witness outside of the presence of the jury, and he invoked the Fifth Amendment's protection against self-incrimination. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in refusing her requests that the other driver invoke Fifth Amendment privilege in the presence of the jury and that the jury be instructed that it could draw an inference from its invocation. The court disagreed. There were reasonable bases for the divergent treatment that Wis. Stat. § 905.13 accorded criminal and civil defendants regarding comment upon or inference from a claim of privilege. Moreover, despite the trial court's denials, defendant was able to offer significant evidence in support of her intervening cause defense.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order was affirmed.

 

1320 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bain


No. 92-0807-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 954



July 29, 1993, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Waupaca county: JOHN P. HOFFMANN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Waupaca County (Wisconsin) convicting him on four counts of soliciting prostitution in violation of Wis. Stat. § 944.32, and from an order denying his postconviction motion for a new trial. Defendant claimed that evidence did not sustain convictions on two counts, the counts were mutiplicitous, § 944.32 was unconstitutional as applied, and evidence of other acts was improperly admitted.


OVERVIEW: Defendant twice solicited two women to pay for sex and to recruit their female acquaintances to pay for sex. Defendant was charged with four counts of solicitation of repeated acts of prostitution in violation of Wis. Stat. § 944.32, one count for each time he solicited each woman. Since it was undisputed that the recruited women might elect to actively participate in sexual acts with others, including defendant, the evidence was sufficient to support a conviction under the statute. However, because § 944.32 punished solicitation of repeated acts of prostitution, it was error to charge defendant separately for soliciting each individual act of prostitution. This error required only that the trial court on remand amend the judgment to delete the statement of conviction and sentence on two of the counts. Defendant waived his claim that the statute was unconstitutional as applied because he failed to raise the issue by a motion before trial, as required by Wis. Stat. § 971.31(2). If evidence of other acts by defendant were improperly admitted, the error was harmless because the jury heard substantively identical admissible evidence and the trial judge gave a cautionary instruction.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction on two of the four counts was reversed, the judgment of conviction on the other two counts was affirmed, and the cause was remanded with instructions to the trial court to amendment the judgment to delete the statement of conviction and sentence on the two counts for which the convictions were reversed.

Nielsen v. Waukesha County Bd. of Supervisors


No. 93-0010


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


178 Wis. 2d 498; 504 N.W.2d 621; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 946


June 11, 1993, Submitted on briefs  
July 28, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Waukesha county: Robert G. Mawdsley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which found in favor of respondents, a county board of supervisors, property owners, and a management district. The circuit court held that the requisite number of valid signatures supported a petition asking the board to create the management district pursuant to Wis. Stat. ch. 33, subch. IV.


OVERVIEW: The landowners opposed the creation of the district, based on the required petitions. The trial court rejected the challenges to the county board's creation of the district and dismissed the action. On review, the court affirmed. A county board could create a public inland lake protection and rehabilitation district with over 51 percent of the landowners' signatures on petitions. Petitions were circulated within the proposed district. Each circulator verified his petition. The substantive words of the circulators' statements met the legal requirements for verification. First, each statement recited that it was made under oath. Therefore, the fundamental ingredient which gave a verification its trust and credibility was satisfied. Second, each statement carried the jurat of a notary public, signifying that the writing was sworn to by the person who signed it. Third, every person giving such an oath was deemed to have been lawfully sworn pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 887.03. Moreover, those who wished to withdraw from the petition were obligated to do so before the public hearing commenced. The withdrawals were untimely, unverified, and ineffective.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the county board's creation of the lake management district and affirmed the trial court's order dismissing the landowners' petition for judicial review.

 

1322 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Allin


No. 92-1326-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 935



July 27, 1993, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: JOHN J. DiMOTTO, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review after the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) convicted him, after a trial by jury, of violating the disorderly conduct statute, Wis. Stat. § 947.01.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a performance artist whose performance consisted of exposing his penis and later his anus, defecating on stage, rubbing feces on his chest and face, tossing feces into the audience, breaking a bottle over his head, simulating fellatio with the microphone, pulling a woman up on stage and pushing her off stage, and biting the breast of another male singer. The jury convicted defendant. The court affirmed. Because § 947.01 conveyed sufficiently definite warning as to the fact that abusive and indecent conduct, as measured by common understanding and practices, were proscribed by law, the claim that the statute was unconstitutionally vague had to fail. The statute as written was not overbroad. The combination of conduct and circumstances were crucial in applying the statute. No authority compelled only a prosecution under Wis. Stat. § 944.21, the obscene performance statute. The complaint was not invalid for intertwining protected conduct with conduct that was properly subject to prosecution. A common sense analysis of the complaint indicated that defendant's alleged actions not only tended to create or provoke a disturbance, but had in fact created a disorderly scene.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Dog Fed'n of Wis. v. City of S. Milwaukee


No. 92-2131


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


178 Wis. 2d 353; 504 N.W.2d 375; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 899


June 2, 1993, Submitted on briefs  
July 20, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to review pending.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: Thomas P. Doherty, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff association and individuals who claimed ownership of dogs that may have been subject to South Milwaukee, Wis., Code § 23.20, imposing restrictions on the ownership and keeping of pit bulls, brought suit against defendant city claiming that the ordinance was unconstitutional. After the filing of cross-motions for summary judgment, the circuit court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) granted the city's motion. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs claimed that the pit bull aspects of the ordinance were facially invalid because the definition of "pit bull" was impermissibly vague, the ordinance was overbroad, and it violated their right to equal protection of the law. Rejecting the contention that an ordinary person would not have been able to discern whether a dog was a pit bull as defined by the ordinance, the court held that the ordinance gave residents sufficient notice concerning the type of dog that was subject to its restrictions. The court added that problems of ultimate proof did not make the ordinance unduly vague on its face. With regard to the overbreadth argument, the court noted that the doctrine had no application outside the First Amendment context. Because no fundamental rights or suspect classes were involved, the rational basis standard was used for the equal protection argument. The court acknowledged that reasonable persons might have differed on the import of the material the common council considered regarding the danger the dogs posed. The court concluded that it could not have been said that the ordinance was arbitrary and had no reasonable purpose or reflected no justifiable public policy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment.

OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which convicted defendant of being a felon in possession of a firearm.

1326 of 2046 DOCUMENTS



State ex rel. Shroble v. Prusener


No. 92-3288


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


177 Wis. 2d 656; 503 N.W.2d 301; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 664


March 30, 1993, Submitted on briefs  
June 9, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to review filed.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Walworth county: Robert J. Kennedy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant candidate sought review of an order of the circuit court for Walworth county (Wisconsin) dismissing his quo warranto action claiming that respondent opponent illegally held the office of county supervisor. The trial court held that Wis. Stat. § 9.01, Wisconsin's recount statute, provided the sole means by which to challenge the opponent's right to hold office.


OVERVIEW: The candidate and opponent ran against each other for county supervisor. After the election, the opponent was declared the winner by 24 votes. The candidate did not seek a recount pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 9.01. The candidate was then advised that mistakes had been made in tabulating the election results and, instead of having lost the election, the candidate had won by 19 votes. The court held that the quo warranto statute, Wis. Stat. § 784.04, challenged the title of a person holding public office. Recount was the candidate's sole remedy when the candidate was informed and believed that the votes were tabulated wrongfully either by irregularity, defect or mistake. Here, the candidate was not litigating whether the counting of the votes was irregular. Rather, he was alleging that the board of canvassers told him he was the actual winner after the canvassing had been completed. The issue was what were the true results of the election. It came down to whether the election officials would testify that indeed the candidate was the winner and whether their testimony was credible. The court reversed and remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order dismissing the candidate's quo warranto action.

State v. Santori


Nos. 92-3030-CR, 92-3031-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 647

NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Washburn county: JAMES H. TAYLOR, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment rendered by the Circuit Court for Washburn County (Wisconsin), which convicted him guilty of first-degree intentional homicide. Defendant claimed that he was improperly convicted and that the trial court should have granted his postconviction motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant filed a postconviction motion for a new trial. The trial court denied the motion. Defendant appealed, claiming that he was improperly convicted. The court held that the trial court did not commit error by excluding evidence allegedly implicating a third person in the murder. The evidence was self-contradictory, uncorroborated, and strongly rebutted. Also, the evidence insufficiently demonstrated that the third person had threatened the victim. Even if the victim had been threatened by the third person, the threat was remote in time to the murder. The court also determined that defendant was not denied effective assistance of counsel because his counsel's decision to not further investigate evidence possessed by others and to not offer witnesses' testimony into evidence was a matter of trial strategy. In addition, the court stated that defendant failed to demonstrate that the trial court's proceeding to sentencing shortly after the jury returned its verdict caused him prejudice. Finally, the court concluded that defendant's telephonic presence at his postconviction hearing met the requirements of due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Millers Nat'l Ins. Co. v. City of Milwaukee


No. 91-2536


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


177 Wis. 2d 573; 503 N.W.2d 284; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 652


January 6, 1993, Submitted on briefs  
June 8, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: Patrick J. Madden, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment and order reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff-appellant insurer challenged a decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) that awarded summary judgment to the City of Milwaukee against its subrogation claim. The insurer asserted that it was entitled to subrogation under Wis. Stat. § 66.189 for payments that it made to the insured, a city employee. The city asserted that § 66.189 unconstitutionally violated the public purpose doctrine.


OVERVIEW: A police officer was struck by an uninsured motorist and received payments from his insurer. The insurer sought subrogation from the officer's employer, the City of Milwaukee, under Wis. Stat. § 66.189. The trial court awarded summary judgment to the city but the court reversed this decision. § 66.189 required the city to provide uninsured motorist coverage for its vehicles and effectively made it an insurer for purposes of uninsured motorist's coverage for its employees that drove city-owned vehicles. In determining whether a contractual right of subrogation existed, courts were required to examine the policy, to interpret it as would a reasonable person in the insured's position, and to give ordinary meaning to its language. The court found that the subrogation clause contained within the insurer's policy gave it a right of subrogation against the city. Further, the court rejected the city's argument that § 66.189 was unconstitutional under the public purpose doctrine, which required public funds to be used for public purposes. The court found that the expenditures required by § 66.189, were justified by public employee concerns over their need for full insurance coverage.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and found that the insurer was entitled to contractual subrogation. The court also found that the disputed statute was constitutional.
