In re Paternity of Jeremy D.L.


No. 92-1899


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


177 Wis. 2d 551; 503 N.W.2d 275; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 638


April 1, 1993, Submitted on briefs  
June 2, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Price county: Gary B. Schlosstein, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and cause remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Price county (Wisconsin) dismissing its paternity action against respondent alleged father entered upon a jury verdict finding that he was not the father of the mother's son.


OVERVIEW: Wisconsin's paternity statutes were comprehensively revised by ch. 352, 1979 Wis. Laws, effective July 1, 1981. Among the revisions, the legislature adopted Wis. Stat. § 767.465(2), which provided that if a respondent was the alleged father and failed to appear at the first appearance scheduled blood test, pretrial hearing or trial, the court must enter an order adjudicating the respondent to be the father and appropriate orders for support, legal custody and physical placement. The trial court denied the State's motion for a default judgment brought pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 767.465(2), when the alleged father failed to personally appear at pretrial proceedings. The court held that even if the statute contemplated a mandatory default in all cases, the provisions of Wis. Stat. § 767.465(3), coupled with the surrounding circumstances rendered any error in denying the default harmless. The State challenged the trial court's decision to try the matter to a jury in view of the alleged father's failure to comply with the provisions of Wis. Stat. § 767.50(1). On appeal, the judgment dismissing the paternity petition was reversed and the matter was remanded for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing the paternity petition was reversed and the matter was remanded to the trial court for a new trial.

Village of Oregon v. Waldofsky


No. 92-0350


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


177 Wis. 2d 412; 501 N.W.2d 912; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 606


February 3, 1993, Submitted on briefs  
May 27, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: Robert R. Pekowsky, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff village issued a citation to defendant charging him with violating a drunk driving ordinance. He was found not guilty in municipal court. The village sought a trial de novo. Defendant challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which denied his motion to dismiss the village's appeal under Wis. Stat. § 800.14(4). Defendant claimed that § 800.14(4) violated his constitutional rights to equal protection.


OVERVIEW: The village appealed to the circuit court under Wis. Stat. § 800.14(4), which allowed a party appealing to the circuit court from municipal court orders to demand a jury trial. Defendant asserted that that § 800.14(4) violated his right to equal protection of the law under the federal and state constitutions because it did not afford him, as a non-appealing party, the same right to demand a jury trial. The court affirmed the trial court's determination. Defendant asserted that appellants and respondents in appeals from municipal court to circuit court were persons similarly situated and thus constituted a single class of persons. He maintained that, by permitting appellants to request a jury trial on appeal, while denying that right to respondents, § 800.14(4) created an irrational classification. The court found that under Wis. Stat. § 800.04(1)(d), persons charged with violating ordinance prohibition drunken driving had a right to a jury trial in circuit court, it they, within 10 days, requested such. Defendant chose not to make such timely request. Further, persons charged with violating municipal ordinances did not have a constitutional right to a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to dismiss the appeal.

Michael L. v. State


No. 92-3103


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


177 Wis. 2d 622; 503 N.W.2d 23; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 614



May 26, 1993, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Winnebago county: THOMAS S. WILLIAMS, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a juvenile, sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court, Winnebago County (Wisconsin), which found the juvenile delinquent for the commission of three acts of party to the crime of possession of an improvised explosive device in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 939.05 and 941.31(2).


OVERVIEW: The juvenile challenged the lower court judgment that found him delinquent for the commission of three acts of party to a crime for possession of an improvised explosive device. The juvenile argued that the term "improvised explosive device" as used in Wis. Stat. § 941.31(2) did not encompass the device he possessed because the bottle with toilet bowl cleaner and aluminum foil did not contain an explosive material and had no means of detonating. The court found that the device was not an "improvised explosive device" because the toilet bowl cleaner, aluminum foil, and hydrogen gas were not "explosive materials" by themselves since the primary or common purpose of each was not to cause an explosion. Although the court determined that the reason for the mixture was to cause a chemical reaction, it had no means of detonating the explosive material and was not an "improvised explosive device" as defined by § 941.31(2).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court judgment that found the juvenile had engaged in delinquent conduct.

 

1332 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Schaefer v. Village Bd. of Potosi


No. 92-2536


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


177 Wis. 2d 287; 501 N.W.2d 901; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 580


December 18, 1992, Submitted on briefs  
May 20, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Grant county: John R. Wagner, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant village board appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Grant County (Wisconsin), which made absolute a writ of mandamus directing the village board to either adopt a resolution initiated by the electors under Wis. Stat. § 9.20 or to submit it to the electors at the next general election.


OVERVIEW: The village board, acting under Wis. Stat. § 61.36, voted to have the Department of Transportation install sidewalks along portions of a highway and widen the highway to allow on-street parking on other portions. The electors, in accordance with Wis. Stat. § 61.36, initiated a resolution and requested that the village board adopt it without alteration or submit it to the electors for their vote. The resolution rescinding the prior decision of the village board to install sidewalks, prohibited the installation of sidewalks from a portion of the highway, and issued directives regarding where parking would and would not be allowed. The village board refused to adopt the resolution or submit it for election. The electors sued for mandamus relief which was granted by the trial court. The court reversed and remanded finding that the proposed resolution would undermine the authority vested in the village board by the legislature under § 61.36. The court held that the proposed resolution impermissible sought to review and repeal existing legislation.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court making absolute a writ of mandamus that directed the village board to either adopt a resolution initiated by the electors or to submit it to the electors at the next general election was reversed.

 

1333 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Steinbach v. Gustafson


No. 92-2162


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


177 Wis. 2d 178; 502 N.W.2d 156; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 544


February 11, 1993, Oral argument  
May 13, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from orders of the circuit court for Dodge county: Andrew P. Bissonnette, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After appellant husband and respondent wife separated, the wife gave birth to a child and entered her surname on the child's birth certificate. The Circuit Court for Dodge County (Wisconsin) granted the parties a divorce and directed that the child's name be changed to the husband's. The circuit court later reopened the judgment, vacated the name change, and denied the husband's motion for reconsideration. The husband sought review.


OVERVIEW: The husband argued that the lower court erred in re-opening the judgment and that Wis. Stat. § 69.14(1)(f)1.b violated his right to equal protection of the law. The court rejected these claims and affirmed the lower court's orders. The court held that the husband was given sufficient notice of the hearing on the wife's motion to re-open the divorce judgment and that his counsel was prepared to proceed, but that the lower court rescheduled the hearing. Thus, there was no showing that the husband was prejudiced. Further, the court held that the wife's motion was timely because the statute granting re-hearings ran from the date of entry of the judgment, not from the date of the trial. The court also held that the lower court did not abuse its discretion in re-opening the judgment. In addition, the court rejected the husband's claim that § 69.14(1)(f)1.b violated constitutional equal protection provisions by granting the custodial parent the right to give a child his or her surname. The court held that § 69.14(1)(f)1.b did not state an unconstitutional preference for the mother because the father could obtain a custody determination prior to a child's birth.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's orders.

State v. Johnson


No. 92-2023-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


177 Wis. 2d 620; 503 N.W.2d 21; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 510



May 4, 1993, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: RUDOLPH T. RANDA, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), denying defendant's post-conviction motion to modify his sentence or to grant him a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two counts of first-degree sexual assault, false imprisonment, and taking hostages. Defendant sought modification of his sentence on the grounds that his sentence was excessive, that there was a change in the parole policy warranting a modification, and that defendant was denied his presentence report. The trial court denied the motion. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion where the sentence was within the sentencing range. In addition, the trial court properly considered the gravity of the offenses, the character of defendant, and the need to protect the public. Second, the court held that because the trial court did not consider the changes in parole in sentencing defendant, any changes did not warrant a modification of sentence. Third, the court held that while defendant that was represented by counsel had a right to view his presentence report, there was no affirmative duty on the trial court to timely deliver to defendant the report or for the trial counsel to share the report. There was no evidence that defendant requested to see a copy of the report, thus, this issue was waived.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

City of La Crosse v. Gilbertson


No. 92-2906-FT


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


176 Wis. 2d 514; 502 N.W.2d 619; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 470



April 22, 1993, Released


NOTICE:   [*1] %60

UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b) , STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for La Crosse county: PETER G. PAPPAS, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin) convicting of her of underage drinking in violation of City of La Crosse Ordinance 20.02(B), and from an order denying her motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged her conviction for underage drinking, arguing that the city ordinance, City of La Crosse Ordinance 20.02(B), was unconstitutional. The trial court initially granted defendant's motion to dismiss on grounds that the ordinance violated her right to equal protection, but later reversed upon reconsideration. Defendant pled no contest to the charge and the circuit court affirmed the municipal court's judgment. The court found that the no contest plea did not constitute a waiver of defendant's challenge to the ordinance's facial validity. However, the court held that the ordinance was constitutional because it was rationally related to the government's objective of reducing alcohol related automobile accidents. The court rejected defendant's argument that adults under the age of 21 were a quasi-suspect class and that therefore the subject ordinance had to satisfy a heightened scrutiny standard of review. The court found that 18 to 20 year old persons prohibited from consuming alcoholic beverages were not a suspect group or one having a fundamental interest in engaging in the activity of drinking.


OUTCOME: The judgment and order were affirmed.

Casteel v. Kolb


No. 92-0519


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


176 Wis. 2d 440; 500 N.W.2d 400; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 476


June 24, 1992, Submitted on briefs  
April 22, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from orders of the circuit court for Dane county: Susan Steingass, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate appealed the orders of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which dismissed the inmate's action against defendants, prison officers and employees, that claimed violations of several federal and state statutes and sought declaratory, injunctive, and monetary relief for alleged violations of due process rights and of state law.


OVERVIEW: The inmate's complaint charged violations in connection with prison disciplinary proceedings. The claims raised under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 were dismissed because the inmate failed to exhaust his state administrative remedies before bringing the action. The complaint, recast as a petition for certiorari review, was dismissed because the hearings and decisions occurred more than six months prior to the date of the original complaint. On appeal, the inmate claimed that he was deprived of a remedy under the 14th Amendment where the postdeprivation remedies provided by the State were inadequate. The court affirmed because the state certiorari proceedings available to inmates for review of prison disciplinary proceedings were both suitable and meaningful where judicial review included determination of whether the committee followed its own rules governing the conduct of its hearings. Further, the trial court did not err when it dismissed the claims brought under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. Finally, the inmate failed to avail himself of the exclusive remedy under Wis. Stat. § 227.40(1) for judicial review of the validity of the rules nor did he allege that any single rule was invalid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's orders.

Szarzynski v. YMCA, Camp Minikani


No. 92-0089


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


176 Wis. 2d 365; 500 N.W.2d 391; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 463


March 2, 1993, Oral argument  
April 20, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: Patricia D. McMahon, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which dismissed a personal injury action against defendant organization.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs filed an action compensation for personal injuries suffered when a child was injured while attending camp. The trial court dismissed the action on the ground that the organization was a "nonprofit organization," as that term was used by Wis. Stat. § 895.52, and, accordingly, was immune from suit. The court concluded that, so applied, § 895.52 violated the equal-protection clauses of the United States and Wisconsin constitutions. There was no rational basis for the classification that was germane to the statute's "articulated rationale." The legislature's purpose to protect property owners who did not derive more than a minimal pecuniary benefit" from the recreational use of their property so as to open their land for recreational use was not advanced by carving out specific protection for the benefit of those landowners that are structured as "nonprofit organizations." The interest that was advanced, namely, protecting those landowners structured as "nonprofit organizations," even though they might derive significant "pecuniary benefit" from the property, had nothing to do with the statute's "articulated rationale.


OUTCOME: The order of the lower court dismissing plaintiffs' personal injury suit against the organization was reversed.

Martin v. Richards


No. 91-0016


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


176 Wis. 2d 339; 500 N.W.2d 691; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 440


March 12, 1992, Oral argument  
April 15, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petitions to review granted. Petitions to review granted. Petitions to review granted. Petitions to review granted.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Jefferson county: Arnold K. Schumann, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, victim and parents, filed a medical malpractice action against defendants, hospital, emergency room doctor, and on-call doctor. The jury awarded damages against the emergency room doctor, but on motions after verdict, the Circuit Court for Jefferson County (Wisconsin) dismissed the complaint as to all defendants. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim suffered a head injury, was diagnosed by the emergency room doctor with a concussion, and was admitted by the on-call doctor to the hospital for observation. The victim then suffered an epidural hematoma resulting from intracranial bleeding and was transferred to another facility for emergency surgery, which was only partly successful. The trial court found that neither doctor was negligent in his care and treatment of the victim, but that the emergency room doctor was negligent in failing to inform the parents about alternative modes of treatment as required by Wis. Stat. § 448.30. The court held that the special verdict was defective because the evidence presented a question for the jury as to whether the doctors' failure to inform was a cause of the victim's injuries. The court also held that the doctors had a statutory duty to inform the parents that a CAT scan of the victim's brain could have been performed to rule out intracranial bleeding and that the hospital could not perform the requisite surgery if the victim suffered such bleeding.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the part of the judgment that dismissed plaintiffs' medical malpractice action as to the hospital and the part that determined plaintiffs' damages. The court reversed the part of the judgment that dismissed the emergency room doctor and the on-call doctor, and remanded the cause for a new trial as to their liability.

State v. Schambow


No. 92-1769-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


176 Wis. 2d 286; 500 N.W.2d 362; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 427


December 18, 1992, Submitted on briefs  
April 14, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Fond du Lac county: Steven W. Weinke, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Fond du Lac County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of first-degree intentional homicide and first-degree sexual assault and denied his motion for postconviction relief. Defendant contended that his Miranda rights were violated when the police took his statements, that a sexual assault jury instruction was improper, and that he was denied effective assistance of counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his wife were found in the desert. She was dead, and he was hospitalized because he had ingested a poisonous fluid. The police questioned him, thinking that he was a victim. He was eventually charged with and convicted of sexually assaulting and murdering his wife. On appeal, the court held that the police were not required to give defendant his Miranda warnings at the hospital because he was not under arrest or otherwise deprived of his freedom. The court concluded that his statements were voluntary because the questioning in the hospital was not custodial, and the police were not coercive. A jury instruction stating that great bodily harm caused by defendant during the course of conduct immediately preceding or following the act of nonconsensual intercourse was sufficient to find him guilty of first degree sexual assault was proper because, in interpreting the statute, the court determined that the sexual act itself did not have to have caused the great bodily harm. The court found that defendant was not denied effective assistance of counsel because he chose to testify, and his trial counsel did not advise him to testify to three different versions of his story.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for first-degree intentional homicide and first-degree sexual assault and the order denying postconviction relief.

City of Sheboygan v. Hou-Seye


Nos. 92-1545, 92-1546, 92-1547, 92-1548, 92-1549


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 405



April 7, 1993, Released [*1] 


NOTICE: UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Sheboygan county: L. EDWARD STENGEL, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Sheboygan County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of five counts of storing abandoned vehicles on private property, contrary to Sheboygan, Wis., Municipal Code, § 38-231(a), and imposed a forfeiture of $ 150 per citation and costs for the City. The trial court ordered attorney's fees for the City as a cost of prosecution and a jail sentence if defendant did not pay the forfeiture judgment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was the chief executive officer of a church that owned the property where the vehicles were illegally stored. He claimed that the seizure of the vehicles was unreasonable and violated due process. The court rejected the claims because the seizure was not a necessary element of the offenses, and the forfeiture judgment imposed fines for abandonment, not for the costs of seizure and impoundment. In regard to defendant's claim that the trial court was not impartial, the court concluded that the trial court gave defendant his day in court with patience, courtesy, and restraint. In the court's view, it was not significant that defendant was not the property owner because the ordinance designated the offender as the person who abandoned the vehicles. The court held that the church did not qualify for exemptions in Sheboygan, Wis., Municipal Code, § 38-231.1(a)-(c). Further, the trial court's imposition of an alternative jail sentence if defendant failed to pay the forfeiture judgment did not violate the state or federal constitutions. However, the award of attorney's fees was improper because they were not "costs of prosecution" under Sheboygan, Wis., Municipal Code § 38.236.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions and forfeiture judgment of the trial court, but reversed the award of actual attorney's fees to the City.

State v. Kraus


Nos. 92-2451-CR and 92-2452-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


175 Wis. 2d 626; 502 N.W.2d 284; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 380



March 30, 1993, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgments of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: ROBERT C. CANNON, Reserve Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant of unlawful use of a telephone as a habitual criminal, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 947.012(5), Wis. Stat. § 939.62(1)(a), and of bail jumping as a habitual criminal, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 946.049(1)(a) and Wis. Stat. § 939.62(1)(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted, following a jury trial, of more than 15 counts of unlawful use of a telephone as a habitual criminal and of bail jumping as a habitual criminal. The allegations stemmed from numerous hang-up telephone calls made to the residences of several of the county district attorney's staff. On appeal, defendant admitted placing the telephone calls but argued that he lacked the intent to "harass" anyone at the called numbers and claimed that he was denied due process of law because he had been found guilty of violating an unconstitutionally vague statute. The court held that the word "harass" was not vague and that, as a matter of law, a person of ordinary intelligence would be able to determine that repeatedly calling a telephone number and hanging up in the early morning hours was conduct that Wis. Stat. § 947.012(5) prohibited. The court stressed that the wording of the statute placed a person of ordinary intelligence on notice of such prohibited behavior.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

State ex rel. Sandra D. v. Getto


Nos. 92-1105, 92-1862


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


175 Wis. 2d 490; 498 N.W.2d 892; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 354


November 24, 1992, Submitted on briefs  
March 25, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: Jack F. Aulik, Judge.

Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: Angela Bartell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Orders reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient appealed from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) a protective placement order and an order denying her petition for a writ of habeas corpus. The dispositive issue raised on appeal was whether the trial court lacked competency to proceed with a final hearing on respondent county's petition for protective placement after expiration of the 30-day limitation in Wis. Stat. § 55.06(11)(c).


OVERVIEW: Two prior protective placement proceedings instituted against the patient were dismissed because the physicians failed to deliver their reports to the patient's counsel. After such dismissals, the physicians filed statements of emergency detention, which had the effect of continuing the patient's detention. There was no question that the patient was detained without a final hearing far in excess of the 14-day requirement Wis. Stat. § 51.20(8)(bm) and the 30-day requirement of Wis. Stat. § 55.06(11)(c). The county contended the court should disregard its failure to meet the statutory time limits because: (1) the physicians' delays were beyond the county's control; and (2) the patient needed to be in protective placement during all the time she was detained. The court found that even though no specific statutory language prohibited successive reinstatement of dismissed petitions, the constitution required that a line be drawn. Under the circumstances presented, the court concluded that the patient's continued temporary detention denied her due process of law. Therefore, the patient's motion to dismiss the third proceeding with prejudice should have been granted.


OUTCOME: The protective placement order and the order denying the patient's petition for a writ of habeas corpus were reversed.

 

1343 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Lange v. Lange


No. 91-0133


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


175 Wis. 2d 373; 502 N.W.2d 143; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 315


February 5, 1992, Submitted on briefs  
March 18, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review filed.
Review denied by Lange v. Lange, 505 N.W.2d 137, 1993 Wisc. LEXIS 573 (Wis., 1993)
Writ of certiorari denied Lange v. Lange, 511 U.S. 1025, 114 S. Ct. 1416, 128 L. Ed. 2d 86, 1994 U.S. LEXIS 2796 (1994)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Clark County: Michael W. Brennan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.E


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent father sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Clark County (Wisconsin), which awarded mother the legal custody of the parties' three minor children and further provided that respondent father was awarded reasonable visitation supervised by a proper person approved by county, yet the court could remove the restriction if father discontinued the imposition of his fundamentalist religious views on the children.


OVERVIEW: Respondent father and petitioner mother's divorce decree awarded to her the legal custody of the parties' minor children, and father was awarded supervised visitation. The restriction on father's visitation could be removed if he would not impose his fundamentalist religious views on the children. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the restriction was valid. The court reasoned that the restriction was limited in scope and duration because father was allowed to discuss religion with the children so long as he did not cross into causing them to reject mother's religion. The restriction lasted until father stopped imposing his religious views on the children. The court found that limiting father's religious conduct was not the object of the restriction, but it was the incidental effect of securing mother's right under a valid law to choose the children's religion. The court concluded that the visitation restriction did not violate father's rights to the free exercise of his religion. Wis. Stat. § 767.001(2m) gave mother, the custodial parent, the choice of religion for the children, and provided her with protection from subversion of her choice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court holding that the trial court had not unnecessarily abridged father's rights and freedom of religion by the visitation restriction. The custody statute had given mother the choice of religion for the children, and it provided mother with protection from subversion of her choice.

State v. Chapman


No. 92-1148-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


175 Wis. 2d 231; 499 N.W.2d 222; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 287


December 8, 1992, Oral argument  
March 10, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Washington County: Richard T. Becker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Washington County (Wisconsin) that convicted him of first-degree intentional homicide. Defendant also sought postconviction relief, which was denied. An issue presented on appeal was whether or not defendant was denied a constitutional right to presentence confinement credit.


OVERVIEW: The case involved defendant's admitted burial of his baby in dirt outdoors. Experts stated that he was buried alive. Where defendant was sentenced to life imprisonment, under Wis. Stat. § 973.014, the trial court could use Wis. Stat. § 973.014(1), which set the minimum amount of prison time before parole eligibility, or use Wis. Stat. § 973.014(2) and judicially set a parole-eligibility date that was consistent with the case's circumstances. The court held that the heinousness of first-degree intentional homicide was a rational basis for making parole for those convicted of it different from that for those convicted of crimes that did not have a penalty of mandatory life imprisonment. The court also held that the circumstances of each case and each defendant supplied a rational basis for the two options given by § 973.014; either repeated criminal behavior or a particularly gruesome crime was a rational basis for setting a parole-eligibility date without the benefit of the formula of § 973.014(1). The court also ruled, inter alia, that the trial court did not make an error by refusing to submit a jury instruction on the lesser-included offense of second-degree reckless homicide.


OUTCOME: Ruling against defendant, the court affirmed the judgment and order of the trial court.

State v. Wooten


No. 91-2824-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


177 Wis. 2d 619; 503 N.W.2d 21; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 249



March 9, 1993, Released


NOTICE: UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: JANINE P. GESKE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) that convicted him of second-degree sexual assault of a child under Wis. Stat. § 948.02(2). Defendant contested the finding of insufficiency under the rape shield law, Wis. Stat. 972.11(2)(b), as to his offer of proof pertaining to alternative semen source evidence, alleging violation of U.S. Const. amend. VI.


OVERVIEW: The victim testified that defendant, the boyfriend of the cousin with whom the victim lived, raped the victim. About 12 hours after the rape, the victim was medically examined. Tests did not identify the source of the semen, but did find that the semen had been deposited within 72 hours. Under Wis. Stat. §§ 971.31(11), 972.11(2)(b), defendant sought to introduce evidence that the victim had intercourse with the victim's boyfriend through the cousin's testimony of what the victim had told the cousin. The victim testified during that she had not had intercourse with anyone the week before the rape. The court affirmed the judgment. What defendant offered to show questioned only the source of the semen, rather than the degree of the offense. Consequently, exclusion was proper under Wis. Stat. § 971.11(2)(b)2. Because defendant's proposed evidence addressed the victim's prior sexual encounters, it did not come within the § 972.11(2)(b)2 exception for determining the offense's degree or the amount of harm suffered. The testimony of the cousin and the victim's boyfriend showed that the intercourse between the victim and the victim's boyfriend did not arise within 72 hours of the rape.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of second-degree sexual assault of a child.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of masked armed robbery as a party to the crime. Defendant also appealed from an order denying his motion for postconviction relief.

EVERS v. UTSCHIG


No. 92-2144


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


175 Wis. 2d 625; 502 N.W.2d 284; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 235



March 2, 1993, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Outagamie county: TIMOTHY L. VOCKE, Reserve Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff criminal defendant challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Outagamie County (Wisconsin), which granted the motion to dismiss that the court reporter filed in the criminal defendant's action that alleged that the reporter and the trial judge who presided over the criminal trial conspired to have the criminal defendant convicted to allow the reporter to gain from preparing the trial transcripts for the appellate proceeding.


OVERVIEW: The criminal defendant alleged error as to concluding that the reporter had absolute immunity and that the complaint did not state a claim under either 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 or 42 U.S.C.S. § 1985. The court affirmed the dismissal, concluding that the criminal defendant's claims lacked merit. The court reasoned that the reporter's position as a court officer gave her absolute immunity as to the conduct of her official duties and that the complaint only alleged misconduct in the reporter's discharge of her court duties, noting that only her official position allowed her to profit or to participate in preparing the transcripts and that none of the criminal defendant's allegations related to the reporter outside of her official role. The court also held that the extension of the doctrine of judicial immunity to court reporters in the discharge of their duties showed that the civil rights complaint did not state a claim on which relief could have been granted and determined that the general allegations of a conspiracy and of malicious intent fell far short of pleading events that supported an inference of a civil rights violation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of the reporter's motion to dismiss the criminal defendant's civil rights action.

 

1348 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Johnny G. v. State


No. 92-1818


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


173 Wis. 2d 909; 499 N.W.2d 301; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 79



 January 26, 1993, Released


NOTICE: UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: RUSSELL W. STAMPER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin). The trial court denied appellant's motion for adjournment and committed appellant to the custody of the Division of Youth Services until his 21st birthday, after appellant entered a Alford plea to the charge of first-degree reckless homicide and endangering safety by use of a dangerous weapon.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with first-degree intentional homicide as a party to a crime, endangering safety by use of a dangerous weapon, and endangering safety while armed. After the juvenile court refused to waive its jurisdiction, the State amended the first charge to first-degree reckless homicide, and appellant entered an Alford plea on that charge, admitted to the facts underlying the second charge, and the third charge was dismissed. The court affirmed. After determining that residential treatment of appellant was inappropriate, the decision not to adjourn was well within the ambit of the juvenile court's discretion. Although Wis. Stat. § 48.01(2) required that the best interest of the child was always of paramount consideration, the juvenile court could also look at the public interest when determining confinement. Appellant was not denied due process for the juvenile court's failure to affirmatively offer an opportunity for allocution prior to disposition, as there was no statute analogous to Wis. Stat. § 972.14 or Fed. R. Crim. P. 32(a) that required such an affirmative opportunity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the juvenile court.

 

1349 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Dixon v. J.C. Penney Co.


No. 91-2794


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


173 Wis. 2d 907; 499 N.W.2d 300; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 84



January 26, 1993, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: FRANCIS T. WASIELEWSKI, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff customer brought an action against defendant retailer, seeking damages arising from a bee sting. Subsequently, the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) entered judgment, upon a jury verdict, in favor of the retailer and awarded the retailer costs and disbursements. The customer appealed and the retailer filed a motion seeking costs for a frivolous appeal pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 809.25(3)(c).


OVERVIEW: After she was allegedly stung by a bee in the retailer's outlet store, the customer filed the action against the retailer in small claims court. Following the denial of the customer's motions for a default judgment and contempt of court, the matter proceeded to trial. On appeal, the customer asserted Wis. Stat. § 799.06(2), allowing a corporation to appear in a small claims action via an employee was an unconstitutional legislative invasion of judicial power. In a related assertion, she contended the trial court erred in denying her motion for default judgment and contempt of court. The customer also argued the evidence was insufficient to support the jury verdict and the trial court improperly awarded costs to the retailer. The court affirmed the judgment because the customer did not meet the proper burden of proof demonstrating § 799.06(2) was unconstitutional, the trial court did not misuse its discretion in denying a default judgment and not finding the retailer in contempt of court, the evidence was sufficient to support the jury verdict, and the award of costs to the retailer was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment entered in favor of the retailer in the action brought by the customer. In addition, the court denied the retailer's motion for costs on appeal.

 

1350 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Harris


Nos. 92-0828-CR, 92-0829-CR, 92-0830-CR, 92-0831-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


174 Wis. 2d 367; 497 N.W.2d 742; 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 90



January 26, 1993, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from judgments and orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: JANINE P. GESKE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from judgments of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) that convicted him of two armed robberies, an attempted first-degree homicide as a party to a crime, attempted escape, assault by a prisoner, and battery by a prisoner as a party to a crime. The trial court also made orders that denied postconviction relief, from which orders defendant also appealed.


OVERVIEW: After he was adjudicated guilty regarding the robbery and attempted homicide charges, he was incarcerated pending sentencing, and he then attempted to escape. Defendant argued that the trial court was without jurisdiction regarding the escape-related charges as there was an alleged unreasonable delay between his arrest and his initial appearance on those charges. In favor of his delay argument, defendant cited Wis. Stat. § 970.01, Wis. Const. art. 1, § 8, and the U.S. Const. amends. IV, XIV. The court disagreed. It was dispositive that defendant was in the State's lawful custody before, during, and after the attempted escape and that therefore he was not detained as a result of any arrest for the escape-related charges. The court held that without either prejudice or other unforeseen circumstances, the time between an "arrest" and an initial appearance was never unreasonable where the arrestee was already in the lawful physical custody of the State. The court also determined that defendant had not shown a new factor that justified a sentencing modification.


OUTCOME: Ruling against defendant, the court affirmed the judgments and orders of the trial court.

 

1351 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jankowski


No. 92-1935-CR-FT


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


173 Wis. 2d 522; 496 N.W.2d 215; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 746


December 18, 1992, Submitted on briefs  
December 30, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the circuit Court for Waukesha County: Kathryn W. Foster, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of violating an extension of a domestic abuse injunction.


OVERVIEW: In 1987, defendant's former wife obtained a two-year domestic abuse injunction prohibiting defendant from having contact with her. First entered on June 10, 1987, the injunction was to last through June 9, 1989. On June 7, 1989, the former wife petitioned to have the injunction extended for an additional two years. The request was supported with a verified petition and documents alleging continued harassment and domestic abuse. An extension was granted to last through June 8, 1991. Defendant did not challenge the extension. Defendant was charged with three violations of the extended injunction. He filed a motion to dismiss the charges, alleging that the extended injunction was invalid because Wis. Stat. § 813.12(4) did not permit any injunction to exceed two years in length. The trial court denied the motion and found defendant guilty of the violation. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded with directions to dismiss, holding that § 813.12(4) was unambiguous and that the total injunction period could not exceed two years, including extensions. The court held that because the extended injunction was a nullity, it could not serve as the basis for a criminal conviction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the conviction and remanded with directions to grant defendant's motion to dismiss.

State v. Ridderbush


No. 92-0202


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


173 Wis. 2d 305; 498 N.W.2d 912; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 921



December 15, 1992, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Brown county: DONALD HANAWAY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction, in accordance with a jury verdict, in the Circuit Court for Brown County (Wisconsin) on a charge of unauthorized practice of law, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 757.30(2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant provided bankruptcy forms, advised persons how to fill out the forms, and charged $ 125 for his services. Defendant was charged with practicing law without a license. The trial court denied his motion to dismiss based on his contention that Wis. Stat. § 757.30(2) was unconstitutional. A jury convicted defendant. As a condition of probation, defendant had to comply with the bankruptcy court's order to provide an accounting of his bankruptcy filings and fees. Defendant's motions for habeas corpus relief and to extend time to file his notice of intent to pursue post-conviction relief were denied, as was a subsequent motion to vacate his sentence. The court affirmed the judgment and held that a motion to vacate under Wis. Stat. § 974.06 could not have been used as a substitute for a direct appeal nor to have extended the time for appeals. He should have appealed directly from the judgment and sentence. Further, the probation conditions did not violate defendant's self-incrimination privilege because the Fifth Amendment did not protect a corporation or its custodian against self-incrimination through compulsory production of corporate records.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for the unauthorized practice of law.

 

1353 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Stephenson


No. 92-0238


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


173 Wis. 2d 305; 498 N.W.2d 913; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 947



December 15, 1992, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: RUDOLPH T. RANDA, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate, convicted of one count of first-degree murder and two counts of endangering safety by conduct regardless of life, sought review of the order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) denying his motion for postconviction relief pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 974.06.


OVERVIEW: In a prior motion for postconviction relief, the inmate had unsuccessfully claimed ineffectiveness of counsel. In denying the inmate's motion for relief pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 974.06, the trial court found that there was no inconsistency between the charges and the verdicts and that the inmate was not denied a fair trial. On review, the court held that the inmate had waived his claims that his convictions were inconsistent and constitutionally defective by failing to raise them before the trial court as required by Wis. Stat. § 971.31(2). The inmate failed to present to the trial court his claim that his mental health history should have been admitted at trial as required under Wis. Stat. § 974.06(1); moreover, there was nothing in the record suggesting that the inmate had attempted to introduce his mental health history at trial. The inmate's claim that the denial of his request for a self-defense jury instruction was error was not cognizable within the context of a § 974.06 motion. The inmate also waived his right to raise his claim of error in the admission of statements that he made to third parties during the commission of the crimes by failing to raise the issue below.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the inmate's motion for postconviction relief.

State v. Chambers


No. 91-2948-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


173 Wis. 2d 237; 496 N.W.2d 191; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 905


August 13, 1992, Submitted on briefs  
December 15, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review dismissed.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: Rudolph T. Randa, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, citing U.S. Const. amends. V, VI, XIV, Wis. Const. art. I, §§ 7, 8, Wis. Stat. § 904.04(2), appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) convicting and sentencing him on three counts of first-degree sexual assault, party to a crime, in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 940.225(1)(c), 939.05.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended on appeal that the evidence was insufficient, that the information was duplicitous, that the trial court abused its discretion in permitting the victim to testify to sex acts in addition to those charged, and that multiplicity in charging violated his right against double jeopardy. The court affirmed the judgment. The court determined that the evidence presented to the jury was sufficient to support each conviction and all modes of proof. The court concluded that because defendant had actual notice of the charges and his defense was not at all based upon the distinctions among various acts, he was able to adequately plead and prepare a defense. The court found that there was no support for defendant's claim of duplicity. The court determined that admission of all evidence of the attacks by defendant and his brother against the victim at the time and place of the crime was not improper or prejudicial and did not affect the unanimity of the verdict. The court stated that even if the original charges were multiplicitous, the final verdict and subsequent punishment did not violate defendant's right to be free of multiple punishments for the same offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court convicting and sentencing defendant for first-degree sexual assault.

 

1355 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rogers


No. 91-2606


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


173 Wis. 2d 305; 498 N.W.2d 912; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 915



December 8, 1992, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: MICHAEL J. SKWIERAWSKI, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed a decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which denied his motion for postconviction relief under Wis. Stat. § 974.06 brought 16 years after he was convicted as party-to-a-crime of first-degree murder and four counts of armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted. He filed an appeal and then 16 years later filed a motion for post conviction relief. The circuit court denied the motion and petitioner appealed. The court affirmed, in part. The court held that because petitioner received the statutory maximum sentence for each robbery conviction, the circuit court properly utilized the enhancer statute, Wis. Stat. § 939.641, to increase his sentence beyond the statutory maximum. The imposition of consecutive sentences was not a condition to the application of an enhancer statute. Petitioner's argument that the jury instruction on party-to-a-crime liability, Wis. Jury Instructions Crim. No. 400, improperly created a presumption of guilt was without merit because it simply provided that all parties to a crime were legally accountable. The court then found that petitioner had alleged sufficient facts that may have entitled him to an evidentiary hearing on the issue of ineffective assistance to trial counsel, but remanded for a determination as to whether the delay in bringing the motion was reasonable, as required by the doctrine of laches, and if so, whether the State had been prejudiced by the delay.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, finding that the circuit court properly enhanced petitioner's sentence, that the party-to-a-crime instruction did not create a presumption of guilt, and that petitioner was barred from challenging an instruction. The court remanded for a determination of whether laches barred petitioner's ineffective assistance of counsel claim.

State v. Daniels


No. 92-1930


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


173 Wis. 2d 308; 498 N.W.2d 914; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1122



December 2, 1992, Released


NOTICE: UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waukesha county: KATHRYN W. FOSTER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the circuit court for Waukesha county (Wisconsin) for operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated. Defendant contended that the evidence of his primary blood test result should have been suppressed in the trial court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's motion to suppress evidence of his primary blood test result was denied and he was convicted. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court reviewed defendant's constitutional challenges despite an inadequate record. The court held that defendant's opportunity to exercise his due process right to any additional tests under the implied consent law was not compromised because the Informing the Accused form used to inform defendant under the implied consent law was not misleading or incorrect and did not functionally tell defendant that an additional test would be futile. The court also held that the trial court's interpretation of the evidence in concluding that defendant did not request an alternate test was not clearly erroneous or otherwise wrong.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction of defendant.

State v. Jennerjahn


No. 92-1235-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


172 Wis. 2d 573; 495 N.W.2d 526; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 985



November 25, 1992, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b) , STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Winnebago county: WILLIAM E. CRANE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Winnebago County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of one count of misdemeanor theft, and four counts of different degrees of sexual assault, and from an order of the same court denying him postconviction relief. Defendant claimed that the trial court erred by precluding him from producing evidence of the victim's experience with counseling for rape or sexual abuse.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sexually assaulted the victim, a wheelchair-bound woman, on a number of occasions. The trial court granted the State's pretrial motion in limine and excluded evidence that the victim previously made a criminal complaint alleging sexual assault by a neighbor, and that the victim had previously availed herself of counseling services for rape victims. The court affirmed defendant's conviction on charges of theft and multiple sexual assaults. The evidence of the victim's prior sexual experiences was clearly barred by the rape-shield statute, Wis. Stat. § 972.11(2)(b), and evidence that the victim had received rape counseling services was inadmissible because it inevitably would lead to testimony about previous sexual conduct, which also would violate § 972.11(2)(b). The court found defendant's argument that the victim misleadingly tried to portray herself as a helpless victim who consented to the assault because she did not say "no" offensive and without basis in law.


OUTCOME: The judgment and order were affirmed.

 

1358 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Amos


Nos. 91-1926, 91-1927


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


172 Wis. 2d 571; 495 N.W.2d 525; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 884



November 12, 1992, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b) , STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: GERALD C. NICHOL, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) that denied his motion made pro se for postconviction relief under Wis. Stat. § 974.06. In sentencing defendant as an adult for burglary and escape, the trial court mentioned defendant's extensive juvenile record, and defendant argued on appeal that it was error to consider his juvenile record.


OVERVIEW: A conviction procured with a violation of the right to counsel could not be used permissibly against a person either to substantiate guilt or to increase punishment for another offense. Defendant contended that his prior juvenile adjudications were imposed when he had no counsel. Where defendant was not represented by counsel at a juvenile proceeding, the adjudication could not be considered at a later adult-sentencing proceeding. The court decided that this rule did not apply to the case sub judice because per the court the trial court's explanation of the sentence for burglary did not reveal any reliance on defendant's juvenile record. The passing mention of a juvenile record did not violate the rule. The court found that the trial court stated that it considered five factors to make its sentencing determination, and the court found that each factor was an appropriate consideration. The court ruled that there was no abuse of discretion in the sentencing of defendant.


OUTCOME: Ruling against defendant, the court affirmed the trial court's order.

State v. Steed


No. 92-0500-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


172 Wis. 2d 572; 495 N.W.2d 526; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 949



November 10, 1992, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: FRANK T. CRIVELLO, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), convicting defendant of felony murder, kidnapping, and bail-jumping following defendant's guilty pleas. Defendant also appealed the denial of his post-conviction motion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction for felony murder, kidnapping, and bail-jumping all stem from incidents surrounding defendant's ex-girlfriend and her sister who intervened and was killed in the process. Defendant appealed his conviction, alleging that the trial court erred by joining the several charges together for trial. The court affirmed. The court held that it was well established that a plea of guilty, knowingly and understandingly made, constituted a waiver of nonjurisdictional defects and defenses, including claimed violations of constitutional rights. The court noted that defendant voluntarily waived his defenses when he entered his guilty plea. Defendant understood the plea questionnaire and was fully informed by the trial court of all consequences of entering a guilty plea. The court further held that departure from the waiver rule was not appropriate because defendant was aware of his defenses regarding the consolidation. There was no manifest injustice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Wielebski v. Ice Age Park & Trial Foundation


No. 92-0242


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


172 Wis. 2d 572; 495 N.W.2d 525; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1157

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin) that granted summary judgment in favor of defendant foundation in the property owners' action to discontinue the construction of a scenic hiking trail in the subdivision in which their residence was located.


OVERVIEW: The foundation purchased three lots in the subdivision where the property owners lived, and it began marking and building a historic scenic trail to run through the subdivision. 1361 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


River Falls v. Marcyan


No. 92-1202


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


171 Wis. 2d 349; 493 N.W.2d 272; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1257



September 29, 1992, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Pierce county: ROBERT W. WING, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Pierce County (Wisconsin), convicting him of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated (OWI) in violation of River Falls, Wis., Ordinance No. 7, adopting Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a)-(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a Minnesota resident who worked in Wisconsin, contended that Wis. Stat. § 343.10(2), which permitted only Wisconsin residents to obtain an occupational license after suspension of their operator's license for OWI, violated the privileges and immunities clause of U.S. Const. art. IV, § 2, cl. 1 and the equal protection and due process clauses of U.S. Const. amends. V, XIV and Wis. Const. art. I, § 1. On review, the court held that River Falls, Wis., Ordinance No. 7, adopting the Wisconsin OWI statutes, was constitutional. Operating a motor vehicle upon public highways was not a fundamental or inherent property right but was in the nature of a license or privilege and thus the denial of the right to apply for a Wisconsin occupational license to a nonresident person whose operating privileges were properly revoked did not violate the privileges and immunities clause or defendant's due process rights. Further, defendant's equal protection rights were not affected because there was a rational basis for creating different classifications between Wisconsin residents and nonresidents as to who might apply for an occupational license after suspension.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

State ex rel. Roberta A. S. v. Waukesha County Human Services Dep't


No. 92-1397


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


171 Wis. 2d 266; 491 N.W.2d 114; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 590


August 5, 1992, Submitted on briefs  
September 23, 1992, Decided  
September 23, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Waukesha county: J. Mac Davis, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ward sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin) that authorized the forcible administration of the approved medications to the ward and the forcible detention of the ward as necessary to administer the psychotropic medication by respondent guardian.


OVERVIEW: At issue on appeal was whether, under Wis. Stat. §§ 55, 880, a guardian appointed for consenting to or refusing psychotropic medications had the power to forcibly detain the ward or to forcibly enter her premises to administer the medications. The ward asserted that the trial court lacked the statutory authority to order forcible entry onto her premises for the purpose of detaining her and forcibly administering psychotropic medications. She also claimed that the order unconstitutionally deprived her of her liberty without due process of law. In reversing, the court held that administration of medication against the will of an individual could only be ordered through a Wis. Stat. § 51 proceeding, even if that individual was incompetent to refuse medication. Accordingly, the court found that the trial court's order exceeded statutory authority and offended due process.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded with directions the order from the trial court.

 

1363 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Zoellick


No. 92-0955-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


171 Wis. 2d 348; 493 N.W.2d 271; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1225



September 17, 1992, Released


NOTICE: UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Jefferson county: ARNOLD SCHUMANN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Jefferson County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant, following his plea of no contest to three counts of violating a harassment injunction, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 813.125(7). Defendant also appealed the trial court's order denying his motion to withdraw his no contest pleas.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed the trial court's entry of a judgment of conviction against him and the trial court's denial of his motion to withdraw his pleas of no contest. Defendant argued that his pleas were not knowing and intelligent. The court found that at the post-conviction motion hearing, defendant testified that he had always wanted to appeal the order denying his motion to dismiss, he did not discuss with his trial counsel the effect a no contest plea would have on the appealability of that order, and that he assumed he could appeal despite his no contest pleas. Notwithstanding defendant's testimony and the facts tending to corroborate his claim, the trial court simply did not believe him. The trial court inferred that defendant wanted to withdraw his plea because he was dissatisfied with the sentence. Defendant thought time served was appropriate for what he was accused of doing and questioned whether a four year sentence was justified. Thus, the trial court reasonably inferred that defendant was pursuing a motion to withdraw because of dissatisfaction with the sentence and that he had pleaded no contest knowing that he was surrendering his right to appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1364 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. De Leon


No. 92-0636-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


171 Wis. 2d 200; 490 N.W.2d 767; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 584


July 3, 1992, Submitted on briefs  
September 16, 1992, Decided  
September 16, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Winnebago county: Robert A. Haase, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; order reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Winnebago County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant of conspiring to possess with intent to deliver more than 25 grams of cocaine, withheld sentence, and ordered defendant to serve a four-year term of probation with a six-month jail confinement and work release privileges.


OVERVIEW: The State appealed the judgment and order of the trial court, arguing that the structure of the probation order was contrary to Wis. Stat. §§ 161.41(1m)(c)3 and 973.09(1)(d). The court held that defendant violated Wis. Stat. § 161.41(1x), thus subjecting her to the mandatory minimum penalties described in Wis. Stat. § 161.41(1m)(c)3. Read together, Wis. Stat. § 161.438 and Wis. Stat. 973.09(1)(d) exposed defendant to a presumptive minimum sentence of one year in prison and a $ 1000 fine. The trial court, however, had withheld defendant's sentence and ordered four years probation and only six months in the county jail with work release privileges, which was a term of confinement clearly less than the minimum one year. Wis. Stat. § 973.09(1)(d) plainly required that when probation was deemed appropriate, the trial court also had to order confinement for at least that mandatory or presumptive minimum period. The statutory scheme was not absurd, vague, or arbitrary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction in the trial court. The court reversed the trial court's sentence of defendant and remanded the matter for resentencing according to the statutes.

State v. Smith


No. 92-0458-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


170 Wis. 2d 701; 490 N.W.2d 40; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 550


June 30, 1992, Submitted on briefs  
August 26, 1992, Decided  
August 26, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Fond du Lac county: John W. Mickiewicz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his convictions for arson and first-degree reckless endangerment in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 943.02(1)(a) and 941.30(1) entered by the Circuit Court for Fond Du Lac County (Wisconsin). Defendant also appealed from an order denying his motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: A fire occurred at a 12-unit apartment building where defendant lived. An accomplice, who was granted use immunity in return for testimony, implicated defendant as responsible for the fire. The accomplice first denied involvement in the fire and later changed his story and testified that on the day of the fire, defendant gave him the only key to the back door of the basement and instructed him to unlock the door. The accomplice further testified that defendant directed him to act as a lookout by watching the basement doors and that, shortly thereafter, he heard sounds similar to the pouring of a liquid and the striking of a match in the front area of the basement where defendant was standing. He also testified that defendant's motive for starting the fire was that defendant did not like a certain tenant. There was no physical evidence of the arson. The court held that the definition of intent under Wis. Stat. § 939.23(3) (1987) was neither vague nor a violation of defendant's due process rights. Additionally, the court found that testimony from a police officer about accomplice's interrogation was not an improper opinion as to the accomplice's truthfulness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and the order.

State ex rel. Brown County v. Hanaway


No. 91-2089


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


170 Wis. 2d 343; 492 N.W.2d 187; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1030



July 30, 1992, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b) , STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: MICHAEL B. TORPHY, JR., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff counties appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which dismissed their complaint against State for failure to state a claim upon which relief can be granted. Their complaint sought payment of claims for reimbursement of court costs honored under former Wis. Stat. § 814.25, which were left unpaid when the statute was repealed.


OVERVIEW: Wis. Stat. § 3202(34)(c) provided that the treatment of Wis. Stat. § 814.25 of the statutes first applied to certificates of repayments unpaid by the state treasurer on the effective date of the new statute. The court found that the language was unambiguous. The legislature intended to leave the counties' pending certificates of repayment unpaid when it repealed § 814.25. Therefore, giving the statutory language its ordinary meaning, the court concluded that the counties' complaint failed to state a claim. The counties' entire claim against the State essentially rested on the argument that the legislature's action was unconstitutional. They maintained that it was a violation of due process of law for the legislature to retroactively extinguish their vested or valuable right by the repeal of the statute. However, a county did not have the legal right or status as against the State or another state agency to challenge the constitutionality of a statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

I. v. Columbia County Dep't of Health Servs.


No. 91-2726


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


170 Wis. 2d 344; 492 N.W.2d 188; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1275



July 30, 1992, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b) , STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Columbia county: FRANZ W. BRAND, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Columbia County (Wisconsin) that entered judgment in favor of respondent department of human services (DHS) and terminated the mother's parental rights pursuant to Wis. Stat. Ann. § 752.31(2)(e).


OVERVIEW: The mother appealed from an order that terminated her parental rights to her son pursuant to Wis. Stat. Ann. § 48.415(2). The mother contended that the statute was unconstitutionally vague or overbroad on its face because it allowed for the termination of parental rights when a parent was unable, due to poverty, to meet the court-ordered conditions for the return of the child to the home. The court found that the statute clearly gave fair notice that failure to comply with the court-ordered conditions for the return of the child could place the mother's parental rights to the son in danger. Furthermore, the mother failed to show how she was inhibited from exercising her fundamental rights to raise her child. The mother also argued that the trial court abused its discretion by allowing a social worker to testify about the quality of the interaction between the mother and the son during the visitations. The court stated the quality of the interaction at the visitations would help to establish the substantial likelihood that the mother would ever be able to meet the conditions established for the return of the son.


OUTCOME: The decision that terminated the mother's parental rights was affirmed.

State v. Jones


No. 91-1628-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


170 Wis. 2d 342; 492 N.W.2d 187; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1374



July 16, 1992, Released  
July 16, 1992, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Dane county: ROBERT R. PEKOWSKY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) of two counts of using threat of imminent force to take a hostage, a crime that violated Wis. Stat. § 940.305. Defendant was also convicted of two counts of recklessly using a weapon, crimes that violated Wis. Stat. § 941.20(1)(c), which was not the subject of the appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to convict on either hostage count, and that it was error to allow the State to use a tape recording as evidence. In affirming the conviction, the court found that there was sufficient evidence to prove all elements of the crime as to each hostage. When defendant entered the establishment, he stated that he wanted a certain individual. He announced two people were hostages. He ordered one hostage to get the individual he sought. It could have been reasonably inferred that defendant intended to hold his captives in order to influence the individual he sought to speak with or see him. That satisfied the intent element. The jury could have also concluded that defendant was demanding that the individual he sought appear and talk with him. Other conduct by defendant proved his guilt on the other hostage count. Further, Wis. Stat. § 940.305 was not unconstitutionally vague. The legislature intended § 940.305 to allow separate charges for each hostage taken in a single incident. Finally, the trial court properly allowed the state to use defendant's taped "bloodbath" remark because it was used solely to rebut defendant's testimony.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of two counts of using threat of imminent force to take a hostage.
