State v. Allen


No. 91-2308-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


170 Wis. 2d 343; 492 N.W.2d 188; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1295



July 14, 1992, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgments and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: MICHAEL J. SKWIERAWSKI, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of two convictions from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) that arose out of the same event; armed robbery, party to a crime, and first-degree intentional homicide while armed, party to a crime. He also appealed the order that denied his motion for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant received life imprisonment with parole eligibility at 35 years. Defendant argued that the jury should have been charged with the lesser-included offense of first-degree reckless homicide for the first-degree intentional homicide charge. In affirming the convictions, the court found that the undisputed facts did not warrant the submission of a reckless homicide instruction. The accomplice's discharge of the shotgun into the victim's chest at close range did not present reasonable grounds for acquittal of first-degree intentional homicide. The accomplice caused the victim's death with intent to kill him. It was not an abuse of discretion to deny defendant's motion to charge the lesser-included offense of first-degree reckless homicide in submitting the issue of the accomplice's homicide. Further, the trial court addressed the primary factors when the sentences were issued and reached a reasonable conclusion based on the facts. Defendant also argued the unconstitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 973.014 because it set forth no standards or guidelines for determination of the parole eligibility date. The court determined that defendant was accorded his due process rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences.

 

1371 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Kuechmann v. School Dist. of La Crosse


No. 92-1685


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


170 Wis. 2d 218; 487 N.W.2d 639; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 527


July 9, 1992, Oral argument  
July 10, 1992, Decided  
July 10, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for La Crosse county: Peter G. Pappas, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed and matter remanded with directions to dismiss the complaint; motion denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school board challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin), which upon appellee elector and school board member's complaint found Wis. Stat. § 9.10(4) unconstitutional and enjoined and prohibited the school board from conducting a recall election. The board argued that the circuit court lacked jurisdiction to hear the matter.


OVERVIEW: An elector and member of the school board was faced with a recall election. He filed a complaint challenging the recall election with the Election Board as required by Wis. Stat. § 5.06(1). But about two days before the board issued a ruling in favor of the school board, the elector filed an action for declaratory judgment and injunctive relief with the circuit court, or in the alternative for a writ of prohibition, on the grounds that the § 5.06(1) was unconstitutional. The circuit agreed and enjoined the recall election. The board appealed and the court held that the circuit court lacked jurisdiction to hear the matter. By Wis. Stat. § 5.06(1), the board was the exclusive avenue of review and had to issue a final ruling as to all issues before the circuit court could hear the matter under Wis. Stat. § 5.06(8). Even constitutional issues that the board did not have authority to rule on still had to be placed on the record before the board before it could be heard by the circuit court. Consequently, the decision of the circuit court was void.


OUTCOME: The court held that the circuit court was without jurisdiction to hear the elector's complaint against the school board and ordered the judgment of the circuit reversed. The case was remanded with instructions to dismiss the complaint.

State v. Slaback


No. 90-1684-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


170 Wis. 2d 342; 492 N.W.2d 187; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1377



July 2, 1992, Released  
July 2, 1992, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL from judgments of the circuit court for La Crosse county: JOHN J. PERLICH, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed five judgments of the Circuit Court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin) by which he was convicted of, inter alia, enticing a child under the age of 18 for immoral purposes under Wis. Stat. §§ 939.05, 944.12 and sexual intercourse with a person under the age of 16 in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.225(2)(e).


OVERVIEW: Defendant objected to the amended information on the basis that it violated the ban against multiplicity. The court invoked Wis. Stat. § 971.31(2), which provided that all objections to the sufficiency of the information had to be raised before trial, or, otherwise, they were waived. Finding that defendant had not objected to the sufficiency of the information by way of any pretrial motion or at trial, the court ruled that he had waived the alleged defect of the amended information. Regarding the trial court's in camera inspection of medical and psychological records of the victims and their mother by which the trial court found nothing material or helpful to the defense that had not been disclosed already, the court found no error and refused to hold that the trial court was required to permit defendant's expert to examine the records. Furthermore, the court held that Wis. Stat. §§ 971.23(5), 971.24(1) did not negate the privilege or privileges that covered the records sought. The court rejected defendant's other arguments, including one that evidence of a prior crime by him was improperly admitted under Wis. Stat. § 904.04(2) at his trial.


OUTCOME: Ruling against defendant, the court affirmed all of the trial court's judgments.

 

1373 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Schmalz


No. 91-2635-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


170 Wis. 2d 344; 492 N.W.2d 188; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 777



July 1, 1992, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Waukesha county: KATHRYN W. FOSTER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which convicted her of operating an automobile while intoxicated, and from an order of the same court denying her motion for a new trial. Defendant claimed that the trial court deprived her of (1) a statutory right to use an accident report to impeach a state's witness, and (2) her constitutional right to confront and cross-examine a witness against her.


OVERVIEW: Defendant identified herself to a police officer as the driver of a car that had struck a house. The officer noted that defendant's breath smelled of intoxicants and that she had an unsteady gait, slurred speech and glassy, bloodshot eyes. He arrested her for operating while intoxicated, and a blood test confirmed that her blood alcohol content exceeded the legal limit. The officer prepared several reports of the accident, including a narrative of the accident, and a uniform traffic accident report ("accident report") pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 346.70(4). The latter contained a small sketch of the accident scene. The court held that the trial court correctly refused to allow defendant to introduce the accident report for use to impeach the officer. Wis. Stat. § 346.73(2) prohibited use of such accident reports in any criminal trial arising out of the accident and took precedence over Wis. Stat. § 906.13(2) which generally allowed the use of prior inconsistent statements to impeach. As so applied, Wis. Stat. § 346.73(2) did not deprive defendant of her unconstitutional right of confrontation because it did not necessarily contradict the officer and was not critical to her defense.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

City News & Novelty, Inc. v. Waukesha


No. 91-2885


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


170 Wis. 2d 14; 487 N.W.2d 316; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 488


April 29, 1992, Submitted on briefs  
June 24, 1992, Decided  
June 24, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Waukesha county: Clair Voss, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff adult-oriented business appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which entered summary judgment in favor of defendant city in a case involving the constitutionality of Waukesha, Wis., Mun. Code § 8.195 (1988). The ordinance regulated adult-oriented establishments.


OVERVIEW: The ordinance required that booths used for viewing adult-oriented videos be open to public view. It was enacted to promote the welfare, health, and safety of the citizenry by curbing sexual activity in the booths that might lead to the transmission of sexual diseases. The business asserted that the ordinance violated its First Amendment rights and that it was preempted by the federal Videotape Privacy Protection Act. The court affirmed holding that (1) the language of the Act did not contain an unequivocal expression by Congress of its intent to preempt local regulation of the physical layout of adult-oriented establishment; (2) the ordinance, a health and safety enactment aimed at curtailing sexual activity in enclosed viewing booths, was not in conflict with the Acts purpose of prohibiting the disclosure of videotape rental or sales records; (3) patrons of the business did not have any constitutionally protected right to private and anonymous viewing of sexually explicit materials in a public accommodation setting; and (4) the ordinance satisfied the requirements for valid time, place, and manner restrictions on the First Amendment rights of the patrons of the business.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to the city.

State v. Williams


No. 91-2311-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


169 Wis. 2d 747; 488 N.W.2d 928; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1297



June 16, 1992, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: ROBERT W. LANDRY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him on a jury verdict of first-degree intentional homicide, party to a crime, Wis. Stat. § 490.01(1), Wis. Stat. § 939.05, and attempted armed robbery, party to a crime, § 939.05, Wis. Stat. § 943.32(1)(b), and Wis. Stat. § 939.32. Defendant was sentenced to life for the homicide, with parole eligibility in 25 years, and to 10 years for robbery.


OVERVIEW: Two sons of the victim connected the killer's raincoat to a raincoat found in a car in which defendant was a passenger. Further, two witnesses testified that defendant was a principal in the crime, and that he fired the shot that killed the victim. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to support the verdict. Further, the trial court's finding that defendant's Miranda rights were properly presented to him prior to his statement was not against the great weight and clear preponderance of the evidence. The court rejected defendant's argument that reversal was mandated by the trial court's response to the jury without counsels' presence. The court noted that defendant did not claim that the trial court's answer was incorrect. The trial court's error was subject to the harmless error rule, and there was no reasonable possibility that the error contributed to the conviction. The court held that defendant was afforded his due process sentencing rights. In the court's view, the trial court's setting of defendant's parole eligibility was a part of its sentencing function, and Wis. Stat. § 973.014 was not an unconstitutional delegation of legislative power to the judiciary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Vargas


No. 91-2040


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


169 Wis. 2d 747; 488 N.W.2d 928; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1294



June 9, 1992, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: RUDOLPH T. RANDA, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which denied his Wis. Stat. 974.06 post-conviction motion. A jury convicted defendant of one count of arson and four counts of endangering safety by conduct regardless of life, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 943.02(1)(a) and Wis. Stat. § 941.30 (1986). He was sentenced to consecutive prison sentences of 15 years for the arson and 5 years for each of the other counts.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that Wis. Stat. § 941.30 (1986) was unconstitutional, that the State failed to prove every element of § 941.30 (1990), that he received ineffective assistance of counsel, and that he was improperly sentenced. The court opined that the Supreme Court of Wisconsin had previously held that § 941.30 (1986), and particularly the phrase "evincing a depraved mind," was not unconstitutionally vague. Further, the 1990 amendment to § 941.30 had no effect on the State's burden or the validity of defendant's conviction. Thus, defense counsel was not deficient for not raising the constitutionality of § 941.30. Counsel was not deficient for failing to introduce a gas company's report because it did not exculpate defendant. Counsel was not deficient in failing to introduce the testimony of the building's owner because he testified on voir dire that he would plead the Fifth Amendment. The court opined that it was precluded from reviewing data in defendant's appendix because it was not part of the record. Finally, defendant's claim that the trial court abused its discretion in sentencing was not properly raised on a Wis. Stat. § 974.06 motion, and he did not raise a "new factor."


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Fetzner v. Fetzner

COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


169 Wis. 2d 466; 487 N.W.2d 660; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1394



May 14, 1992, Released  
May 14, 1992, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: RICHARD CALLAWAY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of an order of the Circuit court for Dane County (Wisconsin) setting his child support payments at $ 704 per month between October 1985 and July 1986.


OVERVIEW: During the time period in question, the father and his ex-wife, stipulated to shared custody of their two children. The father was to have the children overnight for six of every fourteen nights, or 156 nights per year. They would otherwise live with the mother, who assumed all clothing, school and recreational costs. The court affirmed and held that the trial court properly used Wis. Admin. Code § HSS 80.04(2) to establish the father's support obligation. The court held further that a child support award computed under Wis. Admin. Code ch. HSS 80 is presumed fair. The father could not meritoriously argue that the trial court abused its discretion by applying a presumptively fair method that the court expressly authorized on remand from the father's prior appeal. The trial court properly applied Wis. Admin. Code §. HSS 80.04(2) retroactively. The general rule that legislation is to be applied prospectively unless otherwise provided did not prevent the trial court from exercising its discretion to apply the formula contained in § HSS 80.04(2) to reach a fair result.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

State v. James


No. 91-0135-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


169 Wis. 2d 490; 485 N.W.2d 436; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 460


September 6, 1991, Submitted on briefs  
May 14, 1992, Decided  
May 14, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Dane county: Jack F. Aulik, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), for being a felon in possession of a firearm, and the trial court's denial of his motion for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted as a felon in possession of a firearm. His sentence was enhanced because he was a repeat offender. The trial court denied defendant's motion for post-conviction relief. Defendant appealed, and argued that the use of the prior conviction as a basis for the felon in possession charge and the enhancement was double jeopardy. The trial court affirmed the conviction. The court held that defendant did not waive the jeopardy issue by failing to raise it at trial. The court held that repeater status was not a separate crime for which defendant was found guilty, it was a status rather than an offense; therefore, the bar against double jeopardy did not apply.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction as a felon in possession of a firearm. The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's application for post-conviction relief.

 

1381 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Lampkins v. Wisconsin Health Care Liability Ins. Plan


No. 91-1521


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


169 Wis. 2d 466; 487 N.W.2d 660; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1410



May 12, 1992, Released  
May 12, 1992, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: RICHARD G. HARVEY, JR., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, administrator of deceased patient's estate, appealed the order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which dismissed his malpractice claim against defendants, hospital, physicians, and their insurers, as outside the three-year statute of limitations of Wis. Stat. § 893.55(1).


OVERVIEW: The patient was admitted to the hospital and died shortly thereafter. The administrator filed a request for mediation as required by Wis. Stat. § 655.44. Separate attorneys filed notices of retainer for each of defendants. The mediation was unsuccessful. Allegedly, the hospital's counsel requested continued negotiations and agreed to waive the statute of limitations if no settlement were reached. No agreement was reached and the administrator filed suit. Defendants filed a motion to dismiss. The circuit court awarded summary judgment to all defendants. The administrator appealed. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The circuit court erroneously concluded that because there was no writing as a matter of law under Wis. Stat. § 807.05 there was no agreement because § 807.05 only applied to agreements reached during an action or special proceeding. Because a factual dispute existed over whether or not the hospital had agreed to waive the limitations period, summary judgment for the hospital was inappropriate. However, because all of the other defendants had different counsel and were not parties to any such agreement, they were entitled to summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the circuit court, which awarded summary judgment to the physicians and the insurers. The court reversed the order that had awarded summary judgment to the hospital.

 

1382 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Mc Donald v. Hanaman


No. 91-3068-FT


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


168 Wis. 2d 778; 486 N.W.2d 38; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 443



April 30, 1992, RELEASED


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for La Crosse county: John J. Perlich, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landlord sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin), which entered an order vacating a small claims default judgment against appellee former tenant, in contradiction of the statutory six-month limitation on reopening such judgments found in Wis. Stat. § 752.31(2)(a).


OVERVIEW: The landlord filed a complaint alleging that the former tenant owed him $ 1,227 on an oral lease. The complaint was served at the former tenant's last known address. The landlord was granted a default judgment. Later the former tenant sought to have the case reopen past the statutory six-month limitation on reopening such judgments found in Wis. Stat. § 752.31(2)(a). The former tenant challenged the constitutionality of the statute. The lower court granted the motion to reopen ruling that it was not anyone's fault that the wrong address was used and that the court did not favor default judgments. The lower court ultimately dismissed the landlord's claim and the former tenant's counterclaim for rent paid. The court reversed holding that the six-month time limitation was not unreasonable because compliance was not impossible and, in view of the relatively low stakes and quick process of small claims proceedings, six months was a reasonable time to reopen a default judgment. The legislature had the right to resolve this conflict in policies and to impose conditions on an individual's right to recovery. The former tenant was not deprived of due process.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of the former tenant's motion to reopen the case and to vacate the default judgment in the small claims action.

Casteel v. Mc Caughtry


No. 91-0218


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


168 Wis. 2d 758; 484 N.W.2d 579; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 339


September 6, 1991, Submitted on briefs  
April 30, 1992, Decided  
April 30, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to review granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: Robert A. De Chambeau, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed in part; reversed in part and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and the laws of Wisconsin, plaintiff inmate appealed an order of the circuit court for Dane county (Wisconsin), which dismissed his complaint against defendants, the warden, the security director, and the jailers for failure to state a claim.


OVERVIEW: The inmate filed an action against the warden, the security director, and the jailers, alleging that his placement in temporary lockup violated 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and the laws of Wisconsin. The trial court dismissed the complaint for failure to state a claim, and the inmate appealed. The court affirmed the part of the order that dismissed the state law claims, but it reversed and remanded the part of the order that dismissed the § 1983 claim. The court concluded that the inmate's failures to exhaust his remedies and to give notice of claim barred his state law claim but not his § 1983 claim, because a plaintiff need not exhaust administrative remedies before bringing a § 1983 action in state court. His § 1983 claim stated a claim for violation of procedural due process. His failure to allege compliance with Wis. Stat. § 893.82(3), the notice of claim statute, barred his claim for damages under state law, and his failure to allege that he exhausted his remedy under the Inmate Complaint Review System barred his claim for declaratory relief and an injunction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed order insofar as it dismissed the state law claims, but it reversed and remanded the order insofar as it dismissed the § 1983 claim.

 

1384 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mizzles


No. 91-1964-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


168 Wis. 2d 359; 485 N.W.2d 839; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 327



March 26, 1992, RELEASED


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for La Crosse county: DENNIS G. MONTABON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin), which, after convicting her of misdemeanor theft as a repeater, imposed probation for two years with the conditions that defendant spend 90 days in and that she not cohabit with a named man or any other man without permission of her probation officer.


OVERVIEW: On appeal defendant argued that the probation order unconstitutionally infringed upon her right to privacy and freedom of association and was overbroad and unconstitutionally vague. The trial court had concluded that the order was reasonable and appropriate in view of defendant's history, notwithstanding that defendant had married the man with whom she was prohibited from cohabiting. The court held that the probation order was unrelated to defendant's offense of misdemeanor theft. There was no evidence in the record that any man was involved. The order placed no limit on the discretion of defendant's probation officer and did not set any standards for him to apply in determining whether he should allow defendant to cohabit with a particular man. That portion of the order placed an unconstitutional burden on defendant's freedom of association and right to privacy. However, the court held that the condition that prohibited defendant from cohabitating with a named man without her probation officer's consent was a valid condition on her probation. The named man had a criminal record and had abused defendant on several occasions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the portion of the probation order that prohibited defendant from cohabiting with any man without the permission of her probation officer and affirmed the portion of the order that prohibited her from cohabiting with a named man.

Gandhi v. State Medical Examining Bd.


No. 91-2044


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


168 Wis. 2d 299; 483 N.W.2d 295; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 243


February 26, 1992, Submitted on briefs  
March 25, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Racine county: Wayne J. Marik, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner physician appealed from a judgment of the Circuit court for Racine County (Wisconsin), which affirmed a decision of respondent Wisconsin Medical Examining Board, which revoked the physician's license to practice medicine.


OVERVIEW: The Wisconsin Department of Regulation and Licensing charged the physician with improperly touching the intimate parts of three female patients and with other related sexual activity that had no medical purpose. The physician's license was subsequently revoked. On appeal, the issue was whether the preponderance of the evidence standard, which was used by the Board in the disciplinary proceeding violated the physician's constitutional guarantees of due process and equal protection. In affirming the trial court's and the Board's judgment, the court held that the preponderance of the evidence standard was appropriate because although the loss of a license to practice medicine was a substantial loss, the state had a strong interest and an obligation to protect the health, safety, and welfare of its citizens. The court found that there were ample safeguards to ensure due process in the proceedings, which afforded a realistic opportunity to prepare and meet the challenges posed in the proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the revocation of the physician's license to practice medicine.

State v. Pittman


No. 91-1413-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


168 Wis. 2d 358; 485 N.W.2d 838; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 261



March 24, 1992, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)(5), STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: FRANK T. CRIVELLO, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) that convicted him of second-degree sexual assault, which crime was a violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.225(2)(d). Defendant also appealed from an order of the trial court that denied his motion made for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction of second-degree sexual assault. Defendant argued that Wis. Stat. § 940.225(2)(d), which made it a crime to have sexual contact or sexual intercourse with a person that one knew was unconscious, was void for vagueness if the definition of unconscious included a lack of awareness resulting from sleep. Part of this argument depended on the premise that there were no guidelines regarding what stage or level of sleep produced a sufficient lack of awareness to make it equivalent to being unconscious. The court rejected this on the basis that, inter alia, the jury had to decide whether or not the victim was at a level of sleep that produced a sufficient lack of awareness and had to decide whether defendant knew of that lack of awareness or not. Regarding evidentiary rulings of the trial court, the court rejected defendant's arguments, including one that posited that it was an error to exclude proffered expert testimony. The court ruled that the expert testimony was irrelevant because the proposed subject was general research information about sleep that did not inform as to a particular person's sleep patterns on a particular night.


OUTCOME: Ruling against defendant, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment and order.

 

1387 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


LeClair v. Natural Resources Bd.


No. 91-2316


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


168 Wis. 2d 227; 483 N.W.2d 278; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 246


January 8, 1992, Submitted on briefs  
March 19, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: P. Charles Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant commercial fishers sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which granted the summary judgment motion of respondents, Wisconsin Natural Resources Board and Wisconsin Department of Natural Resources (DNR), in an action seeking a declaration that the DNR's new rules involving fishing quotas were invalid and seeking a temporary restraining order prohibiting enforcement of the new rules.


OVERVIEW: The fishers were holders of Wis. Admin. Code ch. NR 25 trawling permits, which authorized them to take set amounts of specified fish in certain waters. The actual fish quotas were set forth in various administrative rules in ch. NR 25. After the Board adopted rules repealing, recreating, and amending ch. NR 25, including those setting the forage fish quotas, the fishers filed an action challenging the validity of the new rules and seeking a temporary restraining order. The trial court granted respondents' summary judgment motion. The court held that the fishers were not entitled to an adjudicatory hearing because their permits were not revoked or suspended. Rather, the permits were subject to the provisions of ch. NR 25. Although the fishers held the only trawling permits in Lake Michigan, the DNR's new rules were not impermissibly directed to a § 227.01(13) closed class because they applied to all commercial fisherman holding forage fish trawling permits. Further, the rule revision did not constitute a "taking" because the fishers' permits created no vested or permanent rights. Finally, the DNR's actions did not violate Wis. Stat. § 101.11 because it was not the fishers' employer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision that granted respondents' summary judgment motion in the action challenging the validity of the DNR's new rules.

State ex rel. Schultz v. Bablitch


No. 91-1946


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


168 Wis. 2d 359; 485 N.W.2d 839; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 328



March 10, 1992, RELEASED


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: P. CHARLES JONES, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which dismissed his 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 complaint for failure to state a claim against defendant corrections officials.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued that officials denied him due process by placing his daughter on the "visitation denied" list, thereby refusing him visitation. He also argued that a social worker in his daughter's "CHIPS" case illegally and unconstitutionally gave prison officials the confidential terms of the CHIPS order denying him visitation. As to the first argument, the instant court found that the juvenile court that denied the inmate visitation in the CHIPS proceedings had already furnished the inmate any process he was due; the order superseded the prison's general policies regarding visitation provided by the corrections department's administrative rules that the inmate maintained created and gave him constitutionally protected liberty interests in visitation. As to the second argument, the social worker had the power to share court orders pertaining to prison inmates with other persons working for the prison system. While exercising her power under a statute, the social worker was often required to make discriminating judgments. Here, she had a legitimate concern that the inmate's parents might attempt to bring his daughter to the prison, in violation of the CHIPS order.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

State v. Schober


No. 91-1145-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


167 Wis. 2d 371; 481 N.W.2d 689; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 111


January 24, 1992, Submitted on briefs  
February 26, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Waukesha county: Lee S. Dreyfus, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant and the State sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which denied a special prosecutor's motion to dismiss defendant's criminal prosecution.


OVERVIEW: A John Doe hearing was held, and defendant was bound over for trial on sexual assault charges, but the special prosecutor determined that new evidence concerning the victim's credibility hindered his ability to obtain a guilty verdict. The special prosecutor filed a motion to dismiss the case, but the trial court denied the motion. On appeal, defendant and the State claimed that the trial court abused its discretion. The court agreed holding that the trial court erroneously determined that the John Doe hearing had the same effect as an order from another circuit court, precluding it from dismissing the case. The court further held that the trial court erroneously concluded that the special prosecutor did not have the same power that an elected district attorney had in deciding whether or not the public interest required the dismissal of the criminal charges. The court also held that the trial court abused its discretion by deciding that the case needed to proceed so long as there was admissible evidence. Finally, the court determined that it was in the public's interest to dismiss the case on its merits.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order, which denied the special prosecutor's motion to dismiss, and the court ordered the dismissal of the charges against defendant.

State v. Schmidt


No. 91-2664-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


167 Wis. 2d 490; 482 N.W.2d 671; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 204



February 18, 1992, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)4, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: DAVID HANSHER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an interlocutory appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), defendant sought review of the trial court's denial of a motion to dismiss on double-jeopardy grounds a second-offense drunk driving case against him.


OVERVIEW: In March 1989, defendant was charged with driving a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant, and driving a motor vehicle while having a blood-alcohol concentration of 0.1 percent or more. The trial was originally set for January 1990, but was adjourned six times until May 1991. At that time, the State requested an adjournment because its witness, a police officer, was on vacation. The trial court denied the request. Only one charge was before the trial court because the other had been dismissed. The trial court ordered the State to proceed, but the State had no witnesses to present. The trial court granted defendant's motion to dismiss based on no evidence. The charges were reissued against defendant and he moved to dismiss on grounds that further prosecution was barred by the double-jeopardy provisions of the federal and state constitutions. Because the earlier proceeding had been a bench trial and no witnesses had been sworn, double jeopardy had not attached under Wis. Stat. § 972.07. The trial court's attempt to effectuate a dismissal with prejudice before the attachment of jeopardy was ineffective and did not bar reissuance of the charges against defendant.


OUTCOME: The trial court order was affirmed.

Novak v. Ceci


No. 90-2709


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


167 Wis. 2d 486; 482 N.W.2d 669; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 145

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: MARK J. FARNUM, Judge.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action by pro se plaintiffs against defendants, the circuit court judge, the Wisconsin Supreme Court justices, and the Executive Director of the Wisconsin Equal Justice Task Force (Task Force), seeking a mandamus to compel the Task Force to comply with the Wisconsin Open Records Law, Wis. Stat. §§ 19.31-.39, plaintiffs sought review from a judgment of the Circuit Court, Dane County (Wisconsin), which granted defendants' motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: After the Wisconsin Equal Justice Task Force (Task Force) failed to provide plaintiffs with all of the records they requested, plaintiffs sued the circuit court judge, the Wisconsin Supreme Court justices, and the Director, seeking an mandamus to order the Director to comply with the Wisconsin Open Records Law. Wis. Stat. §§ 19.31-.39. The trial court granted defendants' motion to dismiss, and denied plaintiffs' request to amend their petition. Stat. § 802.09(1) gave plaintiffs the right to amend their petition once as a matter of course.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment dismissing plaintiffs' action for failure to state a claim, but reversed the trial court's denial of plaintiffs' request to amend their petition, and remanded for further proceedings.

Phillips v. Wisconsin Personnel Comm'n


No. 90-2929


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


167 Wis. 2d 205; 482 N.W.2d 121; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 104; 67 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 639


November 6, 1991, Submitted on briefs  
February 13, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: Angela B. Bartell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, which affirmed an order of appellee Wisconsin Personnel Commission dismissing her employment discrimination complaint against her employer for failure to state a claim upon which relief could be granted in her action alleging discrimination on grounds of marital status, sexual orientation, and gender.


OVERVIEW: The partner of an employee who was a lesbian was denied health care coverage by the employee's employer. The Wisconsin Personnel Commission dismissed her employment discrimination suit for failure to state a claim upon which relief could be granted, and the circuit court affirmed. She appealed the circuit court's decision and the court affirmed. The court held that the commission, as the agency charged by the legislature with administration of the Fair Employment Act (Act), could have reasonably interpreted the applicable statute and rule as legitimately limiting dependent health insurance coverage to employees' spouses and children without violating the marital status discrimination provisions of the Act. The court held that the rule applied equally to hetero- and homosexual employees and thus did not discriminate against the latter group. The court held that the rule did not treat one gender differently than the other; it applied equally to males and females.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order upholding the dismissal of the employee's complaint.

 

1393 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Metropolitan Holding Co. v. Board of Review


No. 90-2748


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


167 Wis. 2d 134; 482 N.W.2d 654; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 102


July 2, 1991, Submitted on briefs  
February 4, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: Charles L. Larson, Reserve Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant partnership challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which denied a certiorari review affirming the City of Milwaukee Board of Review's affirmance of the city tax assessor's valuation of the partnership's property for city real property tax assessment purposes.


OVERVIEW: The parties disagreed as to the correct method of tax assessment for a federally subsidized low-income housing project. The partnership asserted that a capitalization of income method based upon actual income and expenses was correct while the Board supported use of a capitalization of income based upon estimated market rents. Specifically, the partnership challenged the use of market rents as opposed to contract rents in the calculation of assessed value using the income capitalization approach. In affirming the Board's decision, the court rejected the partnership's argument that the Board's assessment was arbitrary because it was based on the directions found in the Assessment Manual created by the Department of Revenue. The Board's affirmation of the assessor's use of market rents to establish the full value for tax purposes of this subsidized housing project was made on the "best information available" and thus the constitutional requirement of uniformity was met. Assessors in Wisconsin had to employ the procedures of evaluation described in the Assessment Manual, and there was no conflict between the assessment methods described in the Manual and Wis. Stat. § 70.32(1).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's upholding of the Board's assessment of the property by denying certiorari.

 

1394 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brinkman


No. 91-1131-CR & 91-1668-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


166 Wis. 2d 1052; 481 N.W.2d 708; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 53



January 22, 1992, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)(5), STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and order of the circuit court for Outagamie county: DENNIS C. LUEBKE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment and order of the Circuit Court for Outagamie County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of criminal damage to property under Wis. Stat. § 943.01(1).


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendant guilty of criminal damage to 12 police cars under Wis. Stat. § 943.01(1). On appeal, the conviction was affirmed. The court held that defendant failed to show that his trial counsel was guilty of deficient performance by waiting until the day of trial to orally move for disclosure of the identity of a confidential informant. The informant's identity was privileged from discovery under Wis. Stat. § 905.10(1). The court ruled that evidence of defendant's "other bad acts" were properly admitted under Wis. Stat. § 904.04(2). The evidence was admitted to show plan, knowledge, and motive. The court determined that defendant did not show a need for the disclosure, and the trial court's reliance on cross-examination was a reasonable, discretionary decision to preserve defendant's rights. Finally, the court ruled that defendant did not indicate how the testimony of adverse witnesses failed to prove guilty beyond a reasonable doubt or what elements of the crime lacked proof. Nor did he show he was unable to confront the witnesses. Thus, defendant's claims of insufficient evidence and that his right to confront adverse witnesses was violated were rejected.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for criminal damage to property.

 

1395 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


J.W. v. State


Nos. 91-2242, 91-2243


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


166 Wis. 2d 1054; 481 N.W.2d 709; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 91



January 15, 1992, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)(4), STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from orders of the circuit court for Manitowoc county: ALLAN J. DEEHR, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant delinquent minor sought review of the determination by the Circuit Court for Manitowoc County (Wisconsin) that the minor should be placed in a secure juvenile detention facility for 26 days for violating an order to attend school. The trial court found that the minor had missed 26 days of school and determined that each day was a separate violation of its previous disposition order and thus, 26 days of detention was appropriate.


OVERVIEW: The minor was adjudicated delinquent. The minor was placed on supervision and was specifically told by the trial court that he must attend school each and every day. The state filed a motion for sanctions after the minor missed a number of days of school. The trial court found that the minor had missed 26 days of school and sent him to a detention facility for 26 days. The court affirmed the trial court's orders. The court held that the minor was adjudged delinquent under Wis. Stat. § 48.12 and was not adjudged a child alleged to be in need of protection and services (CHIPS) under Wis. Stat. § 48.13(6). Thus, the CHIPS' statutes regarding the proper determination of the reasons for the minor's absences from school did not apply to the trial court's hearing on the alleged violations by the minor. Indeed, due to the clear language in the two statutes and the legislative distinction between CHIPS and delinquents, it would inappropriate for the court to extend Wis. Stat. § 118.16(5)'s hearing requirements to situations other than CHIPS. The court also held that the notice to the minor of all the alleged violations in one notice was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's rulings that the minor should be detained at a juvenile facility for 26 days for violating a delinquency court order.

 

1396 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Cornell Univ. v. Rusk County


No. 91-0581


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


166 Wis. 2d 811; 481 N.W.2d 485; 1992 Wisc. App. LEXIS 6; 118 Oil & Gas Rep. 397


December 4, 1991, Submitted on briefs  
January 14, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Rusk county: F.A. Henderson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county challenged the decision of the Circuit Court for Rusk County (Wisconsin) that granted a declaratory judgment in favor of respondent taxpayer. The circuit court held that, under Wis. Stat. § 70.32, the mineral interests were taxed separately from surface interests in land, and that a tax deed did not extinguish the taxpayer's interest in the mineral rights.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer owned mineral rights in land; the surface interest in the land was owned by a third party. After the third party failed to pay real estate taxes for five years, the county obtained a deed to the property. The third party paid taxes for one of the years and redeemed the deed, however, the remaining overdue taxes subjected the property to the possibility of seizure by the county in the future. The taxpayer initiated the action for injunctive and declaratory relief and the circuit court granted the declaratory judgment in its favor. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment, holding that § 70.32, which established a unitary tax scheme, classified mineral interests in such a manner that they were subject to separate taxation from the land. The court found that Wis. Stat. § 706.057(2)(d) protected mineral interest owners who agreed to pay taxes under a contract with the surface interest owner and did not conflict with § 70.32. The court then concluded that the tax deed held by the county extinguished the taxpayer's right to the mineral interests and that the statutory scheme did not constitute a violation of procedural or substantive due process.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

 

1397 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Richland Sch. Dist. v. Department of Indus., Labor & Human Relations, etc.


No. 90-1750


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


166 Wis. 2d 262; 479 N.W.2d 579; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1599; 14 Employee Benefits Cas. (BNA) 2661


May 16, 1991, Oral argument  
December 19, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Richland county: William L. Reinecke, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed; order denying attorney's fees reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school district sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Richland County (Wisconsin), which entered judgment affirming an order by respondent Department of Industry, Labor, and Human Relations in favor of respondent employee after the district refused to substitute accumulated reimbursable leave for unpaid leave under the state Family and Medical Leave Act (FMLA). The employee sought review of the denial of attorney's fees.


OVERVIEW: Upon learning that his family was to receive an adopted son, the employee requested a five-day leave under the FMLA, and was denied a request to substitute five days of accumulated paid sick leave for the unpaid leave provided for in the FMLA. The employee took the leave but complained to the Department, which then ordered the district to reimburse the employee for the five days. Prior to the trial court's entry of judgment in his favor, the employee also sought attorney's fees for the costs of the trial, which the trial court denied. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment as to the Department's order but reversed the trial court's order denying attorney's fees in the trial court. The court first rejected the district's arguments that substitution of paid leave for unpaid leave was improper as against administrative rules or public policy and found that Wis. Stat. § 103.10(5) unambiguously permitted such substitution and did not conflict with either administrative rules or a collective bargaining agreement. The court next determined that the employee's request for attorney's fees was timely and that such award was consistent with the fee-shifting provisions of the FMLA.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment upholding the Department's order that the district reimburse the employee for five-day leave and that awarded attorney's fees and costs. The court reversed the trial court's order denying attorney's fees in the trial court and remanded the cause with directions to determine attorney fees on appeal as well as on review in the trial court.

 

1398 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Datka v. Datka


No. 91-0405


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


166 Wis. 2d 1; 480 N.W.2d 568; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1540



December 11, 1991, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Walworth county: ROBERT J. KENNEDY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband challenged that portion of a judgment of divorce rendered in the Circuit Court for Walworth County (Wisconsin), which required him to pay monthly support for the parties' minor child. Respondent wife sought to have the husband's appeal declared frivolous.


OVERVIEW: The husband was ordered to pay monthly child support for the parties' daughter in their divorce judgment. The husband appealed, contending that a deviation from the percentage standard was appropriate because of substantial periods of physical placement to both parties, the relative circumstances of each party, and his long work weeks. The court affirmed, holding that the husband did not meet his burden of proving that application of the standard was unfair because they were presumptively used pursuant to statute, he was given credit for his custodial periods, and the trial court conducted the proper balancing of the child's needs and the advantages the child would have received from the husband's extra work if the marriage had continued. The court also found no abuse of discretion in the trial court balancing the length of the husband's work week against the needs of the child to arrive at his support obligation. The wife's motion to declare the appeal frivolous was denied, even though the husband's claim that the percentage standards were unconstitutional was without merit, because the appeal was not brought to harass and was not frivolous.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of divorce but denied the wife's motion to declare the husband's appeal frivolous.

 

1399 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Bracegirdle v. La Crosse County


No. 90-2803


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


166 Wis. 2d 1; 480 N.W.2d 568; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1528



December 5, 1991, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1]  UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for La Crosse county: MICHAEL J. ROSBOROUGH, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant nurse challenged the decision of the Circuit Court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin), which granted defendant supervisor and defendant county's motion for summary judgment in the nurse's intentional misrepresentation and tortious interference with contractual relations action and her 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action.


OVERVIEW: This controversy arose over charges that the nurse engaged in misconduct, contrary to Wis. Adm. Code § 7.04(4), by using excessive force in removing a patient's dentures. The supervisor notified the State's Board of Nursing of the incident, pursuant to Wis. Adm. Code §§ 132.31(6)(c) 50.09(6)(b), which required him to report allegations of nursing misconduct. Meanwhile, the nurse resigned her position with the county and took a position with another employer. Thereafter, the Board concluded that the nurse's attempts, by verbal and physical encouragement to persuade a patient to open his mouth after he declined to do so, constituted a violation of Wis. Adm. Code §7.04(4). This complaint resulted in the Board's reprimand of the nurse's new employer. Furthermore, the nurse was reassigned to a new position. On appeal, the court held that summary judgment was proper because the supervisor and the county were immune from suit on the nurse's misrepresentation and intentional interference clam. Furthermore, the court held that the nurse's § 1983 claim failed because the nurse was not deprived of due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

 

1400 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Schwochert v. American Family Mut. Ins. Co.


No. 90-2737


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


166 Wis. 2d 97; 479 N.W.2d 190; 1991 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1594


June 6, 1991, Submitted on briefs  
December 5, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Columbia county: Lewis W. Charles, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff accident victims appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Columbia County (Wisconsin), which denied their motion under Wis. Stat. § 806.07 for relief from the judgment entered pursuant to the mandate of the Wisconsin Supreme Court previously as to their case. The accident victims contended that their initial decision had been overruled, thus they were entitled to the relief.


OVERVIEW: The accident victims filed a motion for relief of judgment from the mandate in their initial case contending that their initial decision had been overruled and that they were entitled to the relief on the basis of new precedent. The initial case was a wrongful death action arising out of an automobile accident. The court held that the accident victims' underinsured motorist coverage did not apply to the vehicle involved in the accident where the endorsement for underinsured motorist coverage was written on another owned vehicle and excluded coverage for damages incurred while in other vehicles of the same household. In the new precedent case, the carrier's reducing clause was enforceable against the insured and issued relief from the initial mandate after decision of another case that was considered on the same point The court found that the issues in the later-decided cases were not the same as the issues in the case from which the accident victims sought relief. The trial court order denying the accident victims relief was affirmed as not an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court order denying the accident victims relief.
